6 min
Prayer of the Sick: When Standing Is Impossible or Difficult
Explanation of rulings on standing and gestures for the sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a sick person who cannot stand or fears severe harm may pray sitting, and distinguish between cases of partial ability and complete inability.

Core Idea
A sick person prays according to ability; severe pain equals inability.

The obligation to pray remains even during illness, but the mode adapts to one's capacity. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the key distinctions: real impossibility (cannot stand at all) and legal difficulty (severe pain or fear of harm). It also covers partial ability and the use of gestures for bowing and prostration. The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and the Quranic principle 'La yukallifu nafsan illa wus'aha' are the foundational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between real impossibility (cannot stand at all) and legal difficulty (severe pain, fear of increased illness or prolongation).
The Hanafi school treats both as equivalent for the ruling.
2
Trace the textual proof
Examine the hadith: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Note the gradation and the Quranic verse on capacity.
The imperative shows obligation; the concessions show permissibility based on ability.
3
Apply the ruling to partial ability
If the person can stand partially, they must stand for as much as possible (even just the takbir and one verse). If severe pain occurs, they may sit from the beginning.
This is the correct madhhab according to al-Tahtawi.
4
Analyze the gesture rules
When bowing and prostration are impossible, the person sits and gestures with the head, making the gesture for sujud lower than for ruku'. Gesturing while standing is also permitted.
If the forehead has sores, prostration on the nose is required before resorting to gestures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض من إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله والمرض حالة للبدن خارجة عن المجرى الطبيعي (إذا تعذر على المريض كل القيام وهو الحقيقي ومثله الحكمي ذكره فقال (أو تعسر) كل القيام (بوجود ألم شديد أو خاف بأن غلب في ظنه بتجربة سابقة أو اخبار طبيب مسلم حاذق، أو ظهور الحال (زيادة المرض أو خاف (بطاه) أي طول المرض (به) أي بالقيام (صلى قاعداً بركوع وسجود) لما روي عن عمران بن حصين قال : كانت بواسير فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلاة فقال : صل قائماً فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنب زاد النسائي عن بي فإن لم تستطع فمستلقياً لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها ( ويقعد كيف شاء) أي كيف تيسر له بغير ضرر من تربع أو غيره في الأصح من غير كراهة كذا روي عن الإمام للعذر (وإلا) بأن قدر على بعض القيام قام بقدر ما يمكنه بلا زيادة مشقة، ولو بالتحريمة، وقراءة آية وإن حصل به ألم شديد يقعد ابتداء كما لو عجز وقعد ابتداء هو المذهب الصحيح لأن بحسب الطاقة (وإن تعذر الركوع والسجود وقدر على القعود ولو مستنداً (صلى قاعداً بالإيماء) للركوع والسجود برأسه ولا يجزيه مضطجعاً (وجعل إيماءه) برأسه للسجود أخفض من إيمائه للركوع كذا في السراج، لو كان بجبهته قروح لا يستطيع السجود عليها يلزمه السجود على الأنف، ولا يجوز له الإيماء لأنه ترك القدرة عليه، وفي النهر ما يفيد أنه عند العجز عن السجود يفترض عليه أن يقوم للقراءة فإذا جاء أوان الركوع والسجود يقعد ويوميء بهما . قوله : (صلى قاعداً بالإيماء) أو والأول أفضل لأنه أشبه بالسجود لكونه أقرب إلى الأرض وهو المقصود التبيين وفي البحر ظاهر المذهب جواز الإيماء قائماً أو قاعداً كما لا يخفي اهـ قال الحلبي : لو السجود به . كذا في
Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick. Derived from attributing an action to its doer. Sickness is a condition of the body outside the natural course. If complete standing is impossible for the sick person – and that is the real impossibility, and similarly the legal impossibility is mentioned – he said: or complete standing becomes difficult due to the presence of severe pain, or he fears (based on a prior experience or the report of a competent, upright Muslim doctor, or the appearance of the condition) the increase of illness, or he fears its prolongation, he prays sitting with bowing and prostration. Based on what is narrated from Imran ibn Husayn: 'I had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Al-Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' (2:286) He sits however he wishes – i.e., as is easy for him without harm – such as cross-legged or otherwise, according to the most correct view without dislike, as is narrated from the Imam due to the excuse. Otherwise – if he is able to perform part of the standing – he stands as much as he can without extra hardship, even if only for the takbir and recitation of one verse. If severe pain occurs, he sits from the beginning, just as if he were incapacitated; sitting from the beginning is the correct madhhab because it is within his capacity. If bowing and prostration are impossible while he is able to sit, even leaning, he prays sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration with his head, and it is not sufficient for him to lie on his side. He makes his gesture for prostration lower than his gesture for bowing. It is stated in al-Siraj: If he has sores on his forehead and cannot prostrate on them, he must prostrate on his nose, and it is not permissible for him to gesture because he is abandoning what he is capable of. In al-Nahr it indicates that when unable to prostrate, it is obligatory on him to stand for recitation, and when it is time for bowing and prostration, he sits and gestures for both. His statement: 'prays sitting with gesture' – the first is better because it is more similar to prostration as it is closer to the ground, which is the goal. In al-Bahr: The apparent madhhab permits gesturing while standing or sitting, as is not hidden. End. Al-Halabi said: '... in'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the chapter of the prayer of the sick. It begins by defining the attribution of actions and the nature of illness. The main ruling: if a sick person is unable to stand (real impossibility) or it becomes difficult due to severe pain or fear of increased or prolonged illness (legal impossibility), he prays sitting with normal ruku' and sujud. The proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and the Quranic verse. The commentator then explains that if the person can only partially stand, he stands as much as he can, even for the opening takbir and one verse. If severe pain occurs, he sits from the start. If unable to bow and prostrate, he sits and gestures with his head, making the gesture for sujud lower than for ruku'. The passage also notes that if one can prostrate on the nose when the forehead is injured, he must do so; gesturing is not allowed if there is a capability. It discusses nuances about standing for recitation when unable to prostrate, and the preferred method of gesturing. The Hanafi position is that the sick person should pray according to his ability, and the hadith provides a gradation: standing > sitting > on side > lying down. The commentator refines the understanding by clarifying that severe pain is treated like inability, and that gesturing while sitting is valid. The authority weight is based on Zahir al-Riwayah (hadith) and later ijtihad.

Key Terms
التعذر الحقيقي (al-ta'adhdhur al-haqiqi): Real impossibility: the sick person is physically unable to stand at all.
التعسر (al-ta'assur): Legal difficulty: the sick person can stand but with severe pain or fear of harm, treated like impossibility.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head for ruku' and sujud when unable to perform them physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick person can stand but only for a few seconds. They experience no pain but cannot maintain standing for the entire prayer. According to the Hanafi school, how should they pray?
A) They must stand for as long as they can, then sit for the remainder.
B) They may pray sitting from the beginning because they cannot stand the whole time.
C) They must pray lying down.
D) They should delay the prayer until they can stand fully.

Key Takeaway
A sick person prays according to their ability; severe pain or fear of harm is treated as legal impossibility, allowing sitting and gestures.

8 min
Sitting in Prayer When Unable to Stand
Ruling on sitting when standing is harmful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that permit sitting in prayer and explain the ruling on partial standing.

Core Idea
Standing is fard, but sitting substitutes when standing harms or is impossible.

The Hanafi school derives the permission to pray sitting from the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn. This lesson examines the conditions that trigger this permission and the extent of standing required when partial ability remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on sitting
Note the ruling: if standing would increase illness or delay recovery, one prays sitting with bowing and prostration. This is a rukhsa (concession).
The ruling is based on the principle of 'la haraj' (no hardship).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith from 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting...' (Bukhari, Muslim, Nasa'i). This is a marfu' hadith with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'salli' indicates obligation. The conditional structure (in lam tastati'...) shows that each subsequent posture is a substitute for the prior, only permitted when the prior is impossible.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Apply to partial standing
The text clarifies that if one can stand partially, they must stand as much as possible, even for just the opening takbir and one verse. Severe pain permits sitting from the start.
This is the correct madhhab according to al-Tahtawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظهور الحال (زيادة المرض أو خاف (بطاه) أي طول المرض (به) أي بالقيام (صلى قاعداً بركوع وسجود) لما روي عن عمران بن حصين قال : كانت بواسير فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلاة فقال : صل قائماً فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنب زاد النسائي فإن لم تستطع فمستلقياً لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها ( ويقعد كيف شاء) أي كيف تيسر له بغير ضرر من تربع أو غيره في الأصح من غير كراهة كذا روي عن الإمام للعذر (وإلا) بأن قدر على بعض القيام قام بقدر ما يمكنه بلا زيادة مشقة، ولو بالتحريمة، وقراءة آية وإن حصل به ألم شديد يقعد ابتداء كما لو عجز وقعد ابتداء هو المذهب الصحيح لأن بحسب الطاقة (وإن تعذر الركوع والسجود وقدر على القعود ولو مستنداً (صلى قاعداً بالإيماء) للركوع والسجود برأسه ولا يجزيه مضطجعاً (وجعل إيماءه) برأسه للسجود أخفض من إيمانه) برأسه (للركوع) وكذا لو عجز عن السجود، وقدر على الركوع يومىء بهما لأن النبي عاد مريضاً فرآه يصلي على وسادة فأخذها فرمي بها فأخذ عوداً ليصلي علیه فرمي به وقال صل على الأرض إن استطعت وإلا فأوم إيماء واجعل سجودك أخفض من ركوعك فإن لم يخفضه) أي الإيماء للسجود (عنه) أي عن الإيماء للركوع بأن جعلهما على حد سواء ( لا تصح صلاته لفقد السجود حقيقة، وحكماً مع القدرة (ولا يرفع بالبناء للمجهول الوجهه شيء) كحجر وخشبة ( يسجد عليه لما قدمناه، ولقوله : (من استطاع منكم أن يسجد فليسجد ومن لم يستطع فلا يرفع إلى وجهه شيئاً يسجد عليه، وليكن في ركوعه وسجوده يومي برأسه) رواه الطبراني
If his condition appears (increase of illness or he fears (his illness) i.e., length of illness) (by standing) he prays sitting with bowing and prostration. For it is narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'I had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Al-Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' (And he sits however he wishes) i.e., however is easy for him without harm, such as cross-legged or otherwise, in the most correct view without dislike, as narrated from the Imam due to the excuse. (Otherwise) i.e., if he is able to perform some of the standing, he stands as much as he can without additional hardship, even if just for the opening takbir and reciting one verse. And if severe pain occurs, he sits from the beginning, just as if he were incapable and sits from the beginning—this is the correct madhhab because (it is) according to capacity. (And if bowing and prostration are not possible, and he is able to sit, even leaning) he prays sitting with gestures (for bowing and prostration) with his head, and lying on his side does not suffice him. (And he makes his gesture) with his head for prostration lower than his gesture with his head for bowing. Likewise, if he is unable to prostrate but able to bow, he gestures with both. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) visited a sick person and saw him praying on a cushion; he took it and threw it away. He took a stick to prostrate on, and he threw it away and said: 'Prostrate on the ground if you can; otherwise gesture, and make your prostration lower than your bowing.' If he does not make it lower, i.e., the gesture for prostration, than the gesture for bowing, making them equal, his prayer is not valid due to the loss of prostration actually and legally while being able. (And he should not raise) (passive voice) to his face anything, like a stone or piece of wood, to prostrate on, due to what we presented, and due to his saying: 'Whoever among you can prostrate, let him prostrate; whoever cannot, let him not raise anything to his face to prostrate on, and let him gesture with his head in his bowing and prostration.' Reported by al-Tabarani.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the rulings for a sick person who cannot stand or prostrate in prayer. It begins by stating that if standing would increase illness or delay recovery, one prays sitting with normal bowing and prostration, citing the famous hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn. The sitting posture is whatever is comfortable without harm, with no dislike in the relied-upon view. If one can partially stand, they must stand as much as possible, even for the opening takbir and one verse; severe pain permitting sitting from the start is analogous to total incapacity. When bowing and prostration are impossible but sitting is possible, one prays sitting with head gestures (ima'), with the gesture for prostration lower than for bowing. The hadith about the sick man and the cushion proves that raising an object to the forehead is prohibited; instead, one must gesture. If the gestures are equal, the prayer is invalid because prostration is effectively missed while capability exists. The text also mentions the narration from al-Tabarani reinforcing this. The commentary notes intra-madhhab differences, such as whether minimal inclination suffices for ima', with the relied-upon view being that a mere movement of the head without lowering is insufficient. Overall, the ruling emphasizes performing as much as one is able, prioritizing sitting over lying, and avoiding objects for prostration.

Key Terms
قاعداً (qa'idan): In the context of prayer for the sick: sitting, with the ability to bow and prostrate normally if possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do if they can only stand for part of the prayer?
A) Pray entirely sitting.
B) Stand as much as possible, even if just for the opening takbir.
C) Lie on their side.
D) Delay the prayer until they can stand fully.

Key Takeaway
Sitting in prayer is a concession granted only when standing is genuinely harmful or impossible; partial standing must be fulfilled to the extent possible.

Gesturing (Ima') and Prohibition of Raising Objects
Ruling on ima' and prohibition of raising objects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rules of gesturing (ima') for the sick and state the Hanafi position on raising objects for prostration.

Core Idea
When unable to prostrate, gesture with the head; raising an object to the forehead is prohibited and invalidates the prayer.

When a sick person cannot prostrate on the ground, the Hanafi school permits gesturing with the head. However, they strictly forbid raising an object (like a cushion) to the forehead, based on explicit hadith. This lesson examines the evidence and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on gesture
If one can sit but cannot bow or prostrate, they pray sitting and gesture with the head. The gesture for prostration must be lower than for bowing.
This applies even if leaning on something.
2
Understand the prohibition
It is forbidden (makruh tahriman) to raise an object to the forehead to prostrate upon. The hadith of the sick man with a cushion is cited.
The hadith is explicit: 'Whoever cannot prostrate, let him not raise anything to his face.'
3
Trace the dalil for both
The hadith of the Prophet visiting a sick man (Tabarani) and the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn provide evidence. The prohibition is based on direct command.
The opponent's qiyas is rejected because the explicit text takes precedence.
4
Apply the konsequence
If gestures are equal (not lower for prostration), or if one raises an object and touches it, the prayer is invalid.
Because prostration is effectively missed while capability exists (had the gesture been correct, it would suffice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظهور الحال (زيادة المرض أو خاف (بطاه) أي طول المرض (به) أي بالقيام (صلى قاعداً بركوع وسجود) لما روي عن عمران بن حصين قال : كانت بواسير فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلاة فقال : صل قائماً فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنب زاد النسائي فإن لم تستطع فمستلقياً لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها ( ويقعد كيف شاء) أي كيف تيسر له بغير ضرر من تربع أو غيره في الأصح من غير كراهة كذا روي عن الإمام للعذر (وإلا) بأن قدر على بعض القيام قام بقدر ما يمكنه بلا زيادة مشقة، ولو بالتحريمة، وقراءة آية وإن حصل به ألم شديد يقعد ابتداء كما لو عجز وقعد ابتداء هو المذهب الصحيح لأن بحسب الطاقة (وإن تعذر الركوع والسجود وقدر على القعود ولو مستنداً (صلى قاعداً بالإيماء) للركوع والسجود برأسه ولا يجزيه مضطجعاً (وجعل إيماءه) برأسه للسجود أخفض من إيمانه) برأسه (للركوع) وكذا لو عجز عن السجود، وقدر على الركوع يومىء بهما لأن النبي عاد مريضاً فرآه يصلي على وسادة فأخذها فرمي بها فأخذ عوداً ليصلي علیه فرمي به وقال صل على الأرض إن استطعت وإلا فأوم إيماء واجعل سجودك أخفض من ركوعك فإن لم يخفضه) أي الإيماء للسجود (عنه) أي عن الإيماء للركوع بأن جعلهما على حد سواء ( لا تصح صلاته لفقد السجود حقيقة، وحكماً مع القدرة (ولا يرفع بالبناء للمجهول الوجهه شيء) كحجر وخشبة ( يسجد عليه لما قدمناه، ولقوله : (من استطاع منكم أن يسجد فليسجد ومن لم يستطع فلا يرفع إلى وجهه شيئاً يسجد عليه، وليكن في ركوعه وسجوده يومي برأسه) رواه الطبراني
If his condition appears (increase of illness or he fears (his illness) i.e., length of illness) (by standing) he prays sitting with bowing and prostration. For it is narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'I had hemorrhoids and asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Al-Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' (And he sits however he wishes) i.e., however is easy for him without harm, such as cross-legged or otherwise, in the most correct view without dislike, as narrated from the Imam due to the excuse. (Otherwise) i.e., if he is able to perform some of the standing, he stands as much as he can without additional hardship, even if just for the opening takbir and reciting one verse. And if severe pain occurs, he sits from the beginning, just as if he were incapable and sits from the beginning—this is the correct madhhab because (it is) according to capacity. (And if bowing and prostration are not possible, and he is able to sit, even leaning) he prays sitting with gestures (for bowing and prostration) with his head, and lying on his side does not suffice him. (And he makes his gesture) with his head for prostration lower than his gesture with his head for bowing. Likewise, if he is unable to prostrate but able to bow, he gestures with both. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) visited a sick person and saw him praying on a cushion; he took it and threw it away. He took a stick to prostrate on, and he threw it away and said: 'Prostrate on the ground if you can; otherwise gesture, and make your prostration lower than your bowing.' If he does not make it lower, i.e., the gesture for prostration, than the gesture for bowing, making them equal, his prayer is not valid due to the loss of prostration actually and legally while being able. (And he should not raise) (passive voice) to his face anything, like a stone or piece of wood, to prostrate on, due to what we presented, and due to his saying: 'Whoever among you can prostrate, let him prostrate; whoever cannot, let him not raise anything to his face to prostrate on, and let him gesture with his head in his bowing and prostration.' Reported by al-Tabarani.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the rulings for a sick person who cannot stand or prostrate in prayer. It begins by stating that if standing would increase illness or delay recovery, one prays sitting with normal bowing and prostration, citing the famous hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn. The sitting posture is whatever is comfortable without harm, with no dislike in the relied-upon view. If one can partially stand, they must stand as much as possible, even for the opening takbir and one verse; severe pain permitting sitting from the start is analogous to total incapacity. When bowing and prostration are impossible but sitting is possible, one prays sitting with head gestures (ima'), with the gesture for prostration lower than for bowing. The hadith about the sick man and the cushion proves that raising an object to the forehead is prohibited; instead, one must gesture. If the gestures are equal, the prayer is invalid because prostration is effectively missed while capability exists. The text also mentions the narration from al-Tabarani reinforcing this. The commentary notes intra-madhhab differences, such as whether minimal inclination suffices for ima', with the relied-upon view being that a mere movement of the head without lowering is insufficient. Overall, the ruling emphasizes performing as much as one is able, prioritizing sitting over lying, and avoiding objects for prostration.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gesture with the head indicating bowing and prostration when unable to perform the physical actions.
أخفض (akhfad): Lower (as in gesture height); the gesture for prostration must be lower than that for bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a sick person makes the head gestures for bowing and prostration equal in height?
A) The prayer is valid but disliked.
B) The prayer is invalid because prostration is not properly indicated.
C) They must repeat only the prostration gesture.
D) They may continue the prayer normally.

Key Takeaway
Inability to prostrate on the ground requires head gestures with clear differentiation, and raising any object to the forehead is prohibited, invalidating the prayer.

intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Ima' for Ruku' and Sujud: Obligation and Proper Form
Fiqh ruling with proof from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ima' for the sick, differentiate the required depth of sujud gesture over ruku', and identify the invalidity when gestures are equal.

Core Idea
Sujud gesture must be lower than ruku' gesture; equality invalidates the prayer.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the obligation of ima' for those unable to perform actual ruku' and sujud, and emphasizes that the gesture for sujud must be visibly lower than that for ruku'. It provides prophetic proofs and explains the consequence of equality. Understanding this ruling ensures the sick person's prayer is valid in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
Determine what act is being ruled upon (ima' for ruku' and sujud) and for whom (the sick person unable to perform actual movements). Note that the ruling is wajib.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the two hadith proofs: the Prophet's instruction to the sick man (the longer hadith) and the Tabarani hadith prohibiting raising an object.
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah
Focus on the command 'make your sujud lower than your ruku''. In Hanafi usul, the imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Thus the lowering is required, not merely recommended.
4
Determine the Consequence of Violation
If the gestures are equal, the prayer is invalid because sujud is not achieved either in reality or legally. The passage explicitly states 'la tasihhu salatuhu'.
5
Note the Additional Prohibition
The passage also prohibits raising an object to the face to prostrate upon. This is based on a separate hadith and reinforces that ima' should be done with the head alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخفض من إيمانه) برأسه (للركوع) وكذا لو عجز عن السجود، وقدر على الركوع يومىء بهما لأن النبي عاد مريضاً فرآه يصلي على وسادة فأخذها فرمي بها فأخذ عوداً ليصلي عليه فرمي به وقال صل على الأرض إن استطعت وإلا فأوم إيماء واجعل سجودك أخفض من ركوعك فإن لم يخفضه) أي الإيماء للسجود (عنه) أي عن الإيماء للركوع بأن جعلهما على حد سواء ( لا تصح صلاته لفقد السجود حقيقة، وحكماً مع القدرة (ولا يرفع بالبناء للمجهول الوجهه شيء) كحجر وخشبة ( يسجد عليه لما قدمناه، ولقوله : (من استطاع منكم أن يسجد فليسجد ومن لم يستطع فلا يرفع إلى وجهه شيئاً يسجد عليه، وليكن في ركوعه وسجوده يومي برأسه) رواه الطبراني
He lowers his head for ruku'. Similarly, if one is unable to prostrate (sajdah) but can perform ruku', he gestures with both because the Prophet visited a sick person and saw him praying on a cushion; he took it and threw it away, then he took a stick to pray on it, and threw it away, and said: 'Pray on the ground if you can; otherwise gesture, and make your sujud lower than your ruku'. If he does not lower his gesture for sujud compared to his gesture for ruku', making both equal, his prayer is invalid due to losing sujud in reality and legally while being capable. And one should not raise to his face anything (like a stone or a piece of wood) to prostrate upon, due to what we have presented, and due to his saying: 'Whoever among you can prostrate, let him prostrate, and whoever cannot, let him not raise anything to his face to prostrate upon, but in his ruku' and sujud let him gesture with his head.' Narrated by Tabarani.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the prayer of a sick person who cannot perform normal ruku' and sujud. It begins by establishing that a person unable to bow (ruku') but capable of prostrating (sujud) should still gesture with his head for both. The proof is a hadith of the Prophet, who instructed a sick man to lower his head for sujud more than for ruku', indicating that the gesture for sujud must be visibly deeper. If the gestures are equal, the prayer is invalid because the required prostration (sujud) is not achieved either realistically or legally, as the person is still capable of performing the gesture properly. The passage then prohibits raising an object (like a stone or wood) to the face to simulate prostration, citing a different hadith where the Prophet forbade this. Instead, the person should gesture with his head only. The hadith is attributed to Tabarani. This ruling underscores that the essence of sujud in prayer must be preserved even in sickness.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-imā’): Gesturing with the head as a substitute for actual ruku' and sujud in prayer when physically unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'make your sujud lower than your ruku'' indicate?
A) It is recommended (sunnah).
B) It is obligatory (wajib).
C) It is optional (mubah).
D) It applies only to the sick.

Key Takeaway
Ima' for sujud must be visibly lower than for ruku'; equality invalidates the prayer.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Extent of Ima' Bending
Resolves whether minimal or maximal bending is required in ima'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the required bending in ima' and identify which is the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
In ima', a slight bow of the head suffices; maximum bending is not required for the sick.

This passage addresses a subtle but important disagreement within the Hanafi school about how much a sick person must bend when performing prayer by gesture (ima'). While some scholars argued that the full act of bowing must be approximated as much as possible, the majority view—and the operative fatwa—is that a minimal indication (lowering the head slightly) is sufficient for both ruku' and sujud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and note the two opposing views: Abu Hanifa's stance that minimal bending suffices, and Ibn al-Fadl's objection that mere head movement does not constitute proper ima'.
The passage also cites a narration from Shaykh al-Islam al-Mumi supporting minimal bending.
2
Locate the proofs for each side
Abu Hanifa relies on practical ease and a hadith that does not specify maximum; Ibn al-Fadl argues that the essence of ima' is bowing the head (ta’ta’at al-ra’s), so slight movement fails to meet that definition.
The text explicitly states that 'the reality of ima' is bowing the head.'
3
Analyze the basis of disagreement
The dispute hinges on whether the act of ima' is defined by the form (bowing) or by the intention (indicating the posture). Minimal bending emphasizes intention over form.
This is a classic usul distinction between haqiqat and majaz.
4
Determine the tarjih
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Bakr, and the author's discovery) is that minimal bending suffices. This is reinforced by the principle of ease for the sick.
Al-Tahtawi confirms this is 'an explicit text on the subject.'
5
Apply to a real scenario
Consider a sick person who can only move his head slightly. According to the mufta bihi, his prayer is valid if he gestures minimally for ruku' and sujud.
No requirement to bend as far as possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في المجتبى : كانت كيفية الإيماء بالركوع والسجود مشتبهاً على في أنه يكفي بعض الانحناء أم أقصى ما يمكن فظفرت على الرواية فإنه ذكر شيخ الإسلام المومي إذا خفض رأسه للركوع شيئاً، ثم للسجود شيئاً جاز اهـ وفي شرح المقدسي مريض عجز عن الإيماء فحرك رأسه عن أبي حنيفة يجوز، وقال ابن الفضل لا يجوز لأنه لم يوجد منه الفعل انتهى فحقيقة الإيماء طأطأة الرأس انتهت عبارته وقال أبو بكر : إذا كان بجبهته وأنفه عذر يصلي بالإيماء، ولا يلزمه تقريب الجبهة إلى الأرض بأقصى ما يمكنه وهذا نص في الباب كما في معراج الدراية
And it is said in al-Mujtaba: The manner of gesturing for ruku' and sujud was ambiguous to me—whether a slight bending suffices or the maximum possible. Then I came upon the narration that Shaykh al-Islam al-Mumi said: If he lowers his head slightly for ruku', then for sujud slightly, it is permissible. In Sharh al-Maqdisi: A sick person unable to gesture moved his head; according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible, but Ibn al-Fadl said it is not permissible because the act (of proper ima') did not occur. So the reality of ima' is bowing the head. His statement ends. And Abu Bakr said: If he has an excuse on his forehead and nose, he prays with ima' and he is not required to bring his forehead as close to the ground as possible. This is an explicit text on the subject as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the required degree of bending in ima' (gesturing) for the sick. The author of al-Mujtaba was uncertain whether minimal bending suffices or the maximum possible. He found the narration from Shaykh al-Islam that minimal bending for both ruku' and sujud is sufficient. Then he cites Sharh al-Maqdisi, where a sick person only moved his head (without bowing). Abu Hanifa permitted this, but Ibn al-Fadl rejected it because the proper act of ima' (which is bowing the head) was not performed. The passage concludes with a statement from Abu Bakr that if someone has an excuse on his forehead or nose, he may pray with ima' and is not required to bring his forehead as close to the ground as possible. The author of this hashiya (al-Tahtawi) points out that this is an explicit text that the maximum possible bending is not obligatory; minimal gesture suffices. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that minimal bending is acceptable, as indicated by the principle that the illness excuses the full degree of bending.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā'): Gestural prayer performed by a sick person, indicating ruku' and sujud by head movements.
طأطأة الرأس (ta’ta’at al-ra’s): Bowing the head, considered the defining act of ima'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The maximum possible bending.
B) A slight lowering of the head.
C) Moving the head in any direction.
D) Touching the forehead to the ground.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that minimal bending suffices for ima', prioritizing ease for the sick over exact form.

Ruling on Using an Object for Sujud While Gesturing
Clarifies the ruling if a sick person uses an object for sujud while also gesturing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick person using an object for sujud while gesturing, and explain why it is considered valid but sinful (makruh tahrimi).

Core Idea
Using an object for sujud when sick is valid but sinful — the gesture must still be present.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a sick person should gesture (ima') for sujud and ruku'. But what if he places a cushion and prostrates on it? This lesson addresses that scenario, clarifying that the prayer remains valid but carries sin because it departs from the sunnah method. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi difference on whether this counts as actual prostration or just gesture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing an object to prostrate upon while performing ima' for sujud and ruku'. The ruling is 'sahha' (valid) but 'ma'a al-isā'ah' (with sin).
2
Locate the dalil
The author references a hadith ('ما روينا') that prohibits raising something to the forehead, implying that using an object is against the sunnah.
The exact hadith is not quoted but is known in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that proper sujud is on the ground without an object. Deviating from this method incurs sin, but the prayer remains valid because the essential gesture (ima') is still performed.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars consider this actual sujud rather than ima'. This affects whether compensations like sajdah al-sahw are needed.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is ima' and valid but disliked.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities (like al-Tahtawi) rely on the view that it is valid but makruh tahrimi. The presence of gesture saves the prayer from invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن فعل) أي وضع شيئاً فسجد عليه وخفض رأسه) للسجود عن إيمائه للركوع (صح) أي صحت صلاته لوجود الإيماء لكن مع الإساءة لما روينا وقيل هو سجود كذا في الغاية
If he does so, meaning he places something and prostrates upon it, and lowers his head for prostration more than his gesture for ruku', it is valid, i.e., his prayer is valid because the gesture exists, but with sinfulness due to what we have narrated. And it is said: It is prostrating, as in al-Ghayah.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage rules on the situation where a sick person places an object (like a cushion or a stone) in front of him and prostrates on it while also ensuring that his head is lowered more for sujud than for ruku'. The prayer is valid because the required gesture (ima') still occurs; the lowering of the head fulfills the obligation of gesturing. However, the act is considered sinful (isā'a) because he is using an object when the proper method is to gesture without any object, as indicated by the previously mentioned hadith prohibiting raising something to the face. The comment 'it is said: it is prostrating' indicates a difference of opinion among scholars: some consider this actual prostration (sujud) rather than mere gesture, which would have different implications. But the relied-upon view is that it remains ima' and is valid but disliked (makruh tahriman).

Key Terms
الإساءة (al-isā’ah): Act of sinfulness or doing something disliked (makruh) in the context of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid because an object is used.
B) Valid but sinful (makruh).
C) Valid and recommended.
D) Invalid if he can gesture without an object.

Key Takeaway
Using an object for sujud when sick is valid only if the gesture (ima') is properly performed; it remains sinful (makruh) due to departure from the sunnah.

Sick Person's Recitation and Posture in Prayer
Describes sick person's obligations and posture for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations of a sick person regarding recitation in prayer and identify the correct posture when sitting is impossible.

Core Idea
Sick persons pray as much as they can; recitation is required if possible, and if sitting is impossible, they pray lying down.

This lesson addresses the prayer of a sick person. It clarifies that all obligatory acts (recitation, tasbih, tashahhud) remain required to the extent of ability. If the person cannot sit, the prayer is performed lying down, with specific preference for lying on the back over the right side.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligations
The sick person must perform recitation, tasbih, and tashahhud just as a healthy person does, as long as they are able.
These are wajib acts; inability excuses them, but no substitute is required.
2
Determine the effect of partial inability
If the sick person cannot perform a specific wajib (e.g., recitation), it is dropped. The prayer continues with what is possible.
This is based on the principle of 'ability' (istita'ah).
3
Apply the ruling for sitting difficulty
If sitting is impossible even with support, the sick person prays lying down—either on the back or on the side—and gestures with the head for ruku' and sujud.
Lying on the back is preferable (awla) because it allows better facing of the qibla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفعل المريض في صلاته من القراءة والتسبيح، والتشهد ما يفعله الصحيح وإن عجز عن ذلك تركه كما في التتارخانية عن التجريد ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه للسجود أنزل عن الركوع بأن جعلهما سواء (لا) تصح صلاته لترك فرض الإيماء للسجود كما فعل ذلك من كما غير رفع شيء تقدم بيانه (وإن تعسر القعود فلم يقدر عليه متكئاً، ولا مستنداً إلى حائط، أو غيره بلا ضرر (أومأ مستلقياً) على قفاه (أو على جنبه) والأيمن أفضل من الأيسر ورد به الأثر (والأول) الاستلقاء على قفاه (أولى) الجنب الأيمن
And the sick person does in his prayer of recitation, glorification, and testimony what the healthy person does. If he is unable to do that, he abandons it, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Tajrid. (If not) that is, if he does not lower his head for sujud compared to his gesture for ruku', then his prayer is invalid because he abandons the obligatory gesture for sujud, as done by that person who did not raise anything as previously explained. (If sitting is difficult) and he is unable to sit leaning or resting against a wall or otherwise without hardship (he gestures lying on his back) or on his side, and the right side is better than the left, as reported. (And the first) lying on his back (is preferable) to the right side.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage consists of two rulings. First, a sick person who can recite, do tasbih, and tashahhud must perform them like a healthy person; if unable, he omits them—there is no substitute. The text then returns to the earlier ruling: if he doesn't lower his head for sujud relative to ruku', the prayer is invalid. Second, if the person cannot sit even with support (leaning or against a wall) without hardship, then he prays lying down (on his back or side) and gestures with his head. The passage notes that lying on the right side is better than the left based on transmitted reports, but lying on the back (which allows better facing of the qibla) is preferable overall. This is a practical ruling for those who are bedridden.

Key Terms
الاستلقاء (al-istiqlā’): Lying on one's back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Sitting with support.

Key Takeaway
Inability excuses obligatory acts; the sick pray to their capacity, and if even sitting is impossible, lying down with gesture is valid.

Qada' When Gesture is Impossible: Four Cases
Ruling on qada' when gesture is impossible with four scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four scenarios for qada' of missed prayers when a person cannot gesture, and state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
Qada' of missed prayers depends on consciousness and duration: if conscious, qada' is required; if unconscious, it is dropped.

When a person is so ill that even gesturing with the head is impossible, the obligation to pray is not lifted. Instead, prayer is postponed. The crucial question is whether those postponed prayers must be made up (qada') when the person recovers. The Hanafi school answers this by examining two factors: whether the person was conscious during the period, and how many prayers were missed. This lesson unravels the four possible combinations and the consensus and disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of postponement
First, note that if gesturing is impossible, prayer is postponed (not dropped). This is the starting point for the qada' discussion.
Consensus exists for a day and night or less.
2
List the two factors: consciousness and duration
The qada' ruling turns on whether the person was conscious (ya'qil) during the incapacity, and whether the number of missed prayers is 'many' (six or more) or 'few' (five or fewer, up to a day and night).
Six prayers corresponds to the five daily prayers plus witr, or six as a technical threshold.
3
Map the four scenarios
The text presents four cases: 1) unconscious for six prayers – qada' dropped by consensus; 2) conscious for less than six – qada' required by consensus; 3) conscious for six prayers – ikhtilaf; 4) unconscious for less than six – ikhtilaf.
Cases 3 and 4 are where scholars differ.
4
Locate the mufta bihi within the ikhtilaf
According to al-Hidayah and the preferred view, if the person is conscious, qada' is required regardless of duration. If unconscious, no qada'. This resolves cases 3 and 4.
Al-Bazdawi al-Saghir held the opposite in case 3 (conscious six prayers – no qada').
5
Apply the rule to the sound-only case
The passage ends with a distinct scenario: a person who can only make inarticulate sounds (like 'ugh') must still pray. If later speech returns, no repetition is needed, reinforcing that the prayer is valid.
This shows that the obligation remains even with minimal ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تعذر الإيماء) برأسه أخرت عنه الصلاة القليلة وهي صلاة يوم وليلة فما دونها اتفاقاً، وأما إذا زادت على وليلة فلما يوم دام يفهم) مضمون (الخطاب) فإنه يقضيها في رواية (قال في الهداية) صلاة كراهة التحريم فيما يظهر للنهي عنه في الحديثين السابقين. قوله: (فلم يقدر الخ) هذا تعذر حقيقي ومثله الحكمي بأن كان بحال لو قعد بزغ الماء من عينيه فأمره الطبيب بالاستلقاء أياماً ونهاه عن القعود والسجود فإنه يجزيه أن يستلقي ويصلي بالإيماء لأن حرمة الأعضاء كحرمة النفس كذا في البحر . قوله : ( بلا ضرر متعلق بقوله فلم يقدر أما إذا قدر على الاتكاء بضرر فلا يلزمه. قوله : (أوما مستلقياً الخ) اعلم أن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال أظهرها أنه بالخيار بين الاستلقاء، والاضطجاع، وهو جواب الكتب المشهورة كالهداية وشروحها ثانيها أن الاستلقاء إنما يجوز إذا عجز عن الاضطجاع كمذهب الشافعي . ثالثها أن الاضطجاع إنما يجوز إذا عجز عن الاستلقاء، وفي القنية أنه الأظهر ورده في البحر، وقال في النهر أنه شاذ. قوله: (وسقوط التوجه) عطف على جواز الخ، وهو من عطف اللازم . قوله فيمتد) برجليه الأولى حذفه . قوله : (أخرت عنه الصلاة القليلة اعلم أن المسألة على أربعة أوجه إن دام به العجز ست صلوات، وهو لا يعقل سقط عنه القضاء إجماعاً، وإن كان أقل، وهو يعقل قضى إجماعاً، وإن دام ست صلوات وهو يعقل أو أقل وهو لا يعقل ففيهما اختلاف المشايخ فمنهم من قال: يلزمه القضاء وهو اختيار صاحب الهداية ومنهم من قال : لا يلزمه وهو اختيار البزدوي الصغير، وفي البحر عن القنية مريض لا يمكنه الصلاة إلا بأصوات مثل أوه، ونحوه يجب عليه أن يصلي، ولو اعتقل لسانه يوماً وليلة فصلى صلاة الأخرس، ثم انطلق لسان لا تلزمه الإعادة
If gesturing with the head is impossible, the few prayers are postponed—that is, the prayers of a day and night or less, by consensus. As for when more than a day and night, as long as he remains conscious of the content of the address, he makes them up (in one narration). He said in al-Hidayah: Prohibition is karahah tahrimah due to the prohibition in the two previous hadith. His statement: 'he is unable' etc. This is real incapacity, and similarly legal incapacity, such as if when he sits, water gushes from his eyes, so the doctor orders him to lie down for days and forbids sitting and prostrating; then it suffices him to lie down and pray with gesture because the sanctity of limbs is like the sanctity of life, as in al-Bahr. His statement: 'without hardship' is attached to his saying 'he is unable'. If he can lean with hardship, it is not obligatory. His statement: 'he gestures lying down' etc. Know that there are three opinions on this issue: the strongest is that he has a choice between lying on his back and lying on his side, which is the answer of famous books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries. Second: lying on the back is only permissible if unable to lie on the side, like the Shafi'i school. Third: lying on the side is only permissible if unable to lie on the back. In al-Qunyah it is considered the stronger view, but al-Bahr rejects it, and al-Nahr says it is shadhdh (irregular). His statement: 'and the fall of facing the qibla' is a conjunction on 'permissibility' etc., and it is a conjunction of necessity. His statement: 'so his legs extend' etc. It is better to delete it. His statement: 'the few prayers are postponed' etc. Know that the issue has four aspects: If the incapacity persists for six prayers and he is not conscious, qada' is dropped by consensus. If less and he is conscious, qada' is required by consensus. If it persists for six prayers while he is conscious, or less while he is not conscious, the scholars differed: some (like the author of al-Hidayah) said qada' is required; others (like al-Bazdawi al-Saghir) said it is not. In al-Bahr from al-Qunyah: A sick person who can only pray with sounds like 'ugh' etc. must pray. If his tongue is constricted for a day and night and he prays the prayer of a mute, then his tongue is released, he is not required to repeat.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage addresses the extreme case where a sick person cannot even gesture with his head. It states that for a short period (prayers of a day and night or fewer), those prayers are postponed. If the period is longer, the ruling depends on whether the person is conscious and aware of the obligation. The text quotes al-Hidayah that the prohibition is karahah tahrimah (close to haram) based on two previous hadith. It then explains real and legal incapacity, noting that if a doctor orders lying down, the person may pray lying down because preserving the limbs is like preserving life. There is a discussion of which lying position is best, with the author favoring the view that one may choose. The most important part is the four cases regarding qada' (making up missed prayers). If the person is unconscious for six prayers or fewer? Actually it says if incapacity lasts six prayers and he is unconscious, qada' is dropped by consensus. If less but conscious, qada' required. If conscious for six prayers or unconscious for less, scholars differ. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school according to al-Hidayah is that qada' is required if the person is conscious, regardless of duration. The passage concludes with a ruling on one who can only produce inarticulate sounds—he must pray; if later his speech returns, he does not repeat.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): Making up missed prayers after the time has passed.
تعذر (ta‘adhdhur): Impossibility or incapacity.
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesture, especially with the head, in place of bowing and prostrating.
الاستلقاء (al-istilqā’): Lying on the back.
الاضطجاع (al-iḍṭijā‘): Lying on the side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qada' is required for the first day and night only.
B) Qada' is required for all missed prayers.
C) Qada' is not required because the duration exceeds a day and night.
D) Qada' is not required because the person is completely incapacitated.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qada' of missed prayers due to total physical incapacity is wajib if the person was conscious, but dropped if unconscious, as settled by the later mujtahids.

Method of Prayer for the Sick Unable to Sit
Rulings on how the sick perform prayer by gestures while lying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a sick person's prayer using gestures and apply the Hanafi rulings on lying positions.

Core Idea
A sick person must perform prayer by gestures; omitting the prostration gesture invalidates the prayer.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains how a sick person who cannot sit or bow should perform salah. It details the obligatory gestures, the recommended lying positions, and the evidence from hadith. Understanding these rulings ensures that the prayer remains valid despite physical limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for the sick
The sick person must perform recitations like the healthy; if unable to lower head for sujud, he must make ruku' and sujud equal. The passage states that omitting the sujud gesture invalidates.
The key is that the gesture of sujud is obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil for lying on the back
The hadith 'فإن لم يستطع فعلى قفاه' is cited as evidence for preferring the back position.
This is an ahad hadith, with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command indicates that when unable to sit, the back position is commanded, thus preferred. Also it facilitates facing qibla.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Shafi'i prefers side-lying (idtijā') over back, while Hanafi holds back better. The difference stems from different interpretations of ease and evidence.
The practical difference: which position to adopt.
5
Derive the practical requirements
From the passage, a sick person must face qibla by placing a pillow, raise knees to avoid pointing legs at qibla, and pray within ability.
These are recommendations for proper adab.

(Otherwise) meaning if he does not lower his head for prostration, he lowers from bowing by making them equal; (not) his prayer is valid because he left the obligatory gesture for prostration as he did that from something other than raising as previously explained. (If sitting is difficult and he is unable to lean, nor support against a wall or other without harm, (he gestures while lying) on his back (or on his side) and the right is better than the left as reported, (and the first) lying on the back (is better) than the right side, because it is easy without hardship from the hadith: 'if he cannot, then on his back' and because facing the qibla is more in it. Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings for a sick person's prayer when unable to sit normally. It states that the sick person performs recitations, tasbih, and tashahhud like a healthy person, and if unable, omits them. If he cannot lower his head for prostration, he must make his bowing and prostrations equal by not lowering his head; otherwise, his prayer is invalid because the gesture of prostration is a fard. If sitting is difficult and he cannot lean on something without harm, he gestures while lying on his back or side. The right side is better than the left per tradition, but lying on the back is better than the right side due to a hadith and because facing the qibla is better. He should place a pillow under his head to face the qibla and to enable gesturing. He should also raise his knees to avoid extending legs toward the qibla, which is makruh if he can refrain.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā'): Gesture with the head to indicate bowing and prostration when unable to perform the actual movements.
استلقاء (istilqā'): Lying on one's back, the preferred position for the sick to gesture prayer.
اضطجاع (idṭijā'): Lying on one's side, specifically the right side, as an alternative to lying on the back.

Key Takeaway

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qada for Persistent Inability to Gesture
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for gesture inability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on qada when a person cannot gesture with the head for more than five prayers, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When inability to gesture persists beyond five prayers, the obligation to make up falls off.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if a sick person cannot even gesture with the head, must they make up prayers later? All agree for a short period (a day and night or less) that qada is required. But if the disability lasts longer, the Hanafi masters divided. The early view held that qada remains obligatory; the later view, which became the fatwa, holds that the prayers drop entirely. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed case
Note that for a period of a day and night or less, all Hanafi scholars agree that qada is required.
This is the starting point before the dispute.
2
State the two positions on longer duration
For more than five prayers, there are two views: (1) qada is obligatory; (2) qada is not obligatory and the prayers fall off.
The first view is found in some early narrations; the second is the majority view.
3
Trace the proofs for each view
The minority view relies on the hadith 'Allah is more entitled to accept the excuse' interpreted as accepting delay, and on the principle that intellect entails responsibility. The majority counters that command requires ability; mere intellect is insufficient when action is impossible.
The hadith is cited but not verbatim in the text.
4
Identify the tarjih and mufta bihi
The majority view (dropping of qada) is confirmed by Qadi Khan, al-Sarakhsi, al-Hidayah (final position), and many others. It is the fatwa in al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khulasah, and other works.
The text repeatedly says 'upon it is the fatwa' and 'it is the correct view.'
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a patient unable to gesture for six months. Under the mufta bihi, no qada is required. Under the other view, all missed prayers must be made up.
The practical difference is enormous.

Source Text

And if gesture with his head is impossible, the few prayers are delayed for him, which is the prayer of a day and night and less, by agreement. As for when it exceeds a day and night, for as long as the disability continues, he understands the content of the address; he makes them up in one narration. (He said in al-Hidayah) and al-Mustasfa is the correct one, and (the author of al-Hidayah) has asserted, contradicting her (i.e., the earlier ruling) in his book al-Tajnīs and al-Mazīd, the dropping of qada if his inability to gesture with his head continues for more than five prayers, even if he understands the content of the address, like the unconscious person. Qadi Ghani and Qadikhan (confirmed it); he said: 'Because mere intellect is not sufficient for the address to be directed.' And al-Kamal said, 'And similar to it (i.e., the confirmation of Qadikhan) is in al-Muhīt, and it was chosen by Shaykh al-Islam Khwāharzādah and Fakhr al-Islam al-Sarakhsī.' And it is said in al-Zāhīriyyah that it is the apparent narration and upon it is the fatwa, as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. And in al-Khulāṣah it is the selected view, and it was confirmed in al-Yanābī'; he said it is correct as in al-Tatarakhāniyyah and al-Badā'i', and al-Walwāljī and al-Fatāwā al-Sughrā affirmed it. And in Sharh al-Tahāwī: if he is unable to gesture and move his head, prayer drops from him. And the consideration in the difference of tarjīḥ is what the majority hold, and they are those who say dropping here (may Allah have mercy on them all and return us to their blessings and aid).
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage discusses what happens if a sick person cannot even gesture with his head. If the disability lasts a day and night or less, the prayers are delayed and must be made up after recovery, by consensus. If it lasts longer, there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars. The author of al-Hidayah initially held that if it lasts more than five prayers, the obligation to make up falls off, but later in al-Tajnīs he adopted the dropping view. Many later scholars like Qadi Khan, al-Sarakhsi, and others confirm that no qada is required because mere intellect does not make the command effective. This is the relied-upon fatwa. They interpret the hadith 'Allah is more entitled to accept one's excuse' as dropping the obligation entirely, not just delaying it.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed prayer after its time.
عذر ('udhr): A valid excuse that permits a person to neglect or modify the performance of prayer, such as sickness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The prayers are not obligatory and no qada is required
C) The person must repeat the prayers immediately
D) The person should pray with heart alone

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person is unable to gesture with the head for more than five consecutive prayers, the obligation to make up those prayers drops entirely.

Valid Gesture in the Sick Person's Prayer
Rulings on valid gesture and posture for the sick in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible substitutes for head gesture in prayer and explain the dispute regarding the interpretation of the hadith on the sick person's prayer.

Core Idea
Only head gesture is valid in prayer; eyes, heart, and eyebrows cannot substitute.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two critical points for the sick person's prayer: which body parts can replace head gesture, and the best posture when one can stand but not bow. It also introduces an important dispute among Hanafi scholars about the meaning of the Prophet's statement regarding the obligatory nature of making up missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is gesturing (īmā') for bowing and prostrating when unable to move the head. The ruling: only gesture with the head is valid; eyes, heart, and eyebrows are invalid because prostration is connected to the head, not those parts.
This is the majority Hanafi position.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalīl)
The hadith: 'The sick person prays standing; if unable, then sitting; if unable, then on his back, gesturing; if unable, then Allah is more entitled to accept his excuse.' The word 'gesturing' (yūmī) is understood as head gesture, as corroborated by other texts.
The hadith is aḥad but accepted in practice.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafī dispute
Imam Zufar allowed eye and heart gesture, but the majority reject this because the hadith only mentions gesture without specifying other parts, and prostration is physically linked to the head.
The practical consequence: prayer invalid according to majority if eyes are used.
4
Examine the dispute over the hadith's concluding phrase
The phrase 'Allah is more entitled to accept his excuse' is interpreted two ways: (1) excuse for delay, requiring qaḍāʾ; (2) excuse for dropping, so no qaḍāʾ. The majority adopt the latter.
This affects whether missed prayers must be made up.
5
Apply the ruling for a specific scenario
If a person can stand but cannot bow/prostrate, he should pray sitting with gesture. This is better than standing and gesturing, because the hadith sequence prioritizes sitting when unable to perform bowing/prostration.
The text ends abruptly here; the full ruling may continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) من عجز عن الإيماء برأسه (لم يوم) أي لم يصح إيماؤه (بعينه و لا قلبه و لا (حاجبه لأن السجود تعلق بالرأس دون العين والحاجب والقلب، فلا ينتقل إليها حفله كاليد لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (يصلي المريض قائماً فإن لم يستطع فقاعداً فإن لم يستطع فعلى قفاه يومىء إيماء فإن لم يستطع فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه وقد اختلفوا في معنى قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه فمنهم من فسره بقبول عذر التأخير، فقال بلزوم القضاء ومنهم من فسره بقبول عذر الإسقاط ، فقال : بعد القضاء وهم الأكثرون وقد علمتهم وإن قدر على القيام وعجز عن الركوع والسجود صلى قاعداً بالإيماء) وهو أفضل من إيمائه قائماً، ويسقط الركوع عمن
(And) whoever is unable to gesture with his head, (does not gesture) meaning his gesture is not valid (with his eye, nor his heart, nor his eyebrow) because prostration is connected to the head, not the eye, eyebrow, and heart, so it cannot be transferred to them, like the hand, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The sick person prays standing; if unable, then sitting; if unable, then on his back, gesturing; if unable, then Allah is more entitled to accept his excuse.' And they differed on the meaning of his saying 'Allah is more entitled to accept his excuse': some interpreted it as accepting the excuse of delay, so they said qada is binding; others interpreted it as accepting the excuse of dropping, so they said (no qada?), and they are the majority, as you know. And if he is able to stand and unable to bow and prostrate, he prays sitting with gesture, and that is better than his gesture while standing, and bowing drops from whoever...
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, if a person cannot gesture with his head, he may not substitute with his eyes, heart, or eyebrows. This is because prostration relates to the head, not these parts, and the textual evidence (the hadith) only mentions head gesture. Zufar reportedly differed, allowing eye and heart gesture, but the majority reject this. The hadith quoted says: 'The sick person prays standing; if unable, then sitting; if unable, then on his back, gesturing; if unable, then Allah is more entitled to accept his excuse.' The interpretation of this hadith is contested: some say it means the excuse allows delay (so qada required), while the majority say it means the excuse drops the obligation (no qada). Second, if a person can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, he should pray sitting and gesture for those acts. This is better than standing and gesturing, because the hadith indicates the sequence of positions.

Key Terms
عذر الإسقاط ('udhr al-isqāt): The excuse that drops the obligation entirely, as interpreted by the majority of Hanafi scholars in the context of inability to gesture.
إيماء بالعين (īmā' bil-'ayn): Gesturing with the eyes, which the Hanafi school deems invalid for replacing head gesture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is not valid because prostration is related to the head
D) It is valid according to the majority of Hanafis

Key Takeaway
Only head gesture is valid in the sick person's prayer; if unable, no substitution with eyes or heart, and if able to stand but not bow, sitting and gesturing is better.

Ruling on Gesture (Ima') and Make-up (Qada) for the Incapacitated Patient
Explains the ruling on one unable to gesture with the head

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling on the obligation of make-up prayers when a patient is unable to gesture with the head for more than five prayers, and explain the basis for the intra-school dispute.

Core Idea
If inability to gesture exceeds five prayers, the majority of Hanafis hold that no make-up is required—Allah accepts the excuse of dropping the obligation.

This passage addresses a crucial question: what happens when a sick person cannot even gesture with the head for an extended period? The majority Hanafi position, supported by many authorities, is that the obligation to make up those prayers is dropped entirely. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the intra-school disagreement, and the practical implication for the patient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on gesture (ima')
Determine the substitute allowed for the head when one cannot perform ruku' and sujud.
The passage explicitly limits ima' to the head; eyes, heart, and eyebrows are invalid.
2
Identify the dispute over make-up (qada)
When inability persists beyond five prayers, is qada required? Note the opposing views.
Author of al-Hidayah says yes; majority says no.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Locate the hadith: 'The sick person prays standing...' and analyze its structure.
All parties use the same hadith.
4
Trace the interpretation of the final clause
How does 'Allah is more worthy of accepting the excuse' yield the two positions?
One school says accept delay (qada remains); the other says accept dropping (qada falls).
5
Note the majority position and its weight
Identify the authorities who side with dropping qada and the tarjih mechanism.
The majority view is mufta bihi.

The most correct: The book of prayer. Al-Mustasfa is the correct [view]. And the author of al-Hidayah decisively opposed her [the narration] in his book al-Tajnis, adding the dropping of make-up if his inability to gesture with his head continues for more than five prayers even if he understands the content of the address like one who is unconscious. Qadi Ghani and Qadikhan confirmed it. He said: because mere intellect is insufficient for the address to be directed. Al-Kamal said: and similar to it in al-Muhit, and chosen by Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zada and Fakhr al-Islam al-Sarakhsi. And in al-Zahiriyya it is the manifest narration and upon it is the fatwa. In al-Khulasa it is the chosen [view]. And in al-Yanabi' he confirmed it, said it is the correct [view] as in al-Tatarkhaniyya and al-Bada'i', and al-Walwaliji and al-Fatawa al-Sughra confirmed it. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: if one is unable to gesture and move his head, prayer drops from him. The consideration in difference of tarjih is upon what the majority are upon, and they are those who say dropping here. And one who is unable to gesture with his head: he does not gesture with his eye nor his heart nor his eyebrow because prostration is attached to the head, not to the eye, eyebrow, and heart, so it does not transfer to them like the hand, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'The sick person prays standing, if he cannot then sitting, if he cannot then on his back gesturing, if he cannot then Allah is more worthy of accepting the excuse from him.' And they differed over the meaning of his saying peace be upon him 'Allah is more worthy of accepting the excuse from him.' Some interpreted it as accepting the excuse of delay, so they said make-up is necessary. And some interpreted it as accepting the excuse of dropping, so they said no make-up, and they are the majority, as you know.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prayer of a person who is continuously unable to gesture with his head for more than five prayers. The core ruling, held by the majority of Hanafi authorities, is that no make-up (qada) is required for those prayers if the inability persists beyond five. This is based on the hadith: 'Allah is more worthy of accepting the excuse,' interpreted by the majority as dropping the obligation for the duration. The passage also clarifies that if a person cannot gesture with his head, he cannot substitute with the eye, heart, or eyebrow, because prostration is specifically attached to the head. This is supported by the same hadith, which only mentions gesturing with the head. The commentator notes that al-Hidayah opposed the majority view, but other authorities like Qadikhan and al-Sarakhsi confirm the dropping. The fatwa is upon the view that no make-up is required, especially when the inability is continuous.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-imā'): Gesturing with the head as a substitute for bowing and prostration in prayer when one cannot physically perform them.
سقوط القضاء (suqūṭ al-qaḍā'): The dropping of the obligation to make up missed prayers due to continuous legal incapacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, what is the ruling on making up missed prayers if a patient is unable to gesture with his head for more than five consecutive prayers?
A) He must make them all up eventually.
B) He does not need to make up any beyond the fifth prayer.
C) He must make up all prayers immediately upon recovery.
D) He only needs to make up if he regains ability within the same day.

Key Takeaway
The majority of Hanafi authorities rule that make-up prayers are not required if a patient is unable to gesture with the head for more than five consecutive prayers, based on the hadith that Allah accepts the excuse of dropping the obligation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Completing Prayer During Illness and Rulings of Fainting/Insanity
Critical refinement of rulings on illness and fainting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on completing prayer when illness occurs during prayer and determine the qada obligation for missed prayers due to fainting or insanity from a celestial cause.

Core Idea
When illness strikes during prayer, you complete as able; fainting or insanity up to five prayers must be made up, beyond that not.

This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two important scenarios: what to do if you become ill while already in prayer, and how many prayers are owed after prolonged fainting or insanity. The Hanafi school balances obligation with capacity, allowing gestures when needed, and distinguishes between temporary and extended unconsciousness based on cause and duration. Understanding these rulings ensures that one neither unduly burdens the sick nor neglects obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the illness scenario and the well-known view
Focus on the passage ‘إذا افتتح صلاته صحيحاً وعرض له مرض فيها يتمها بما قدر ولو أتمها بالإيماء في المشهور وهو الصحيح’. Understand that the mashhur view allows completion by gestures, contrary to a narration from Abu Hanifa requiring restart.
The key principle: performing part of the prayer with actual bowing/prostration is better than invalidating the entire prayer.
2
Examine the building rules when capacity returns
Note the distinction: if the sick person prayed sitting with bowing/prostration and then recovers, they build upon the prayer (following Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). If they prayed with gestures only, they cannot build and must restart.
Building is like following an imam; a strong act cannot be built upon a weak one.
3
Analyze the fainting/insanity scenario and the key condition
Read the passage beginning ‘ومن جن بعارض سماوي أو أغمي عليه...’ Identify that the ruling depends on a celestial cause and continuity. If the condition lasts for five prayer times, those five are made up; if the sixth time enters, no qada.
The cause must be celestial (not self-inflicted like intoxication) to benefit from leniency.
4
Differentiate the intra-Hanafi dispute on measurement
Compare Muhammad’s view (counting prayer times) with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf’s view (measuring by hours exceeding a day and night). Understand the thamarah (practical consequence) using the example of fainting at forenoon and waking the next day before noon.
The fatwa in this text follows Muhammad’s view because it is verified in most reliable books.
