لما فيه ركنية القيام أصلاً قوله : (وإذا استمسك عذره بالقعود كجرحه وسلسه. قوله: (اختلف الترجيح) والمفتى به أنه يصلي منفرداً كما في البحر، والخلاف محمول على ما إذا لم تتيسر له الجماعة في بيته وإلا لم يجز له الخروج وترك القيام بالاتفاق قاله السيد. قوله: (في المشهور، وهو الصحيح وروى أبو يوسف عن الإمام: أنه يستقبل لأن تحريمته انعقدت موجبته للركوع والسجود فلا تجوز بدونهما قوله : (وأدائها) بالجر عطفاً على الإبطال، وقوله بعده ضميره يعود للإبطال قوله : (ومن جن بآفة سماوية احترز بالآفة السماوية عما لو زال عقله بالخمر فإنه يلزمه القضاء وإن طال لأنه حصل بما هو معصية، فلا . يوجب التخفيف، ولهذا يقع طلاقه، وكذا إذا ذهب عقله بالبنج ، أو الدواء عند الإمام لأن سقوط القضاء عرف بالأثر إذا حصل بآفة سماوية، فلا يقاس عليه ما حصل بفعله ولا فرق بين الجنون العارض والأصلي، بأن بلغ مجنوناً، وهو قول محمد وقال أبو يوسف الأصلي كالصبا، وفي رواية أن الجنون يسقط مطلقاً متداولاً كما في البرهان قوله واستمر به) قيد به لأنه إذا كان يفيق في وقت معلوم نحو أن يخف عند الصبح فيفيق قليلاً، ثم يعاوده الإغماء تعتبر الإفاقة فتبطل ما قبلها من حكم الإغماء إذا كان أقل من يوم وليلة، وإن لم يكن لإفاقته وقت معلوم إلا أنه يتكلم بغتة بكلام الأصحاء، ثم يغمى عليه فلا عبرة بهذه الإفاقة كذا في الشرح عن التارخانية . قوله : (بأن خرج وقت السادسة) هذا قول محمد، وهو المصحح في أكثر المعتبرات . الأنهر، وقال ابن أمير حاج قول محمد أشبه لأن المسقط للقضاء وقوعه في الحرج، وذلك بدخول الفوائت في حد التكرار وقال في الفتح وقول محمد أصح تخريجاً على قضاء
الفوائت، وعند الإمام، وأبي يوسف تعتبر بالزيادة على ساعات يوم، وليلة، ولو بلحظة لأنه المأثور عن علي، وابن عمر فكان الأخذ به أولى إذ المقادير لا تعرف إلا سماعاً، وتظهر الثمرة فيما إذا أغمي عليه عند الضحوة، ثم أفاق من الغد قبل الزوال بساعة، فهذا أكثر من يوم وليلة من حيث الساعات فلا قضاء عليه عندهما، وعند محمد يقضي لعدم مضي ستة أوقات . قوله: (والجنون مثله اعلم أن الأعذار ثلاثة ممتد جداً كالصبا يسقط به جميع العبادات، وقاصر جداً كالنوم، فلا يسقط به شيء، ومتردد بينهما، وهو الإغماء فإذا امتد ألحق بالممتد جداً، وإلا ألحق بالقاصر جداً ذكر الحدادي، ولا يعتبر الإغماء في الصوم، والزكاة لأنه يندر وجوده سنة، أو شهراً بخلاف الجنون فإنه يمتد فاعتبر في سقوط العبادات، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
By itself, no: one who is unable to prostrate but able to bow, because standing is a means to prostration, so when the objective is missed, it is necessary to skip it. And if his excuse remains while sitting, and he prays while standing, or he gestures with his head, and he prays while sitting and gesturing, and he leaves standing and prostration. If he is unable to stand due to going out for congregation, but is able at home, the preferred view differs. And if he begins his prayer healthy and then illness occurs during it, he completes it as much as he can, even if he completes it with gestures according to the well-known view, which is correct, because performing part of it with bowing and prostration is better than invalidating it, and performing all of it afterward with gestures. And if a sick person prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, then becomes healthy, he builds upon it, because building upon it is like following an imam, so it is valid according to both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?] contrary to Muhammad? And in his statement 'he prays' there is an indication that if he was able before bowing and prostration, he builds by agreement, because a strong act is not built upon a weak one. And if he performed part of it with gestures and then became able to bow and prostrate, even while sitting, he does not build, due to building a strong act upon a weak one. Similarly, whoever becomes able to sit after gesturing while he was gesturing lying on his side must start anew according to the chosen view. And whoever becomes insane due to a celestial cause or faints, even from fear of a wild animal or a human, and it continues for five prayers, he makes up those prayers. And if more, i.e., the sixth time exits, he does not make up what he missed. Thus from Ibn Umar regarding fainting, and insanity is similar; that is correct. Because standing is a pillar originally. His statement: 'And if his excuse remains while sitting, like his wound or incontinence.' His statement: 'The preferred view differs' and the fatwa is that he prays alone, as in al-Bahr, and the disagreement is when congregation is not available at home; otherwise, he is not permitted to go out and leave standing by agreement, said al-Sayyid. His statement: 'The well-known, and it is correct, and Abu Yusuf narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that he must start anew, because his tahrimah was concluded with the obligation of bowing and prostration, so it is not valid without them.' His statement: 'And performing it' in the genitive case is a conjunction of 'invalidating', and the pronoun afterward refers to 'invalidating'. His statement: 'And whoever becomes insane due to a celestial cause' is to exclude the case where his mind is lost by wine, for he must make it up even if long, because it occurred through disobedience, so it does not bring leniency; therefore his divorce is valid. Similarly, if his mind is lost by hemp or medicine according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the dropping of qada is known by effect when it occurs by a celestial cause, so what occurs by his own action cannot be analogized to it. There is no difference between temporary and original insanity, such as reaching puberty insane; this is the view of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: original insanity is like childhood. In another narration, insanity drops it absolutely, as in al-Burhan. His statement: 'and it continues' is a condition, because if he becomes conscious at a known time, e.g., he lightens at dawn and becomes conscious briefly, then fainting returns, that consciousness is considered and invalidates the previous ruling of fainting if it was less than a day and night. And if his consciousness has no known time, but he suddenly speaks like healthy people, then faints again, this consciousness is not considered. Thus in al-Sharh from al-Tarkhaniyya. His statement: 'i.e., the sixth time exits' is the view of Muhammad, and it is the verified view in most reliable books, al-Anhur. Ibn Amir Haj said: Muhammad's view is more appropriate because the dropping of qada is its occurrence in hardship, and that is by the missed prayers entering the limit of repetition. Al-Fath said: Muhammad's view is sounder based on the derivation of qada. Missed prayers: according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is measured by exceeding the hours of a day and night, even by a moment, because it is reported from Ali and Ibn Umar, so adopting it is better, since measures are only known by hearing. The fruit appears when one faints at forenoon, then becomes conscious the next day an hour before noon, this is more than a day and night in terms of hours, so there is no qada upon him according to them. According to Muhammad, he makes it up because six prayer times have not passed. His statement: 'And insanity is similar to it.' Know that excuses are three: very extensive like childhood, which drops all acts of worship; very temporary like sleep, which drops nothing; and between them, which is fainting. If it extends, it is joined to the very extensive, otherwise to the very temporary. Mentioned by al-Haddadi. Fainting is not considered in fasting and zakat because it rarely occurs for a year or a month, unlike insanity which extends, so it is considered in dropping acts of worship. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, expanding rulings on prayer for those with illness or unconsciousness. The author, al-Tahtawi, first addresses a person who cannot prostrate but can bow: such a person sits and gestures for prostration, because standing is a means to the objective (prostration), and when the objective is lost, the means is dropped. If the excuse continues, he prays sitting. He then discusses a scenario where one becomes ill after starting prayer: the well-known view (mashhur) is that he completes it as able, even by gestures, because performing part with actual bowing and prostration is superior to invalidating the entire prayer. If a sick person praying sitting becomes healthy, he may build upon his previous prayer according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), contrary to Imam Muhammad? (the text has a corruption 'falmuhammad' likely meaning 'contrary to the two Imams' or similar). The commentary clarifies that building is like following an imam, valid at them (the two). However, if one was gesturing and then gains ability to bow and prostrate, he cannot build the strong act on the weak—he must start anew. The passage then covers fainting and insanity: if caused by a celestial (divine) affliction, and it continues for five complete prayer times, those five are made up; if it exceeds five (i.e., enters the sixth), no makeup is required. This is based on a narration from Ibn Umar. The dispute between Muhammad (who uses the number of prayer times) and Imam Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (who measure by total hours exceeding a day and night) is detailed. The author favors Muhammad's view as verified in most reliable books. Finally, excuses are categorized: extensive (childhood), temporary (sleep), and intermediate (fainting if prolonged). Fainting does not affect fasting or zakat due to rarity, but insanity does. This passage guards against misunderstanding that any fainting requires full makeup; the rule depends on duration.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesturing with the head or other body part to indicate bowing and prostration when unable to perform physically.
الإغماء (al-ighmā’): Complete loss of consciousness due to a celestial cause (not self-inflicted).
البناء (al-binā’): Continuing a prayer after temporary incapacity without restarting, by building the remaining part on the valid part already performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known (mashhur) Hanafi view, if a person becomes ill after starting prayer and cannot bow or prostrate, he should:
A) Immediately end the prayer and restart when healthy.
B) Complete the prayer by sitting and gesturing with his head; his prayer is valid.
C) Continue standing but only perform slight nods; prayer is valid.
D) Lie down and gesture; the prayer is valid only if he does not move.

Key Takeaway
When illness strikes during prayer, complete as able (even by gestures) – that is the relied-upon Hanafi view; for fainting or insanity from a celestial cause, make up only up to five prayers if continuous, otherwise no qada.

Isqat of Missed Prayers and Fasts: Conditions and Proofs
Introduces isqat of prayer and fasting with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isqat for missed prayers and fasts after death, identify the condition of inability to gesture, and apply the proof from hadith and istihsan.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, missed prayers and fasts can be compensated after death by fidya, but only if the deceased was capable of performing them.

This lesson addresses the common question: can missed prayers and fasts be compensated after death? The Hanafi school affirms this through the mechanism of isqat (dropping) by fidya from the estate. However, the ruling pivots on the deceased's capacity: if they were permanently unable to perform the acts, no compensation is required; if capable, the heirs must pay fidya. This passage also defends the school's position against critics and clarifies an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum standard of gesture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
State the ruling: when a sick person dies unable to pray even by head gesture, no bequest for fidya is required. The condition is that they must have been unable to perform the acts in any valid manner.
The condition uses the minimum gesture for prayer (ima).
2
Locate the direct proof (dalil naqli)
The hadith 'If he cannot, Allah is most worthy to accept the excuse' is cited to show that inability removes the obligation of qada and thus of bequest.
The hanafi_position_box in the toolbox confirms this.
3
Trace the istihsan analogy
The mashayikh agreed that prayer is analogous to fasting by istihsan because prayer is more important. The text provides an explicit basis for fasting (Quran or hadith), and prayer is made analogous.
Each fard (prayer) is equated to one day's fast for fidya.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute and refutation
Imam Zufar argues that gesture with the eyebrow suffices, so bequest is required. The majority holds eyebrow gesture invalid. The author also refutes outsiders who deny isqat for prayer, calling their view ignorance of the madhhab.
The madhhab_dispute_map block details this.

فصل في إسقاط الصلاة والصوم وغيرهما إذا مات المريض ولم يقدر على أداء الصلاة بالإيماء) برأسه (لا يلزمه الإيضاء بها وإن قلت بنقصها عن صلاة يوم وليلة لما رويناه لعدم قدرته على القضاء بإدراك زمن له على قول من يفسر قبول العذر بجواز التأخير ومن فسره بالسقوط ظاهر (وكذا) . لا يخفى حسن ذكر هذا الفصل بعد ذكر أحكام المريض، اعلم أنه قلا ورد النص في الصوم بإسقاطه بالفدية، واتفقت كلمه المشايخ على أن الصلاة كالصوم استحساناً لكونها أهم منه، وإنما الخلاف بينهم في أن صلاة أو كل فريضة كصوم يوم، وهو المعتمد كصومه، يوم إذا علمت ذلك تعلم جهل من يقول أن إسقاط الصلاة لا أصل له إذ هذا إبطال للمتفق عليه بين أهل المذهب، وأراد المصنف بقوله : والصوم صوم رمضان بدليل قوله: بعد وغيرهما فإن المراد به صوم كفارة اليمين وقتل وظهار وجناية على إحرام وقتل محرم صيد، أو صوم منذور أفاده في الشرح قوله : (بالإيماء برأسه) قيد به لأنه لا يعتبر الإيماء بنحو الحاجب، فلا بعد به قادراً فلا تلزمه الوصية وقياس قول زفر أنه إذا تركها مع قدرته على الإيماء بنحو الحاجب أوصى قوله : (عن) صلاة يوم وليلية) إنما ذكره لأنه إذا سقط في هذه الحالة القليل الذي لا حرج فيه فأولى الكثير الذي فيه الحرج. قوله : (لما رويناه) من قوله : «فإن لم يستطع فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه قوله : (لعدم قدرته الأولى الإتيان بالواو لتكون علة ثانية عقلية بعد النقل، ويحتمل أنه علة للعلة قوله : ( بإدراك زمن متعلق بقوله: قدرته، والباء للسببية. قوله : ( على قول من يفسر الخ) فإن القائل به لا يقول بلزوم القضاء إلا بإدراك زمن يسعه ولم يوجد، ولزوم الوصية فرع لزوم القضاء، وبه يندفع ما أورد من أن الوجوب قد تعلق
Chapter on Dropping of Prayer and Fasting and Others. When a sick person dies and was unable to perform prayer even by gesturing with his head, isqat (dropping) does not necessitate bequest for it, even if the missed prayers amount to less than a day and night, because of what we have narrated, due to his inability to make up by reaching a time that would allow it, according to the view of one who interprets acceptance of the excuse as permissibility of delay; and whoever interprets it as dropping, it is apparent. And likewise. It is not hidden the goodness of mentioning this chapter after the rulings on the sick. Know that the text came in fasting regarding dropping it by fidya, and the mashayikh agreed that prayer is like fasting by istihsan because it is more important. The dispute among them is whether a single prayer or every fard is like a fast of a day, and this is the relied-upon view: like his fast of a day. When you know that, you know the ignorance of one who says that dropping of prayer has no basis, for this would nullify what is agreed upon among the scholars of the madhhab. The author meant by his statement 'and fasting' the fast of Ramadan, as evidenced by his statement 'and others', for what is meant is the fast of atonement for oath, homicide, zihar, violation of ihram, killing a game animal while muhrim, or a vowed fast, as explained in the sharh. His statement 'by gesturing with his head' is a condition because gesturing with something like the eyebrow is not considered; thus he is not considered capable, so bequest is not obligatory. By qiyas on the statement of Zufar, if he left it while being able to gesture with something like the eyebrow, he would bequeath. His statement 'from a day and night' is mentioned because if the small amount which has no hardship is dropped in this situation, then the great amount which has hardship is even more apt to be dropped. His statement 'because of what we have narrated' refers to his statement: 'If he cannot, Allah is most worthy to accept the excuse.' His statement 'due to his inability'—the first [author] inserted the waw to make it a second rational cause after the transmitted cause, and it is possible it is a cause for the cause. His statement 'to attain a time' relates to 'his ability', and the ba' is for causality. His statement 'according to the interpretation of one who interprets...' for the one who says this does not say that qada is obligatory unless a time sufficient for it is attained, and it was not found; and the obligation of bequest is subsidiary to the obligation of qada. And by this is repelled the objection that obligation had attached...
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This lesson begins a new chapter (fasl) on isqat—dropping of missed prayers and fasts after death through bequest or fidya. The passage clarifies that when a sick person dies unable to perform prayer even by gesturing with his head, he is not required to make a bequest for those prayers, because he lacked the capacity to perform them (even by gesture) and thus no qada burden arises. This is based on the hadith 'If he cannot, Allah is most worthy to accept the excuse.' The commentary notes that the mashayikh unanimously consider prayer analogous to fasting in that fidya can be given for missed fasts (based on textual evidence), and by istihsan, prayer likewise can be dropped by fidya, though prayer is more important. The dispute is only whether each single prayer equals one day's fast or something else; the relied-upon view is that each fard (prayer) is like a fast of one day. The author refutes the claim that isqat of prayer has no basis, saying it is agreed upon in the madhhab. He specifies that 'fasting' in the text primarily refers to Ramadan fasts, but also includes other obligatory fasts (kaffarah, nadhr, etc.) as indicated by 'and others'. The condition for isqat is that the deceased was unable to perform prayer even by head gesture; gesturing with eyebrow or eye is not valid, so if he could do that, he is considered capable and isqat by bequest does not apply (except by Zufar's qiyas). The mention of 'a day and night' is because if a small amount is dropped, more is even more entitled. The commentary ends mid-sentence discussing the rational cause for the ruling. This passage guards against misunderstanding that missed prayers cannot be compensated after death; the Hanafi school affirms isqat by bequest based on istihsan and the greater import of prayer.

Key Terms
الإسقاط (al-isqāṭ): Dropping of the obligation to perform missed prayers or fasts after death by means of a bequest of fidya (ransom) from the deceased's estate.
الفدية (al-fidya): Compensation given in place of missed obligatory acts of worship, typically feeding a poor person per missed prayer/fast day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a sick person dies and was unable to pray even by gesturing with his head, what is the ruling regarding isqat of missed prayers?
A) He must make a bequest for fidya for each missed prayer.
B) No bequest for those prayers is required because he was unable to perform them.
C) The heirs must perform the prayers on his behalf.
D) Isqat does not apply to prayer, only to fasting.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, missed prayers and fasts can be compensated after death by fidya from the estate if the deceased was capable of performing them before death; if they were permanently unable, no compensation is needed.

The Hanafi Ruling on Dropping Missed Prayers Due to Unconsciousness
Ruling with proof on dropping prayers and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a sick person's missed prayers are dropped without a will, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifah/Abu Yusuf from Muhammad al-Shaybani on the threshold for unconsciousness.

Core Idea
Prayers are dropped for one who never regains capacity; the threshold is hours exceeding a day and night.

This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies a nuanced ruling: for a sick person who dies without being able to pray even by gesture, no will is required because there was no time for qada. The same applies to unconsciousness, but the imams differ on the exact duration that triggers the dropping. Let's unpack the proof and the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and core ruling
The act is missing prayers due to sickness or unconsciousness. The ruling is that no will (wasiyya) is required, and the prayers are dropped if the person never regains capacity to make them up.
The text starts with a sick person who dies unable to pray even by gesture.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf
They consider the period of unconsciousness by hours; if it exceeds 24 hours even by a moment, the missed prayers are dropped and no qada is required.
They rely on the report from Ali and Ibn Umar.
3
State the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
He requires that six complete prayer times (i.e., a full day and night) have passed without recovery for the prayers to be dropped.
This is a stricter criterion.
4
Apply the ikhtilaf to the example given
If unconscious at forenoon (duha) and wakes next day an hour before noon (zawal), Abu Hanifah/Abu Yusuf say period exceeds 24 hours → no qada; Muhammad says only five prayer times passed → qada required.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear in this scenario.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the school is that of Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, supported by the hadith from Ali and Ibn Umar.
Al-Tahtawi indicates this is the stronger view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إسقاط الصلاة والصوم وغيرهما إذا مات المريض ولم يقدر على أداء الصلاة بالإيماء برأسه لا يلزمه الإيضاء بها وإن قلت بنقصها عن صلاة يوم وليلة لما رويناه لعدم قدرته على القضاء بإدراك زمن له على قول من يفسر قبول العذر بجواز التأخير ومن فسره بالسقوط ظاهر (وكذا) الفوائت، وعند الإمام، وأبي يوسف تعتبر بالزيادة على ساعات يوم، وليلة، ولو بلحظة لأنه المأثور عن علي، وابن عمر فكان الأخذ به أولى إذ المقادير لا تعرف إلا سماعاً، وتظهر الثمرة فيما إذا أغمي عليه عند الضحوة، ثم أفاق من الغد قبل الزوال بساعة، فهذا أكثر من يوم وليلة من حيث الساعات فلا قضاء عليه عندهما، وعند محمد يقضي لعدم مضي ستة أوقات . قوله: (والجنون مثله اعلم أن الأعذار ثلاثة ممتد جداً كالصبا يسقط به جميع العبادات، وقاصر جداً كالنوم، فلا يسقط به شيء، ومتردد بينهما، وهو الإغماء فإذا امتد ألحق بالممتد جداً، وإلا ألحق بالقاصر جداً ذكر الحدادي، ولا يعتبر الإغماء في الصوم، والزكاة لأنه يندر وجوده سنة، أو شهراً بخلاف الجنون فإنه يمتد فاعتبر في سقوط العبادات، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Chapter on Dropping Prayer, Fasting, and Others: When a sick person dies and was unable to perform prayer even by gesturing with his head, he is not obligated to will it, even if the missed amount is less than a day and night's prayer, based on what we have narrated, due to his inability to make it up by reaching a time that can accommodate it, according to the one who interprets acceptance of the excuse as permissibility of delay, and according to the one who interprets it as dropping it is apparent. Likewise missed prayers. According to Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, [the period] is considered by exceeding the hours of a day and night, even by a moment, because that is reported from Ali and Ibn Umar, so it is more appropriate to adopt it, since measures are only known through hearing. The application appears when one falls unconscious at forenoon, then wakes up the next day an hour before noon; this is more than a day and night in terms of hours, so no making up upon the two of them. According to Muhammad, he must make up because six prayer times have not elapsed. His saying: (Insanity is like it). Know that excuses are of three types: very prolonged like childhood, which drops all acts of worship; very short like sleep, which drops nothing; and intermediate, which is unconsciousness. If it is prolonged, it is joined to the very prolonged; otherwise, it is joined to the very short. Al-Hadadi mentioned this. Unconsciousness is not considered in fasting and zakat because it rarely lasts a year or a month, unlike insanity which is prolonged, so it is considered in dropping acts of worship. And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Almighty.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining when missed prayers are dropped (isqat) for a sick person who dies without being able to perform them, and it also addresses the status of unconsciousness and insanity. The text first states that if a sick person dies and was unable to pray even by gesturing, he is not required to make a will (wasiyya) for the missed prayers, regardless of how few they are. The proof is that he was unable to make them up because he did not experience a time that could accommodate the prayers. The author then notes a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf consider the period of unconsciousness in terms of hours—if it exceeds the hours of a day and night even by a moment, the missed prayers are dropped. Muhammad al-Shaybani requires that six complete prayer times (i.e., a day and night) must pass without recovery for the prayers to be dropped. The consequence is illustrated: if someone falls unconscious at forenoon (duha) and wakes up the next day an hour before noon, that period exceeds 24 hours, so Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf drop the prayers, but Muhammad requires making them up because six prayer times have not elapsed. The text then equates insanity with prolonged unconsciousness, and categorizes excuses: very prolonged (e.g., childhood) drops all obligations; very short (e.g., sleep) drops nothing; intermediate (unconsciousness) is judged by its duration. Unconsciousness is not considered for fasting and zakat because it rarely lasts a full year or month, unlike insanity. The authority weight is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah positions of the three imams.

Key Terms
إسقاط (isqat): The legal dropping of an obligation, so that no qada or wasiyya is required.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness that can be prolonged or short; treated as mid-level excuse.
إيصاء (isa'): The act of making a will (wasiyya) for missed religious obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling for a person who is unconscious for exactly 24 hours?
A) No qada is required because 24 hours is a day and night.
B) Qada is required because the period did not exceed 24 hours.
C) Only if the unconsciousness occurred during illness.
D) Depends on the number of prayer times missed.

Key Takeaway
Prayers of an unconscious person are dropped only if the unconsciousness exceeds 24 hours (mufta bihi); otherwise qada is required.

The Three Categories of Legal Excuses in Hanafi Fiqh
Classification of excuses and their legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any excuse (like sleep, childhood, unconsciousness, insanity) into one of three categories and state the effect on the obligation of prayers, fasting, and zakat.

Core Idea
Unconsciousness is an intermediate excuse: prolonged it drops all obligations, short it drops nothing. Insanity is like prolonged unconsciousness.

In this passage, Al-Tahtawi explains a foundational Hanafi classification: excuses are of three types – very prolonged (like childhood), very short (like sleep), and intermediate (like unconsciousness). The ruling on dropping acts of worship depends on which category the excuse falls into. Insanity is treated as a prolonged excuse, while unconsciousness is assessed by its duration. Additionally, there are special rules for fasting and zakat.

Guided Path
1
List the three categories of excuses
The text identifies three types: mumtadd jiddan (very prolonged, e.g., childhood), qasir jiddan (very short, e.g., sleep), and mutaraddid (intermediate, e.g., unconsciousness).
Al-Hadadi is cited as source for this classification.
2
Determine the effect of each category
Very prolonged excuses drop all acts of worship; very short excuses drop nothing; intermediate excuses, if prolonged, are treated as very prolonged, and if short, as very short.
This is a rule of thumb: duration determines categorization.
3
Apply to unconsciousness specifically
Unconsciousness is intermediate; if it extends (i.e., is prolonged), it joins the very prolonged category and drops prayers. If it is short, it joins the very short category and does not drop prayers.
The threshold for 'prolonged' in this context is the one discussed in the previous lesson (exceeding 24 hours).
4
Note the exception for fasting and zakat
Unconsciousness is not considered a valid excuse for missing fasting or zakat because it rarely lasts a full year or month. Insanity, however, does drop these obligations because it can be prolonged.
This is a practical distinction based on typical duration.
5
Understand how insanity is treated
Insanity (junun) is equated with prolonged unconsciousness; it is a very prolonged excuse and drops all acts of worship, including fasting and zakat, because it can extend for long periods.
The text states 'al-junun mithluha' (insanity is like it).

Source Text

Fidyah for Missed Prayers and Fasts of the Deceased: Ruling and Amount
Ruling with proof for fidyah amount and basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for missed prayers and fasts of the deceased, identify the amount, and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Feeding is the only valid substitute for missed fasts and prayers of the deceased – each day or prayer requires half a sa' of food.

This lesson covers the core Hanafi ruling that when a person dies with missed obligatory fasts or prayers, the only valid compensation is fidyah – feeding the poor. The proof is a specific hadith, and the amounts are detailed. We will also see the istihsan applied by the later mashayikh to extend the ruling from fasts to prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Missed fasts and prayers of the deceased: ruling that fidyah is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'من مات وعليه صوم شهر فليطعم عنه مكان كل يوم مسكين' and the parallel for prayers via istihsan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليطعم' indicates obligation; the hadith is ahad, so the hukm is wajib not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi: some said fidyah for one day's prayers equals fidyah for one day's fast; correct view is each prayer has its own fidyah.
5
Determine the amount and optional value
Half sa' of wheat or equivalent; giving value is better.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكفارات المالية كالدماء التي تلزمه بجنايته على إحرامه مثل تطيبه ولبسه بغير عذر. والوصية بالحج والصدقة المنذورة والاعتكاف المنذور عن صومه لا عن اللبث في المسجد. وقد لزمه وهو صحيح ولم يعتكف حتى أشرف على الموت كان عليه يوصي لصوم اعتكاف كل يوم بنصف صاع من ثلث ما له. وإن كان مريضاً وقت الإيجاب ولم يبرأ حتى مات فلا شيء عليه. فإذا لم يف به الثلث توقف الزائد على إجازة الوارث فيعطي الصوم كل يوم طعام مسكين لقوله عليه السلام: «من مات وعليه صوم شهر فليطعم عنه مكان كل يوم مسكين». وكذا يخرج الصلاة كل وقت من فرض اليوم والليلة حتى الوتر لأنه فرض عملي عند الإمام وقد ورد النص في الصوم والصلاة كالصيام باستحسان المشايخ لكونها أهم واعتبار كل صلاة بصوم يوم هو الصحيح. وقيل: فدية صلاة اليوم الواحد كفدية صوم يوم. والصحيح أنه لكل صلاة فدية هي نصف صاع من بر أو دقيقة أو سويقة أو صاع تمر أو زبيب أو شعير أو قيمته وهي أفضل لتنوع حاجات الفقير. وإن لم يوص وتبرع عنه وليه أو أجنبي جاز إن شاء الله تعالى لأن محمداً قال في تبرع الوارث بالإطعام في الصوم: يجزيه إن شاء الله تعالى من غير جزم، وفي إيصائه به جزم بالأجزاء. وإذا تبرع أحد بالاعتاق عنه لا يصح لما فيه من إلزام الولاء على الميت بغير رضاه بخلاف وصيته به. وفي الوصية بالحج يحج من منزله من ثلث ماله والمتبرع به من حيث شاء سواء الوارث وغيره. ولا يصح أن يصوم الولي ولا غيره عن الميت ولا أن يصلي أحد عنه لقوله عليه السلام: «لا يصوم أحد عن أحد ولا يصلي أحد عن أحد ولكن يطعم عنه». وما ورد من قوله: «صومي عن أمك» وقوله: «من مات وعليه صيام صام عنه وليه» فمنسوخ كذا في البرهان وغيره. فما يفعله جهلة الناس الآن من إعطاء دراهم لصومه ليس بشيء وإنما الله سبحانه وتعالى يتجاوز عن الميت بواسطة الصدقة التي قدرها الشارع كما بيناه وإن قلنا بأن للعبد أن يجعل ثواب طاعته لغيره فهو غير هذا الحكم فليتنبه له.
And the financial expiations like the blood (offerings) that become obligatory due to his violation of his ihram such as applying perfume and wearing (sewn clothes) without excuse. And the will for Hajj and vowed charity and vowed i'tikaf concerning its fast, not concerning staying in the mosque. And it became obligatory upon him while he was healthy, and he did not perform i'tikaf until he was near death, then he must will for the fast of i'tikaf for each day half a sa' from one third of his wealth. And if he was sick at the time of obligation and did not recover until he died, then nothing is upon him. If one third does not cover it, the surplus is suspended on the permission of the heir, and he gives for each day's fast food of a poor person due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever dies and has upon him a month of fasting, let him feed on his behalf for each day a poor person.' And similarly, he gives for prayer every time of obligatory prayer of the day and night, including witr, because it is a practical obligation according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), and the text has come regarding fasting and prayer like fasting by the istihsan of the mashayikh because they are more important. And considering each prayer like a day's fast is the correct view. And it was said: the fidyah for one day's prayers is like the fidyah for one day's fast. And the correct view is that for each prayer there is a fidyah, which is half a sa' of wheat, or (flour of) ground wheat, or gruel, or a sa' of dates, or raisins, or barley, or its value – and that is better due to the diversity of the poor person's needs. And if he did not will, and his guardian or a stranger donated on his behalf, it is permissible, if Allah wills, because Muhammad said regarding the donation of the heir by feeding in fasting: it suffices, if Allah wills, without certainty; and in his willing it, there is certainty of suffocation. And if someone donates by manumitting on his behalf, it is not valid because it involves imposing wala' on the deceased without his consent, unlike his will for it. And in the will for Hajj, he performs Hajj from his residence if it suffices, otherwise from where it suffices, and the one who donates it performs it from wherever he wishes, whether heir or other. And it is not valid for the guardian or anyone else to fast on behalf of the deceased, nor for anyone to pray on his behalf, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'No one fasts on behalf of anyone, and no one prays on behalf of anyone, but he feeds on his behalf.' And what has come of his statement: 'Fast on behalf of your mother' and his statement: 'Whoever dies and has fasting upon him, his guardian should fast on his behalf' is abrogated – thus in al-Burhan and others. So what ignorant people do nowadays of giving dirhams for his fasting is nothing; rather Allah Almighty overlooks the deceased through the charity that the Lawgiver has specified as we explained. And even if we say that a servant can assign the reward of his obedience to someone else, this is different from this ruling; so let one pay attention to this.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah deals with the rulings on various obligations that may be owed by a deceased person and how they are to be discharged. The passage type is a ruling with proof. The author first discusses financial expiations (kaffarat maliyyah) such as those due for violations of ihram. Then he moves to wills for Hajj, vowed charity, and vowed i'tikaf – specifically the fast of i'tikaf, not the staying in the mosque. For a person who was healthy when the fast of i'tikaf became obligatory but did not fulfill it until near death, he must will that for each day of missed i'tikaf fast, half a sa' of food be given from one-third of his wealth. If he was sick at the time of the vow and died without recovering, nothing is due. If the one-third does not cover all days, the excess depends on the heirs' permission. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever dies and owes a month of fasting, let food be given on his behalf for each day to a poor person.' This ruling extends to prayers as well: for every missed obligatory prayer of the day and night, including witr, one must give half a sa' of wheat or its equivalent, or a sa' of dates, raisins, or barley, or its value. The preferred view is to give the value because it suits the diverse needs of the poor. If the deceased did not will, and his guardian or a stranger donates the food on his behalf, it is permissible but conditional on Allah's will – meaning it is not certain to be accepted. However, if the deceased himself willed it, then there is certainty. Manumission on behalf of the deceased is not valid because it imposes clientage (wala') without consent. The author then emphasizes a crucial point: it is not valid for anyone to fast or pray on behalf of the deceased. The hadiths that seem to allow it, such as 'Fast on behalf of your mother' and 'Whoever dies and owes fasting, his guardian should fast on his behalf,' are abrogated. Therefore, the only valid method is feeding (fidyah). Even if one believes that the reward of one's good deeds can be transferred to others, that is a different matter; the specific legal ruling for missed prayers and fasts of the deceased is feeding, not direct performance. The author warns against the common practice of giving money in exchange for someone else's fasting, stating that it is nothing.

Key Terms
فدية (fidyah): Compensation paid in the form of food or money for missed religious obligations (fasts, prayers) that cannot be made up by the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the amount of fidyah for each missed prayer of the deceased?
A) Same as fidyah for one missed fast day, i.e., half a sa' of wheat
B) One fourth of a sa'
C) One sa' of wheat
D) No fidyah, prayers can be performed on behalf

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires fidyah (feeding) for each missed obligatory prayer and fast of the deceased, at half a sa' per unit, based on hadith and istihsan.

Salah — Prayer

Prohibition of Fasting and Praying on Behalf of the Deceased and the Abrogation of Permissive Hadiths
Ruling with proof and abrogation discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that fasting or praying for the deceased is invalid, identify the abrogated hadiths, and explain the correct method (fidyah).

Core Idea
No one may fast or pray for the deceased; only feeding is valid. Permissive hadiths are abrogated.

A common question is whether one can perform acts of worship on behalf of a deceased person. This lesson addresses the Hanafi position: it is not valid to fast or pray for the deceased. The evidence is a clear hadith prohibiting it, and any hadith suggesting otherwise is abrogated. The only valid substitute is fidyah (feeding), as established in the previous lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Fasting and praying on behalf of the deceased: invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
Hadith: 'لا يصوم أحد عن أحد ولا يصلي أحد عن أحد ولكن يطعم عنه'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation indicates prohibition; the alternative 'يطعم' indicates the valid method.
4
Identify the naskh
The apparent permissive hadiths (e.g., 'صومي عن أمك', 'صام عنه وليه') are abrogated.
5
Address the common error
Ignorant practice of giving money for someone to fast is invalid; only charity as specified works.

Legal Device (Hila) to Discharge Deceased's Obligations
Procedure for a legal stratagem to exonerate the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the sequence of the Hanafi hila for discharging multiple obligations of the deceased and identify the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
A small gift can be cycled through repeated transfers to exonerate all a deceased's obligations.

When a deceased person has many missed prayers or fasts and insufficient funds to pay fidyah for all, the Hanafi school provides a practical legal stratagem (hila). This device uses a small amount of wealth in a cycle of giving, re-gifting, and re-giving, each time with a fresh intention. Understanding this hila clarifies how Hanafi law creatively uses valid contracts to fulfill obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying problem
Recognize that the deceased owes multiple missed prayers and fasts, but the available wealth (whether from a will or donation) is insufficient to pay fidyah for each one separately.
2
Understand the core mechanism
The hila uses a single small amount that is given to a poor person, then gifted back to the guardian or agent, then given again to the poor person, repeating the cycle until each obligation is considered discharged.
Each transfer must involve actual possession (qabd) and a distinct intention.
3
Trace the legal steps
Follow the sequence: (1) donor gives fidyah to poor person intending to drop one obligation; (2) poor person gifts it back to guardian; (3) guardian gives it again to poor person for next obligation; repeat.
The donor can be the guardian or any person acting on behalf of the deceased.
4
Note the Hanafi reliance on intention and ownership
Each transfer establishes a new ownership and a separate intention, making the cycle permissible despite the same item being reused.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that gifts and intentions are renewed with each transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يف ما أوصى به الميت عما عليه أو لم يكف ثلث ما له أو لم يوص بشيء وأراد أحد التبرع بقليل لا يكفي فحيلته لإبراء ذمة الميت عن جميع ما عليه أن يدفع ذلك المقدار اليسير بعد تقديره لشيء من صيام أو صلاة أو نحوه ويعطيه للفقير بقصد إسقاط ما يرد عن الميت فيسقط عن الميت بقدره ثم بعد قبضه يهبه الفقير للولي أو للأجنبي ويقبضه لتتم الهبة وتملك ثم يدفعه الموهوب له للفقير بجهة الإسقاط متبرعاً به عن الميت فيسقط عن الميت بقدره أيضاً ثم يهبه الفقير للولي أو للأجنبي ويقبضه ثم يدفعه الولي للفقير متبرعاً عن الميت وهكذا يفعل مراراً حتى يسقط ما كان على الميت من صلاة وصيام ونحوهما مما ذكرناه من الواجبات. وهذا هو المخلص في ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى بمنه وكرمه. ويجوز إعطاء فدية صلوات وصيام أيام ونحوها.
And if what the deceased willed does not cover what is upon him, or one third of his wealth does not suffice, or he did not will anything, and someone wants to donate a little that does not suffice, then the legal device (hila) to exonerate the deceased's liability from all that is upon him is that he gives that small amount after estimating it for something of fasting or prayer or the like, and gives it to the poor person with the intention of dropping what is due from the deceased, so it drops from the deceased to its extent. Then after the poor person takes it, the poor person gifts it to the guardian or a stranger, and he takes it so that the gift is completed and ownership is established. Then the donee gives it to the poor person with the intention of dropping (the obligation) as a donation on behalf of the deceased, so it drops from the deceased to its extent as well. Then the poor person gifts it to the guardian or stranger, and he takes it, then the guardian gives it to the poor person as a donation on behalf of the deceased. And thus he does repeatedly until what was upon the deceased of prayers, fasts, and the like from the obligations we have mentioned drops. And this is the way out in that, Allah willing, by His favor and generosity. And it is permissible to give fidyah for prayers and fasts of days and the like.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage provides a legal device (hila) for discharging multiple religious obligations owed by a deceased person when there is insufficient wealth or will. The situation arises when a person has many missed prayers or fasts, and the funds available (whether through a will or donation) are not enough to cover all of them. The device works by using a small amount of wealth repeatedly in a cycle. One estimates the number of obligations and the fidyah for each. A small amount (e.g., half a sa' of wheat) is given to a poor person with the intention of dropping one obligation. The poor person then receives it and gifts it back to the guardian (or any person acting on behalf of the deceased). The guardian then gives it again to the same or another poor person, again intending to drop another obligation. This cycle is repeated until all obligations are deemed dropped. The device relies on the legal principle that ownership is transferred each time and the intention can be renewed. The text emphasizes that this is the way out (al-mukhlis) and hopes for Allah's acceptance. This hila is specific to the Hanafi school and shows the importance of legal stratagems (hiyal) in facilitating worship obligations. The commentary after adds details: the duration of childhood (12 years for boys, 9 for girls) can be estimated and excluded, and the need for actual hand-to-hand transfer (qabd) each time is essential.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem or device that achieves a legitimate result (here, exoneration of the deceased) by using permissible transactions in a sequence.
إبراء ذمة (ibra' dhimmah): Exoneration or discharge of liability – the deceased's moral and legal obligation is considered fulfilled through the hila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi hila for discharging multiple obligations of the deceased, after the poor person receives the fidyah, what must happen next?
A) The poor person keeps it permanently.
B) The poor person gifts it back to the guardian.
C) The guardian immediately gives it to another poor person.
D) The money is spent on the deceased's family.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila permits a single small amount of fidyah to be cycled through valid gift contracts to exonerate the deceased from multiple missed religious obligations.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Legal Trick (Hila) for Discharging the Deceased's Obligations
Presents a hila to discharge missed prayers/fasts of deceased via repeated giving and taking back.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi hila for discharging the deceased's missed prayers and fasts, and identify its conditions, mechanism, and validity according to the later Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Through a repeated gift and return, the deceased's obligations can be discharged – a Hanafi concession when the estate is insufficient.

This passage addresses a common practical problem: what to do when a deceased person has missed prayers and fasts, and the estate is insufficient to pay fidya for all of them. The Hanafi school provides a legal trick (hila) that uses a repeated cycle of giving and receiving to effectively discharge the obligations. This lesson unpacks the proof for the general prohibition (no one can fast or pray for another) and then explains the precise mechanism of the hila, its conditions, and its validity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the General Ruling
Identify the main rule: it is not valid for anyone to fast or pray on behalf of the deceased. Cite the hadith proof and note that the contradictory command was abrogated.
This is the background that creates the need for an alternative method.
2
Recognize the Problem of Insufficient Estate
When the estate is insufficient or the deceased made no will, a voluntary payment may not cover all obligations. The hila is introduced as a solution.
The hila is not needed if the estate fully covers the fidya.
3
Trace the Hila’s Mechanism
Follow the steps: (1) Guardian gives apportioned amount to a poor person as fidya. (2) Poor person gifts it back to guardian (or a third party). (3) Guardian takes possession and gives it again to the poor person as fidya for another obligation. Repeat until all obligations are discharged.
Each cycle requires actual possession (qabd) to make the gift valid.
4
Note the Conditions for Validity
The hila requires: genuine intention to discharge, proper apportioning of amount per missed act, repeated delivery and possession, and that the poor person does not abscond with the money after the first gift.
If the poor person refuses to gift back, the hila fails.
5
Distinguish from Common Mispractice
The text criticizes the common practice of simply giving money without the gift-back cycle. Only the specified hila is effective.
The hila is a concession from later Hanafi scholars, not found in earlier works.

In the will for Hajj, he performs Hajj from his home from one-third of his wealth, and the volunteer performs it from wherever he wishes, whether heir or other. It is not valid for the guardian or anyone else to fast for the deceased, nor for anyone to pray for him, because of his statement: 'It is not valid for anyone to fast for another, nor to pray for another, but he should feed on his behalf.' (If what the deceased willed does not suffice for what is due upon him, or one-third of his wealth is insufficient, or he did not will anything, and someone wants to volunteer a small amount that is insufficient, then the hila to discharge the deceased's liability for all that is upon him is to pay that small amount after apportioning it for something of fasting or prayer or the like, and give it to the poor person with the intention of discharging what is due from the deceased, so it is discharged from the deceased to its extent. Then after the poor person takes possession, he gifts it to the guardian or to a stranger, and he takes possession to complete the gift and ownership. Then the donee gives it to the poor person as a voluntary discharge on behalf of the deceased, so it is discharged from the deceased to its extent again. Then the poor person gifts it to the guardian or to a stranger, and he takes possession, then the guardian gives it to the poor person as a voluntary discharge on behalf of the deceased. This is done repeatedly until all that is assumed upon the deceased of prayers, fasts, and similar obligations we mentioned is discharged. This is the way out in that, Allah willing, by His grace and generosity. It is permissible to give the commutation (fidya) of prayers and fasts of days and the like (to a single poor person) all at once, unlike the kaffarah of the oath where it is not permissible to give more than half a sa' to one person in a day due to the text specifying the number therein. Similarly, whatever number is specified in kaffarah. (And Allah the Exalted knows best) and He is the Grantor of success by His grace and generosity.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
The passage begins with a ruling: the guardian or anyone else cannot fast or pray on behalf of the deceased. The proof is the hadith: 'It is not valid for anyone to fast for another...' The hadith commanding fasting for the deceased is abrogated. Then it discusses the hila (legal trick) for discharging the deceased's obligations when the estate is insufficient. The method: a small amount is given to a poor person as fidya (commutation) for a specific missed prayer or fast. The poor person then gifts it back to the guardian, who takes possession, then gives it again to the poor person for another day's obligation, repeating until all obligations are discharged. This works because each time the poor person owns the money and gifts it back. The text also permits giving fidya for multiple prayers or fasts to one poor person at once, unlike kaffarah where distribution to multiple recipients is required due to the text specifying number. The commentary notes that the lifespan should be estimated, excluding childhood, and that repeated transfers are necessary. If the poor person absconds with the money after the first gift, the hila fails.

Key Terms
هبة (hiba): A gift transferring ownership of property from one person to another without compensation, requiring offer, acceptance, and possession (qabd).
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive taking possession of the gifted item, necessary for completion of the hiba.
فدية (fidya): A monetary compensation given for missed religious obligations such as prayers or fasts that cannot be made up; in this context, an amount apportioned to a missed day.
إسقاط (isqāt): The legal discharge or dropping of an obligation; here, the removal of the deceased's liability for missed prayers/fasts through fidya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for the hila to effectively discharge the deceased's missed prayers?
A) The money must be given as a gift to the poor, who then gives it back, and this is repeated.
B) The guardian must directly pray and fast for the deceased.
C) The money must be given to multiple poor people at once.
D) The amount must be at least one-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila allows discharging the deceased's obligations through repeated fidya and gift, but only when the direct gift-back method is followed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Definition of Qada and Its Rulings
Defines qada linguistically and legally, distinguishing ada, qada, and i'ada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ada, qada, and i'ada, and state the Hanafi ruling on qada and i'ada.

Core Idea
Qada is the same obligation as the original, performed after time; delaying a prayer is a separate sin not expiated by qada.

This lesson opens the chapter on making up missed prayers by defining the key terms: ada (performance in time), qada (making up after time), and i'ada (repetition within time due to a defect). The Hanafi position is that qada is the same obligation deferred, not a new obligation. We also explore the ruling that qada removes the sin of non-performance but not the sin of delay—a critical distinction for proper spiritual accountability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Categories
From the passage, list the three types of commanded acts: ada, qada, and i'ada. Note their definitions and how they relate to time and obligation.
2
Define Qada Linguistically and Legally
Linguistically, qada means 'judgment' (al-hukm). Legally, it is 'discharging the obligatory with its like when it is available'—i.e., performing the missed act after its time.
The legal definition implies the act is identical to the original obligation, not just similar.
3
Understand the Hanafi Position on the Nature of Qada
The preponderant view (rajih) is that qada becomes obligatory by the same cause as ada. Both are the submission of the same wajib, differing only in timing. An alternative view (qada as new obligation) exists but has no practical effect.
This distinction is theoretical; the ruling that qada is fard remains unchanged.
4
Distinguish the Sins: Delay vs. Non-Performance
Delay without excuse is a major sin (kabira) that qada does not remove. Qada only removes the sin of leaving the prayer entirely. Removing the delay sin requires repentance (tawba) or Hajj.
This is a critical point for practical fiqh and spiritual self-assessment.
5
Apply the Ruling of I'ada
I'ada is defined as repeating an act within its time due to a defect less than invalidity (e.g., karahah tahrim). In the Hanafi school, i'ada is wajib within the time if the first act was valid but disliked; after the time it becomes mandub.
This differs from Shafi'i view where i'ada is never wajib unless the first was batil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت القضاء لغة الأحكام وشريعة إسقاط الواجب بمثل ما عنده الترتيب بين الفائتة القليلة قوله : (وكذا ما نص على عدده في كفارة ككفارة الظهار على ما ذكره، فإن الله تعالى قال : فمن لم يستطع فإطعام ستين مسكينا ) وهل تكفي الإباحة في الفدية قولان المشهور نعم واعتمده الكمال ولو فدى عن صلاته في مرضه لا يصح بخلاف الصوم، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. باب قضاء الفوانت لم يقل المتروكات ظناً بالمؤمنين خيراً لأن ظاهر حال المسلم أن لا يترك الصلاة وإنما تفوته من غير قصد لعذر واعلم أن المأمور به ثلاثة أقسام أداء وقضاء، وإعادة والأداء أنواع كامل كالصلاة بجماعة، وقاصر كالصلاة منفرداً لفوات الوصف المرغوب فيه، وأداء شبيه بالقضاء، وهو فعل اللاحق بعد فراغ الإمام أما أنه أداء فلبقاء الوقت، وأما أنه شبيه بالقضاء فلأنه قد التزمه مع الإمام وقد فاته ذلك الملتزم، ولما فرغ المصنف من الأداء بأنواعه شرع في القضاء قوله : (القضاء لغة (الأحكام لقضا بالقصر، والمد، وقوله الأحكام الأولى أن يقول الحكم قوله: (إسقاط الواجب بمثل ما عنده اعلم أن القضاء وجب بالسبب الذي وجب به الأداء فكل من الأداء والقضاء تسليم عين الواجب إلا أن الأداء تسليم عين الواجب في وقته والقضاء تسليم عين الواجب بعد خروج الوقت، وهذا هو الراجح وقيل : يجب القضاء بسبب جديد، وإن المؤدى مثل الواجب وليس لهذا الخلاف ثمرة إذا علمت هذا تعلم أن قوله بمثل ما عنده جرى على غير الراجح والتأخير بلا عذر كبيرة لا تزول بالقضاء بل بالتوبة أو الحج فالقضاء مزيل لإثم الترك لا لإثم التأخير، والإعادة فعل مثله في وقته لخلل غير الفساد لقولهم، كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم تعاد أي وجوباً في الوقت وأما بعده فندباً وقوله إسقاط الواجب يفيد أن السنة لا توصف بالقضاء وإذا أريد ما هو أعم أبدلنا الواجب بالعبادة فيقال : الأداء فعل العبادة في وقتها والإعادة فعل مثلها لخلل غير الفساد، وغير عدم صحة الشروع والقضاء فعلها بعد وقتها فتكون السنة التي تفعل في وقتها إداء وما أذن الشارع في فعله منها في غير وقته قضاء كسنة الفجر وأما سنة الظهر القبلية إذا صليت بعد فإطلاق القضاء عليها مجاز

And are the mubah (permissibility) sufficient in fidya? Two sayings: the famous is yes, and al-Kamal adopted it. If he gives fidya for his prayer during his illness, it is not valid, unlike the fast. And Allah knows best, and I seek Allah's forgiveness. Chapter on Making Up Missed (Prayers). Know that the commanded is of three types: ada (performance), qada (making up), and i'ada (repetition). Ada types: perfect like prayer in congregation, deficient like prayer alone due to lack of the desired description, and ada similar to qada: it is the act of the latecomer after the imam finishes. It is ada because the time remains, and it is similar to qada because he had committed to the imam and missed that commitment. When the author finished the ada types, he began with qada. His saying: (Qada linguistically: judgments; qada with shortening and lengthening. And his saying 'al-ahkam' - it would be better to say 'al-hukm'. His saying: (Legally: discharging the obligatory with its like when it is available). Know that qada became obligatory by the same cause that made ada obligatory. So both ada and qada are the submission of the identical obligatory, except that ada is the submission of the identical obligatory in its time, and qada is the submission of the identical obligatory after the time has exited. This is the preponderant view. It is said that qada is obligatory due to a new cause, and that the performed act is like the obligatory, but this difference has no practical consequence. When you know this, you know that his saying 'with its like when it is available' follows the non-preponderant view. Delay without excuse is a major sin that is not removed by qada but only by repentance or Hajj. So qada removes the sin of leaving (the act) but not the sin of delay. I'ada is performing its like in its time due to a defect other than invalidity, as they said: every prayer performed with karahah tahrim (disliked prohibition) is repeated, i.e., obligatorily within the time, and after the time it is recommended. And his saying 'discharging the obligatory' indicates that the sunna is not described by qada. If a more general meaning is intended, we replace 'obligatory' with 'act of worship'. So it is said: Ada is the performance of the act of worship in its time, i'ada is the performance of its like due to a defect other than invalidity and other than lack of valid commencement, and qada is performance after its time. Thus the sunna that is performed in its time is ada, and what the Lawgiver has permitted of it outside its time is qada, like the sunna of Fajr. As for the pre-noon sunna of Zuhr if prayed after, calling it qada is metaphorical.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers. It begins with linguistic and legal definitions of qada: linguistically 'judgments', legally 'discharging an obligation with its like when it is available'. The author discusses the order of making up few missed prayers later. Then follows a long commentary on the definition. The preferred view is that qada becomes obligatory by the same cause that made the original ada obligatory; both are submission of the exact same obligation, but ada is in time and qada after time. There is an alternative view that qada is a new obligation, but it has no practical effect. Delaying a prayer without excuse is a major sin that qada does not remove; only repentance or Hajj can do that. The term 'i'ada' is defined as repeating the act in its time due to a defect less than invalidity, which is obligatory in time and recommended after time. The commentary clarifies that voluntary sunna prayers are not described as qada unless specifically permitted by the Lawgiver after their time, like the sunna of Fajr. For other sunan, applying qada is metaphorical.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā): Linguistically: judgment (al-hukm). In shari'a: performing a missed obligatory act of worship after its time has exited.
أداء (adā'): Performing an act of worship within its prescribed time.
إعادة (i'āda): Repeating an act of worship in its time due to a defect that does not invalidate the original (e.g., karahah tahrim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ada is for fard, qada is for sunna.
C) Ada is with congregation, qada is alone.
D) Ada requires intention, qada does not.

Key Takeaway
Qada is the same obligation performed after time; it does not remove the sin of delaying, which requires separate repentance.

Salah — Prayer

Tartīb (Order) for Missed Prayers: Ruling and Conditions
Explains obligatory order between missed and current prayers and when it drops.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartīb between missed and current prayers, cite the primary proof, and identify the three situations in which the obligation drops.

Core Idea
Tartīb binds for few missed prayers with ample time, but drops when time is tight or missed prayers exceed five.

When you remember a missed prayer while the current prayer's time is still open, must you pray the missed one first? The Hanafi school says yes—this order (tartīb) is a practical obligation. But there are clear exceptions. Let's examine the proof and the conditions that lift this requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Tartīb (order) applies in two scenarios: between a current prayer and a remembered missed prayer, and among the missed prayers themselves. The ruling: it is binding (lāzim) as a practical fard (farḍ ‘amalī).
2
Analyze the primary dalil
The hadith about the man who remembers a missed prayer while praying with the imam contains imperatives ('let him pray', 'then let him make up') indicating obligation. The word 'thum' (then) implies sequence.
This hadith is classified as khabar mashhūr, accepted by the scholars for practical obligations.
3
Identify the authority weight
The hadith is mashhūr, which is zannī al-thubūt and zannī al-dalāla. It establishes a practical fard, not a belief matter.
Hanafī usūl: khabar mashhūr binds in amal (practice) but not in 'aqīdah.
4
Note the exceptions
The obligation drops in three cases: (1) narrowness of time that cannot accommodate all prayers, (2) forgetfulness, (3) when the missed prayers number six or more.
Only the first exception is detailed here; the other two are mentioned elsewhere in the text (implied by 'less than six').
5
Evaluate the tarjīh
Although some early Hanafīs considered tartīb as sunnah, the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is that it is wājib / practical farḍ. The commentator affirms this based on the hadīth and scholarly acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي ما دون ست صلوات (و) بين (الوقتية) المتسع وقتها مع تذكر الفائتة لازم (و) كذا الترتيب (بين) نفس (الفوائت) القليلة (مستحق) أي لازم لأنه فرض عملي يفوت الجواز بفوته، والأصل في لزوم الترتيب قوله : من نام عن صلاة أن نسبها فلم يذكرها إلا وهو يصلي مع الإمام فليصل التي هو فيها ثم ليقض التي تذكر ثم ليعد التي صلى مع الإمام وهو خبر مشهور تلقته العلماء بالقبول فيثبت به الفرض العملي ورتب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضاء الفوائت يوم الخندق (ويسقط) الترتيب بأحد ثلاثة أشياء) الأول (ضيق الوقت) عن كل الفوائت وأداء الحاضرة للزوم العمل بالمتواتر حينئذ لأن العمل بالمشهور يستلزم إبطال
And they (the few missed prayers) are what is less than six prayers. And between the current prayer whose time is expansive with remembrance of the missed prayer, it is binding. And likewise the order between the few missed prayers themselves is binding, because it is a practical fard whose permissibility is lost by its loss. The basis for the necessity of order is his saying: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, and only remembers it while praying with an imam, let him pray the one he is in, then make up the one he remembered, then repeat the one he prayed with the imam.' This is a well-known hadith (mashhur) which the scholars accepted, so a practical fard is established by it. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) arranged the making up of missed prayers on the day of the Trench. The order is dropped by one of three things: the first: narrowness of time for all the missed prayers and performing the present prayer, because it is necessary to act on the mutawatir at that time, since acting on the mashhur would necessitate nullifying...
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of tartīb (order/sequence) when making up missed prayers and praying the current (present) prayer. The commentator explains that the order is binding (lāzim) in two situations: (1) between the current prayer (with expansive time) and a missed prayer that one remembers, and (2) between the missed prayers themselves, provided they are 'few' (less than six). The ruling is described as 'mustahaqq' (binding) because it is a practical fard (farḍ ‘amalī)—its omission makes the prayer impermissible (fawt al-jawāz). The proof: the famous hadith of the person who missed a prayer and remembers during the current congregational prayer—he should complete the current prayer, then make up the missed one, then repeat the one with the imam. This hadith is mashhur (well-known) and accepted by scholars, thus establishing a practical fard. Additional evidence: the Prophet's own practice on the Day of al-Khandaq (the Trench) where he made up prayers in order. Then the commentator lists three situations that drop the obligation of tartīb. Only the first is given here: narrowness of time (ḍīq al-waqt) that cannot accommodate both the missed prayers and the current prayer. In that case, one acts on the mutawātir (the clearly established proofs for the present prayer's obligation) rather than the mashhur (the hadith on tartīb), to avoid nullifying the current prayer's obligation.

Key Terms
فرض عملي (farḍ ‘amalī): A ruling that is considered fard (obligatory) from a practical perspective, not from belief (i‘tiqādī); its omission affects the permissibility (jawāz) of the act.
خبر مشهور (khabar mashhūr): A hadith transmitted in the first two generations by more than two but not reaching tawātur; accepted by the scholars and considered binding in practical matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tartīb (order) between a current prayer with expansive time and a remembered missed prayer?
A) It is recommended (sunnah)
B) It is binding (lāzim) as a practical fard
C) It is not required
D) It is obligatory only if the missed prayer is the same type

Key Takeaway
Tartīb is a practical obligation that binds when missed prayers are few and time permits, but it drops when time is narrow or the number of missed prayers is six or more.

Obligation of Order Between Missed and Time-Bound Prayers
Establishes obligation of order and its exception when time is tight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of order (tartib) between a missed prayer and the current time-bound prayer, identify the proof, and explain when the order drops according to the mufta bihi (Muhammad’s view).

Core Idea
Order between a missed prayer and the time-bound prayer is obligatory when time is ample; when time is tight, the time-bound prayer takes precedence.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi establishes the ruling of order (tartib) in making up missed prayers. It clarifies that the order is a practical obligation (mustahaqq) derived from a mashhur hadith and the Prophet's practice at the Battle of the Trench. The text also details the conditions under which the order drops, particularly when the time for the current prayer is tight, including an intra-Hanafi disagreement resolved by the later preponderant view of Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the order between a missed prayer and the time-bound prayer (or between missed prayers themselves).
The act is the sequence: which prayer to pray first.
2
Classify the ruling level (mustahaqq) and why
Understand why the author uses 'mustahaqq' instead of fard or wajib: it is a practical obligation whose omission invalidates the prayer, but based on zanni evidence.
This is a key Hanafi fiqh nuance.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
Examine the hadith cited and the Prophet’s action at Khandaq. Note its authority (mashhur) and how it yields obligation via al-amr.
The hadith is zanni in transmission, so the ruling is not absolute fard.
4
Explore the exception and the intra-Hanafi dispute
The order drops when the time for the current prayer is tight. The dispute is whether 'tight' means the original time or the preferred time. Identify the positions and the preponderant view.
This is a critical refinement of the ruling.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
In practice, use Muhammad’s criterion: if performing the missed prayer would push the current prayer into the disliked time, the order drops; otherwise, it remains.
The mufta bihi is from al-Muhit and al-Zahiriyya.

And it [prayer] is less than six prayers and between the time-bound prayer whose time is ample while remembering the missed prayer, it is necessary. And likewise, order between few missed prayers themselves is obligatory. It is a practical obligation whose validity is lost by its omission. The basis for the obligation of order is his saying: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it and does not remember it except while praying with the Imam, let him pray the one he is in, then let him make up the one he remembered, then let him repeat the one he prayed with the Imam.' And it is a well-known hadith accepted by scholars, so a practical obligation is established by it. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) arranged the making up of missed prayers on the day of the trench. And the order is dropped by one of three things: first, the time being too tight to perform all the missed prayers and the present prayer, because then acting on the mutawatir is necessary, since acting on the well-known would necessitate invalidating the definitive, and it is not acted upon except when combination is possible with ample time. And it is not wisdom to waste the present in seeking the absent when time is tight. The order is dropped due to tight time even of the preferred time, because observing the order would cause the present prayer to be performed deficiently, thereby changing the ruling of the Book. So the order is dropped due to tight time even of the preferred time, and it does not return after its exit in the soundest view. Its example: if one occupied himself with making up Zuhr, then Asr or part of it falls in the time of deficiency, then the order is dropped in the soundest view. And consideration is given to tightness at the commencement. So if he began the time-bound prayer remembering the missed one, then when... because the end of time for the time-bound prayer is established by mutawatir reports and texts, and the time of remembrance for the missed prayer is established by the previous hadith. For in some of its narrations: 'that is its time.' And it indicates the obligation of order, and it is described as a solitary hadith, and it is only obligatory to act upon it if it does not entail abandoning action on the text. But if it does, then it would involve abrogating the Book by it, and that is not permissible. Similarly in the commentary. His statement: 'at that time' means when time is tight. His statement: 'and it is not acted upon' means the well-known, which is the previous hadith. It negates the obligation of order. His statement: 'with ample time' – the ba is for causation, and in a copy: 'with'. His statement: 'by tight time' is linked to his statement: 'waste', and the ba is for causation. And if he advanced the missed prayer, and it was not a time of dislike, it is valid, but he sins for wasting the time-bound prayer without justification, so it becomes like if he occupied himself with supererogatory prayer when time is tight. Contrary to when time is ample, and he advanced the time-bound prayer, then it is not valid because he performed it before its time established by the hadith while combination is possible. His statement: 'the preferred time' – this is not mentioned in the apparent narration, so there was disagreement among the mashayikh. Al-Tahawi attributed consideration of the original time to both (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and consideration of the preferred time to Muhammad. And in al-Muhit, Muhammad's view is preponderated, and also in al-Zahiriyyah based on al-Muntaqa: that if one began Asr in its early time while forgetting Zuhr, then the sun became red, then he remembered Zuhr, he continues in Asr. He said: this is textual evidence that the consideration is for the preferred time. At that point, the disagreement of the mashayikh ended because the issue was not mentioned in the apparent narration, and it is established in another narration, so it is necessary to adopt it. And the fruit of the disagreement appears in the case where one began Asr while forgetting Zuhr, then remembered it at a time that if he occupied himself with it, Asr would fall in the disliked time. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), he breaks Asr and prays Zuhr; according to him (Muhammad), he continues in Asr and then prays Zuhr after sunset. Al-Sayyid mentioned this fruit from Miskin. His statement: 'it changes the ruling of the Book' – and it is His statement: 'Indeed, prayer has been a decree upon the believers at fixed times' and changing the ruling of the Book by diminishing the time-bound prayer by placing it in the disliked time. Similarly in the commentary. For the mentioned verse, like His statement: 'Establish prayer', indicates coming with the obligation in a perfect manner because it is legally required. And the interpretation of tight time is that the remaining time is insufficient for both the time-bound prayer and the missed prayer in reality, not according to his assumption. So if the one who has Isha thinks that the time of Fajr is tight and prays Fajr, then it becomes clear that time was ample, then Fajr is invalid. Then he looks: if the time can accommodate both such that he sits in Fajr for the amount of tashahhud before sunrise after Isha prayer, then he prays Isha and then repeats Fajr. And if there is not that capacity, he repeats only Fajr. And so he does, time and again.
Source pages p. 441

Key Terms
مستحق (mustahaqq): A legal term meaning 'obligatory' but in a sense that it is a practical obligation whose omission affects validity, without being a definitive fard or a mere wajib.
الفائتة (al-fa'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that must be made up (qada).
الوقتية (al-waqtiyyah): The current time-bound obligatory prayer (e.g., the prayer whose time has entered).
الوقت المستحب (al-waqt al-mustahab): The preferred time for prayer, i.e., the early part of the time, as opposed to the time of dislike (makruh) or the entire legal time.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are considered the primary and most authoritative narrations of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, when does the obligation of order (tartib) between a missed prayer and the current time-bound prayer drop due to time pressure?
A) When the current prayer's original time ends
B) When the current prayer's preferred time has passed
C) When the current prayer's entire time ends
D) When the missed prayer's time ends

Key Takeaway
The obligation of order (tartib) in making up prayers is a mustahaqq that drops when the current prayer's preferred time would be missed, ensuring the time-bound prayer is performed in its best time.
