Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer with the Imam and Other Than Him. (If) the worshiper (commences) (in performing) an (obligatory) prayer, or making it up, (alone) or in supererogatory, and a funeral is present that he fears will be missed, or a vowed prayer, (then the congregation is established) in the place of his performance, not elsewhere, by the imam’s takbir, because the reality of establishing something is its actual doing, not merely commencing the establishment. So if it is not restricted by a sajdah... Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer: i.e., a person catching the obligatory prayer with the imam. The principle is that deficiency in worship intentionally without excuse is forbidden, and deficiency for completion is completion, because even though it is a deficiency in form, it is completion in meaning, and consideration of meanings takes precedence over consideration of forms, like demolishing a mosque to renew it, and like the deficiency of prostration when one raises his head because a thorn pricked his forehead and he could not prostrate, then he placed it where it did not count as two prostrations. As for when the incidental deficiency is legitimate, sometimes it is permitted, sometimes it is obligatory, and this has been covered in full. His saying: (and other than him) is a conjunct to 'catching' so this chapter should be titled 'Various Issues' as in al-Fath. His saying: (in performing an obligation or its qada) excludes supererogatory prayer, for he does not cut it for the congregation; rather he completes it as pairs because cutting it is nullification, not completion. His saying: (or its qada) i.e., qada of the very obligation for which the congregation is established, because it is completion of it. The excuse that qada itself is a sin, so it should not be made apparent, is not consistent. As for if it is qada of a different obligation, he does not cut it because it is nullification from every angle. His saying: (or in supererogatory, and a funeral is present) then he cuts the supererogatory because it is a follower of qada, unlike the funeral, if he chose to miss it, it would be with no substitute—thus in al-Fath. His saying: (or) vowed prayer—this contradicts what is in al-Bahr from al-Khulasah: 'If one commenced qada of missed prayers and then the congregation was established, he does not cut it, just like supererogatory, and the vowed prayer is like the missed prayer.' Except that it can be interpreted that his saying 'then the congregation was established' means the congregation for performing the obligation and its qada and the vowed prayer, as when one vows to pray two rak‘ahs, and then makes a congregation for that very vow, and prays one of them alone, and then the congregation for that vow is established, he may cut and join because it is completion. We have only pictured it as mentioned because a different vow, like a different obligation, does not permit following (the imam), as previously. And the statement of al-Sayyid that the distribution in the author’s wording regarding qada is invalid because by following he reveals the sin of delay and it should be concealed—and it would necessitate using a homonym in more than one meaning, which is permissible but subject to consideration—is not correct, because the first reasoning is not consistent, and there is no homonym used in multiple meanings; rather his saying 'then the congregation was established' has under it three particulars, not three meanings. Those particulars are: the congregation for performance, the congregation for qada, and the congregation for a vow. Let this be considered. His saying: (in the place of his performance) so if the congregation is established in the mosque while he is at home, or if he is in his mosque and the congregation is established in another, he does not cut absolutely—as in al-Sharh and others. And it is stated that they explicitly say to seek the congregation in a mosque if the congregation in one's current place is missed, and that congregation is obligatory and not restricted to one's mosque, and that cutting is for completion, so no difference appears. His saying: 'by the imam’s takbir, etc.' : no picture.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This lesson begins a new chapter: 'Bab Idrak al-Faridah' (Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer). The main ruling discussed is whether a person who has started a prayer (or other worship) alone may cut it to join the congregation. The underlying principle (asl) is that deliberately reducing worship without excuse is haram, but reduction for the purpose of completion is itself completion—form vs. meaning. The commentary then parses the key phrases from the matn. First, the ruling applies only to obligatory prayers (adā') or their qada, not to supererogatory prayers (nafl), because cutting a nafl prayer would be an invalidation, not completion. However, a nafl prayer may be cut if a funeral prayer is feared to be missed, because funeral prayer is more important (it is a fard kifayah with no substitute). For a vowed prayer (nadhr), the ruling is similar to the obligation being fulfilled: if the congregation is established for the same vowed prayer, he may cut and join for the sake of completion; but if the vow is different, he may not. The commentary also addresses a potential contradiction from al-Bahr and al-Khulāsa. Finally, the condition 'in the place of his performance' is discussed: if the congregation is elsewhere, he does not cut his prayer because it would not be completion in the same place. The passage ends with a nuanced discussion of the three particulars under 'the congregation is established'—performance, qada, and vow—rejecting the idea of multiple meanings in a homonym.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Catching the obligatory prayer with the imam, i.e., joining the congregation after having started alone.
نفل و منذور (nafl wa madhūr): Supererogatory prayer and vowed prayer; both are treated similarly but with conditions in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Cutting a fard prayer to join the congregation for the same fard in the same place is permissible because it is considered completion in meaning, not invalidation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Cutting One's Prayer to Join Congregation
Fiqh ruling on cutting prayer to join congregation with conditions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting an individual fard prayer to join the congregation and apply the conditions that determine when cutting is permissible, obligatory, or prohibited.

Core Idea
Cutting a prayer to join the congregation is a completion, not a nullification.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi refines the commentary on the chapter of 'Catching the Obligatory Prayer' from Maraqi al-Falah. The central question is whether a person who has started an obligatory prayer alone may cut it to join the congregation when the iqamah is called. The Hanafi answer is yes, based on the principle that a reduction aimed at a greater completion is itself a form of completion. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proofs, and the detailed conditions that determine when cutting is allowed, when it becomes obligatory, and when it is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Identify the principle that reducing for completion is completion (al-naqs li al-ikmal ikmal).
This principle is the foundation for the permissibility of cutting.
2
Identify When Cutting is Allowed for Fard
For a fard (ada or qada) when the congregation is for the same prayer in the same place, cutting is permissible.
The congregation must be for the identical prayer; otherwise, cutting is nullification.
3
Distinguish Between Types of Prayers
Nafl prayers are not cut for ordinary congregations (complete as two rak'ahs). However, nafl is cut for a funeral prayer feared to be missed. Vowed prayers follow the same rule as qada.
Funeral prayer has no substitute, making cutting obligatory.
4
Apply the Timing Condition
Depending on whether the sajdah of the first rak'ah has been performed, the ruling differs: before sajdah, cut immediately; after sajdah, for 2/3-rak'ah prayers cut after the rak'ah, for 4-rak'ah complete two rak'ahs then cut.
This ensures that the cut is a completion, not pure nullification.
5
Locate the Ikhtilaf and the Mufta Bihi
Some Hanafis said to complete two rak'ahs in all cases, but the sound opinion (mufta bihi) is to cut immediately with one taslim while standing, except where specified otherwise after sajdah.
Al-Tahtawi confirms the sound opinion (ala al-sahih).

Source Text

باب إدراك الفريضة
أي إدراك الشخص الفريضة مع الإمام والأصل فيه أن نقص العبادة قصداً بلا عذر حرام وان النقص للإكمال إكمال لأنه وإن كان نقصاً صورة فهو إكمال معنى، واعتبار المعاني أولى من اعتبار الصور كهدم المسجد لتجديده، وكنقص سجود من رفع رأسه لشوك أصاب جبهته فلم يتمكن من السجود ثم وضعه حيث لم يعد ذلك سجدتين، وأما إذا كان النقص العارض شرعي فتارة يجوز وتارة يجب، وقد تقدم مستوفى قوله: (وغيره) عطف على إدراك فحق هذا الباب أن يلقب بمسائل شتى كما في الفتح. قوله : (في أداء فرض أو قضائه أخرج به النفل، فإنه لا يقطعه بالإقامة، بل يتمه شفعاً لأن القطع فيه إبطال لا إكمال . قوله : (أو قضائه أي قضاء الفرض الذي أقيم لأنه إكمال لها والتعليل بأن القضاء معصية، فلا يظهرها لا يطرد، وأما لو كان قضاء فرض غير المقام، فلا يقطعه لأنه إبطال من كل وجه . قوله : (أو في نفل، وحضرت جنازة فإنه يقطع النفل لأنه معقب للقضاء بخلاف الجنازة لو اختار تفويتها كان لا إلى خلف كذا في الفتح. قوله : (أو) منذور) هذا يخالف ما في البحر عن الخلاصة شرع في قضاء الفوائت ثم أقيمت لا يقطع كالنفل والمنذور كالفائتة اهـ إلا أن يحمل قوله فأقيمت الجماعة أي جماعة أداء الفرض وقضائه والمنذور كما إذا نذر صلاة ركعتين فنذر جماعة هذا النذر بعينه فصلى إحداهما منفرداً، فأقام الجماعة هذا النذر فله أن يقطع، ويقتدي لأنه إكمال، وإنما صورناه بما ذكر لأن النذر المختلف كالفرض المختلف لا يجوز فيه الإقتداء كما مر ، وقول السيد لا يصح التوزيع في كلام المصنف بالنظر إلى القضاء لأنه بالاقتداء أظهر معضية التأخير وينبغي سترها، ولأنه يلزم استعمال المشترك في أكثر من معنى واحد، وهو يجوز منظور فيه لما قدمناه من أن العلة الأولى غير مطردة، وليس هنا مشترك استعمل في معان، بل قوله : فأقيمت الجماعة تحته جزئيات ثلاثة لا معان ثلاثة، وتلك الجزئيات جماعة الأداء، وجماعة القضاء، وجماعة النذر فليتأمل. قوله : ( في محل أدائه) فلو أقيمت في المسجد، وهو في البيت، أو كان في مسجده، فأقيمت في آخر لا يقطع مطلقاً كما في الشرح، وغيره وفيه أنهم صرحوا بطلب الجماعة في مسجد إن فاتته فيما هو فيه، وإن الجماعة واجبة ولم تقيد بمسجده وأن القطع للإكمال، فلا يظهر فرق حينئذ قوله بأن أحرم الخ)
قطع بتسليمة قائماً واقتدى على الصحيح وقيل : لا يقطع حتى يتم ركعتين من رباعية كالمتنفل الذي لا يخشى فوت جنازة قلنا : القطع للإكمال إكمال وهو بمحل الرفض، ولأنه لو حلف لا يصلي لا يحنث بما دون الركعة والجنازة لا خلف لها وبالقضاء يجمع بين المصلحتين إن لم يسجد لما شرع فيه ولو غير رباعية أو سجد للركعة الأولى في غير رباعية بأن كان في الفجر، أو المغرب فيقطع بعد السجود بتسليمة لأنه لو أضاف في الثنائية ركعة أخرى تم الفرض وتفوته الجماعة في الفجر ولا يتنفل بعدها مطلقاً، وفي المغرب للأكثر حكم الكل فتفوته الجماعة، ولا يتنفل مع الإمام فيها لمنع التنفل بالبتيراء، ومخالفة الإمام بإضافة رابعة وإن سجد وهو في رباعية كالظهر
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. That is, a person catching the obligatory prayer with the imam. The basis for this is that intentionally reducing an act of worship without excuse is forbidden, and that reduction for completion is completion, because even though it is a reduction in form, it is completion in meaning. Considering meanings is more important than considering forms, like demolishing a mosque to rebuild it, and like reducing the prostration of one who raised his head because a thorn hit his forehead and he could not prostrate, then he placed it where that did not count as two prostrations. As for when the incidental reduction is permitted by law, sometimes it is permissible and sometimes obligatory, and it has been discussed in full. His saying: 'and other than it' is a conjunction on 'catching', so this chapter deserves to be titled 'Various Issues' as in al-Fath. His saying: 'in performing a fard or making it up' excludes nafl, for he does not cut it for the iqamah, but rather completes it as two rak'ahs because cutting it is nullification, not completion. His saying: 'or making it up' means making up the fard for which congregation is established, because it is completion for it; and the reasoning that making up is a sin and should not be manifested is not consistent. As for if it is a make-up of a different fard than the one for which congregation is established, he does not cut it because it is nullification from every aspect. His saying: 'or in nafl, and a funeral prayer is present that is feared to be missed' – then he cuts the nafl because it is followed by make-up, unlike the funeral prayer; if he chose to miss it, it would be without substitute, as in al-Fath. His saying: 'or a vowed prayer' – this contradicts what is in al-Bahr from al-Khulasah: 'Someone who starts making up missed prayers, then iqamah is called, he does not cut it like nafl, and the vowed prayer is like the missed prayer', unless his saying 'then congregation is established' is interpreted as a congregation for performing the fard and its make-up and the vowed prayer, as when someone vows two rak'ahs and then a congregation is formed for that same vow, so he prays one of them alone, and then the congregation for that vow is established – he may cut and join because it is completion. We have only given this scenario because a different vow, like a different fard, does not permit joining, as has passed. And the master's saying that the distribution in the author's speech is not valid with regard to make-up because joining makes the sin of delay apparent and should be concealed, and because it necessitates using a homonym in more than one meaning – this is considered, because we already said that the first cause is not consistent, and there is no homonym used in multiple meanings here. Rather, his saying 'then the congregation is established' includes three particulars, not three meanings. Those particulars are: congregation for performance, congregation for make-up, and congregation for vow. So reflect. His saying: 'in the place of its performance' – if the iqamah is called in the mosque while he is at home, or if he is in his own mosque and iqamah is called in another, he does not cut at all, as in the sharh and others. And in it, they explicitly state that congregation is sought in the mosque if he missed it where he is, and that congregation is obligatory and not restricted to his mosque, and that cutting is for completion, so no difference appears then. His saying: 'because he commenced the iqamah' – he cuts with one taslim while standing and then joins, according to the sound opinion. It is said: he does not cut until he completes two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, like one performing nafl who does not fear missing a funeral prayer. We say: the cutting is for completion, and it is in a place of revocation, and because if he swore not to pray, he would not be breaking the oath for less than a rak'ah. The funeral prayer has no substitute, and by cutting he combines the two benefits, if he has not prostrated for what he started. Even if it is not a four-rak'ah prayer. Or if he has prostrated for the first rak'ah in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, such as Fajr or Maghrib, then he cuts after the prostration with one taslim, because if he adds another rak'ah in a two-rak'ah prayer, the fard is completed and he misses the congregation in Fajr, and he cannot perform nafl after it at all. In Maghrib, the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he misses the congregation, and he cannot perform nafl with the imam in it because of the prohibition of nafl with an odd number, and opposing the imam by adding a fourth. And if he has prostrated while in a four-rak'ah prayer, such as Zuhr.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on the chapter of 'Catching the Obligatory Prayer' from Maraqi al-Falah. The core issue is: when a person has started an obligatory prayer (either performance or make-up) alone, and then the congregation is established for that same prayer, may he cut his prayer to join the congregation? The Hanafi position is that he may cut his prayer with one taslim while standing and then join the imam. This is because the reduction (cutting the prayer) is considered a completion in meaning, even though it is a reduction in form. The principle is that reducing an act of worship for the sake of completing it in a better way is permissible, analogous to demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better. The text distinguishes between cases: if the prayer is a nafl (supererogatory), it should not be cut but completed as two rak'ahs because cutting it would be pure nullification, not completion. If it is a funeral prayer (janazah) that is feared to be missed, one may cut the nafl to join it because the funeral has no substitute. For vowed prayers, the ruling follows the same principle as make-up of the same fard. The text also discusses the condition that the congregation must be in the same place (the mosque where one is praying); if the iqamah is called elsewhere, one does not cut. A significant point of discussion is when exactly one cuts: before or after the first sajdah of the first rak'ah. Before the sajdah (i.e., within the first rak'ah), one cuts immediately. After the sajdah, for two-rak'ah (Fajr) or three-rak'ah (Maghrib) prayers, one completes the rak'ah and then cuts after the sajdah, because adding another rak'ah would complete the fard and cause one to miss the congregation. For four-rak'ah prayers, if one has already performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah, the better view is that one does not cut but continues to complete two rak'ahs, then joins the congregation as a nafl, because one can still join the congregation after completing two rak'ahs. The hashia here refines the commentary by clarifying the reasoning and resolving apparent contradictions in the sources.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): The act of a person catching the obligatory prayer with the imam (joining the congregation) after having started it alone.
قطع (qaṭʿ): Cutting or terminating one's current prayer before completion, specifically to join the congregation.
اقتدى (iqtadā): To follow the imam in prayer, i.e., to join the congregation after cutting one's individual prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is praying Maghrib alone. After performing the sajdah of the first rak'ah, he hears the iqamah for the same Maghrib congregation in the same mosque. According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Cut with one taslim immediately.
B) Complete two rak'ahs then cut.
C) Cut after completing the first rak'ah with one taslim.
D) Complete the prayer alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits cutting an individual prayer to join the congregation, based on the principle that reduction for completion is completion, with conditions regarding the type of prayer, timing, and location.

Cutting Short a Nafl Prayer to Join Congregational Prayer
Ruling with proof for cutting short nafl to join congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for cutting short a nafl prayer upon the iqama and apply the conditions correctly in different nafl types.

Core Idea
You may cut a nafl short to join congregation — but how depends on how many rak'ahs you've done.

When you're in the middle of a voluntary prayer and the iqama is called, you face a dilemma: leave the nafl to join the fard or complete it and risk missing the congregation. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance based on the type of nafl and how far you have progressed. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its intra-madhhab variations, and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the type of nafl (2-rak'ah, 3-rak'ah, or 4-rak'ah) and how many rak'ahs you have completed, especially whether you have performed sajdah in the first rak'ah.
The ruling differs based on whether you are in a two-rak'ah (Fajr-like), three-rak'ah (Maghrib-like), or four-rak'ah (Zuhr-like) nafl.
2
Apply the cut-off rule before sajdah
If you have not yet prostrated in the first rak'ah, you may cut off immediately with one salam while standing and then join the congregation.
This is the simplest case, analogous to saving a life.
3
Apply the rule after sajdah by nafl type
If you have prostrated, the ruling splits: for 2-rak'ah (Fajr) or 3-rak'ah (Maghrib), cut off after that sajdah with salam. For 4-rak'ah (Zuhr), add a second rak'ah to complete a valid two-rak'ah unit, then salam and join.
The rationale is to avoid turning the nafl into an unintended fard and to preserve the opportunity for congregation.
4
Handle the case of three rak'ahs completed
If you have already performed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say complete the fourth standing, then join as mutanafifil. Muhammad al-Shaybani says complete the fourth sitting to keep it as nafl, then join.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Note exceptions for Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib
After completing the nafl alone, you may join the congregation as a nafl prayer, except for Asr and Fajr (prohibition of nafl after them) and Maghrib (due to opposition to the imam).
The hadith cited removes Fajr and Maghrib from the general permission to join as nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة (قطع) بتسليمة قائماً (و) بعده (اقتدى) على الصحيح وقيل : لا يقطع حتى يتم ركعتين من رباعية كالمتنفل الذي لا يخشى فوت جنازة قلنا : القطع للإكمال إكمال وهو بمحل الرفض، ولأنه لو حلف لا يصلي لا يحنث بما دون الركعة والجنازة لا خلف لها وبالقضاء يجمع بين المصلحتين إن لم يسجد لما شرع فيه ولو غير رباعية (أو سجد) للركعة الأولى في غير رباعية) بأن كان في الفجر، أو المغرب فيقطع بعد السجود بتسليمة لأنه لو أضاف في الثنائية ركعة أخرى تم الفرض وتفوته الجماعة في الفجر ولا يتنفل بعدها مطلقاً، وفي المغرب للأكثر حكم الكل فتفوته الجماعة، ولا يتنفل مع الإمام فيها لمنع التنفل بالبتيراء، ومخالفة الإمام بإضافة رابعة ( وإن سجد) وهو (في رباعية) كالظهر ضم ركعة ثانية صيانة للمؤدي عن البطلان وتشهد وسلم لتصير الركعتان له نافلة ثم اقتدى مفترضاً لإحراز فضل الجماعة (وإن صلى (ثلاثاً) من رباعية فأقيمت (أتمها) أربعاً منفرداً حكماً للأكثر وعن محمد يتمها جالساً لتنقلب نفلاً فيجمع بين ثواب النفل والفرض بالجماعة (ثم ) بعد الإتمام (اقتدى متنفلاً) إن شاء وهو أفضل لعدم الكراهة (إلا في العصر) والفجر للنهي عن التنفل بعدهما وفي المغرب للمخالفة لأنه لم قال : (إذا صليت في أهلك، ثم أدركت الصلاة فصلها إلا الفجر والمغرب) وقوله : فصلها يعني نقلاً لأنه أمر به نصاً لرجلين لم يصليا معه الظهر وأخبرا بصلاتهما في رحالهما، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: إذا صليتما في رحالكما ثم أتيتما صلاة قوم فصليا معهم واجعلا صلاتكما معهم سبحة، أي معه
Book of Prayer: He cuts off with one salam while standing, and after that he follows (the imam) according to the sound opinion. It is said: he should not cut off until he completes two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah (nafl), like one who does not fear missing a funeral prayer. We say: cutting off for completion is completion, and it is subject to rejection. And because if he swore not to pray, he would not be breaking his oath by less than a rak'ah. The funeral prayer has no alternate. By making up (the prayer), he combines the two benefits if he has not prostrated for what he began. And if it is other than a four-rak'ah (prayer) – meaning if he prostrated for the first rak'ah in other than four-rak'ah (prayer), such as in Fajr or Maghrib – then he cuts off after the prostration with one salam, because if he adds another rak'ah in the two-rak'ah (nafl), the obligatory prayer would be completed and he would miss the congregation in Fajr, and he cannot perform supererogatory prayer after it absolutely. And in Maghrib, the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he misses the congregation, and he cannot perform supererogatory prayer with the imam in it because supererogatory prayer with 'betira' (cut-off) is prohibited, and because adding a fourth rak'ah would be opposing the imam. And if he prostrated while in a four-rak'ah (prayer) like Zuhr, he adds a second rak'ah to protect what he has performed from invalidity, then recites the tashahhud and says salam so that the two rak'ahs become supererogatory for him, then he follows (the imam) as one offering the obligatory prayer to attain the virtue of congregation. And if he prayed three (rak'ahs) of a four-rak'ah (nafl) and the iqama is called, he completes it as four alone according to the majority. According to Muhammad, he completes it sitting so that it becomes supererogatory, then he can combine the reward of supererogatory and obligatory prayer with the congregation. Then, after completion, he follows (the imam) as one offering supererogatory prayer if he wishes, and that is better because there is no dislike, except in Asr and Fajr due to the prohibition of supererogatory prayer after them, and in Maghrib due to opposition. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you pray in your dwellings, then you catch up with the prayer, pray it – except Fajr and Maghrib.' His saying 'pray it' means supererogatory prayer, because he ordered it explicitly regarding two men who did not pray Zuhr with him and informed him that they had prayed in their dwellings. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you pray in your dwellings, then you come to a congregation, pray with them and make your prayer with them a supererogatory prayer (subha).'
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi expands on the rulings for a person who is engaged in a supererogatory (nafl) prayer when the iqama for the congregational obligatory prayer is called. The central question is whether and how he should cut short his nafl to join the congregation. The author explains the general principle: if he has not yet prostrated for the first rak'ah, he may cut off immediately with one salam while standing and then join the congregation. This is considered a valid excuse similar to saving a life. However, if he has already prostrated for the first rak'ah, the ruling depends on the type of nafl prayer he is performing. For a two-rak'ah nafl (like Fajr) or a three-rak'ah nafl (like Maghrib), if he has prostrated the first rak'ah, he should cut off with one salam after that prostration. This is because adding another rak'ah would turn his prayer into an obligatory one, causing him to miss the congregation. In Maghrib, the majority view treats the three rak'ahs as essentially one unit, so he would miss the congregation and also cannot join the imam as a muqtadi because doing so would require him to add a fourth rak'ah, conflicting with the imam. For a four-rak'ah nafl (e.g., Zuhr), if he has prostrated for the first rak'ah, he should add a second rak'ah to complete a valid two-rak'ah unit, then recite tashahhud and salam. This two-rak'ah unit becomes his nafl, and then he joins the congregation as one offering the fard prayer. If he has already completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that he should complete the fourth rak'ah standing, then join the congregation as a mu'tanafifil (offering nafl again). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that he should complete the fourth rak'ah sitting to keep the entire prayer as nafl. After completing alone, he may join the congregation as a nafl prayer, except for Asr and Fajr due to prohibition of nafl after them, and for Maghrib due to opposition. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet instructed two men who had already prayed at home to pray with the congregation and make that prayer a supererogatory one (subha). Thus, the ruling acknowledges the virtue of congregation while providing flexibility for those already engaged in nafl.

Key Terms
البتيراء (al-batīrā'): A supererogatory prayer consisting of only two rak'ahs, considered 'cut off' from additional rak'ahs.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is praying a 4-rak'ah nafl (e.g., before Zuhr). He has completed one rak'ah with sajdah and the iqama is called. What should he do?
A) Cut off immediately with one salam and join the congregation.
B) Add a second rak'ah, complete two, then join the congregation.
C) Complete all four rak'ahs, then pray the fard alone.
D) Continue the nafl and ignore the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides flexible rulings to allow one to join the congregation even if engaged in nafl, prioritizing communal prayer while preserving the validity of the voluntary prayer.

When to Cut Your Prayer to Join the Congregation
Ruling on cutting the prayer when the imam starts the congregation after standing for the third rak'ah before sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on cutting a voluntary or supererogatory prayer to join the congregation, distinguishing the cases of fard, sunnah, and special exceptions.

Core Idea
Cutting a prayer to join the congregation is wajib if it means not missing the fard with congregation; the method of cutting is by taslim or takbir while standing.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi explains the Hanafi rulings on leaving a prayer midway to join the congregation. The key question is whether and how one can terminate a prayer already begun. The text presents different opinions within the Hanafi school, especially regarding the third rak'ah case and sunnah prayers. Understanding these rulings helps avoid common errors in daily prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation: a person praying a four-rak'ah fard alone stands for the third rak'ah before performing sajdah, and then the congregation is established. Determine whether he can cut his prayer and how.
This is a common occurrence in mosques where iqamah is given while individuals are already praying.
2
State the preferred ruling
According to the relied-upon view (al-ashah), he cuts his prayer while standing by giving one taslim, or he returns to the sitting position and then cuts. This preserves the validity of his prayer while allowing him to join the congregation.
The reason given: 'because the sitting is for dissolution (tahallul)' meaning the tashahhud is not yet required.
3
Analyze internal ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement within the Hanafi school: Al-Sarakhsi insists that returning to sitting is necessary; otherwise the prayer is invalid. Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) says he can simply say takbir while standing intending to join the imam, thereby fulfilling the obligation within the new prayer.
The author sides with Fakhr al-Islam, calling it 'the most correct' (al-ashah).
4
Apply to sunnah prayers
For the sunnah of Friday or Zuhr: the preferred view is to complete two rak'at, say taslim, then join the congregation for fard, and later make up the sunnah as four rak'at. This combines the benefits of both prayers.
Some scholars say complete four rak'at as it is like one prayer, but the author prefers the two-taslim approach.
5
Identify the general principle and exception
The general rule: if the imam is already in the fard prayer, join immediately without delaying for sunnah. Exception: For Fajr, one may pray the sunnah even in the mosque if confident of not missing the fard (even if catching the imam in tashahhud).
This is because the Fajr sunnah is strongly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings about cutting one's prayer to join the congregation. First, if a person is praying a four-rak'ah fard alone and has stood for the third rak'ah without having performed sajdah, the congregation begins. The relied-upon position (al-ashah) is that he should cut his prayer while standing, either by giving one taslim or by returning to the sitting position (qa'dah). Al-Sarakhsi warns that if he does not return to sitting, his prayer becomes invalid because the sitting is essential for tashahhud and the prayer would not count as fard. Fakhr al-Islam says he can simply make takbir while standing with the intention to join the imam, thereby the obligatory part is fulfilled within the new prayer. Second, for sunnah prayers: if someone begins the sunnah of Friday and the khatib comes out, or begins the sunnah of Zuhr and the iqamah is given, the preferred view (al-awjah) is to complete two rak'at, say taslim, then after joining the congregation and praying the fard, he can make up the sunnah as four rak'at. This combines the benefits of both praying the sunnah and listening to the khutbah or joining the congregation promptly. Some scholars say he should complete the sunnah as four because it is like one unit. However, the author (Al-Tahtawi) notes that if he is engaged in reciting the Quran or the muezzin is chanting, it is better to complete because that is not a state of listening to the khutbah. Third, a general principle: when someone arrives and the imam is already in the fard prayer, he should join immediately and not delay by praying the sunnah, even if he has not missed anything. The exception is Fajr: he may pray its sunnah even in the mosque, away from the row, if he is confident he will not miss the fard (even if he catches the imam in tashahhud). This is because the Fajr sunnah is strongly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the time for Fajr is short.

Key Terms
قطع قائماً (qata'a qā'iman): To terminate the prayer while standing, without performing additional actions, by saying one taslim or by intending to join the imam.
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): The most correct opinion among the transmitted views.
الأوجه (al-awjah): The most appropriate or preferable view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the exception to the rule of joining the imam immediately without praying sunnah?
A) Friday prayer, because the sunnah is long
B) Fajr, because its sunnah is strongly emphasized
C) Zuhr, because one can make up later
D) Asr, because the time is short

Key Takeaway
When the congregation begins, one may cut a sunnah or nafilah prayer to join; the method varies by case, but the preferred Hanafi view facilitates joining without invalidation.

Joining the Congregation: When to Pray Sunnah and When Not
General rule: join immediately, do not pray sunnah; exception for Fajr sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling for joining the imam when sunnah prayer is due, and identify the exception for Fajr with its condition.

Core Idea
Join the imam immediately; sunnah is set aside — except for Fajr if you are sure to catch the fard.

When you enter the mosque and find the imam already in the fard prayer, the Hanafi school commands you to join immediately. You must not delay by performing the sunnah prayer, even if you have not missed any rak'ah. There is one exception: the sunnah of Fajr. This lesson clarifies the rule and its single exception.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The matn says: 'And whoever attends while the imam is in the obligatory prayer, he joins him and does not engage in sunnah.' This applies even if he hasn't missed anything.
The rule is absolute inside the mosque.
2
Identify the exception
The exception is signaled by 'except' (إلا) for the Fajr prayer: he prays its sunnah.
Only Fajr is excepted, not any other prayer.
3
Understand the condition for the exception
The exception applies only if he is safe from missing the fard prayer, even if it means catching the imam in the tashahhud.
The key word is 'amana' (he is safe from missing).
4
Recognize the underlying rationale
The Fajr sunnah is highly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah) and its time is short. Therefore, it is permissible to combine both virtues: the sunnah and the congregation.
This rationale is specific to Fajr and does not extend to other prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(And whoever attends while the imam is in the obligatory prayer, he joins him and does not engage in sunnah) in the mosque, even if he has not missed anything. And if he is outside the mosque and fears missing a rak'ah, he joins. The original sunnah [is prayed first] then he joins, because it is possible to combine both virtues. (Except) in Fajr: he prays its sunnah, even in the mosque far from the row if he is safe from missing it, even if he catches him in tashahhud.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This is a general principle: when a person enters a mosque and the imam is already leading the obligatory (fard) prayer, the Hanafi ruling is that he should immediately join the congregation and not occupy himself with the sunnah prayer first, even if he has not missed any part of the fard. This is because joining the congregation for the fard is more important than performing the sunnah at that moment. The exception is the Fajr prayer: due to the strong emphasis (sunnah mu'akkadah) of the two rak'at before Fajr and the short time, one is permitted to pray the Fajr sunnah even in the mosque, provided one is confident of catching the fard (even if it means joining the imam in the final tashahhud). The phrase 'and the original sunnah, then he joins' suggests that if one is outside the mosque and fears missing a rak'ah, he should first pray the sunnah (outside) and then join, because he can combine the two virtues (sunnah and congregation). However, the general rule is to prioritize the congregation.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The supererogatory (nafl) prayers performed before or after the obligatory prayers, especially the rawatib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: join the imam for fard immediately, setting aside sunnah; the only exception is the Fajr sunnah, provided you are sure to catch the fard.

Cutting Voluntary Prayer When Congregation Begins: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on cutting voluntary prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on cutting a nafl prayer when jama'ah starts and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When congregation starts, you must cut the nafl and join—but how you cut depends on whether it's a nafl or a sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a practical scenario: you are in the middle of a voluntary prayer (nafl or sunnah) and the jama'ah begins. The Hanafi school holds that you must cut the voluntary prayer to join the congregation, but there is disagreement among Hanafi authorities on the exact method. Understanding this dispute clarifies both the ruling and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the voluntary prayer is a general nafl (e.g., four-rak'ah) or a sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr. The ruling differs based on the type of prayer and the point at which the congregation begins.
The base matn distinguishes: for nafl, the person has already stood for the third rak'ah; for sunnah, the khatib has come out or iqamah is said.
2
List the positions
Three Hanafi views are noted: (1) cut while standing and join the imam (relied-upon), (2) return to sitting then cut (Sarakhsi), (3) for sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr, cut with taslim after two rak'ahs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
The first view is attributed to Fakhr al-Islam and favored by al-Tahtawi.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The dispute centers on whether sitting (qu'ud) is necessary for the prayer to be valid. Sarakhsi argues that missing the obligatory sitting invalidates the nafl. The relied-upon view considers that standing intention suffices to exit the nafl and enter the congregation.
The term 'tahallul' (exiting prayer) is key: cutting with one taslim or by intention.
4
Apply to sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr
For the sunnah, the preferred method is to sit after two rak'ahs and say taslim, then join the congregation. This allows listening to the khutbah (Jumu'ah) or performing the fard with the congregation, and later making up the sunnah.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf transmitted this view; it is considered 'al-awjah' (more appropriate).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Tahtawi confirms that the relied-upon position is to cut standing for nafl and to cut with taslim after two rak'ahs for sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr. The fatwa today follows this, as it combines the benefits of not missing the congregation and preserving the sunnah.
The authority weight is zahir_riwayah, and this is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from a hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the ruling on cutting a voluntary prayer (nafl or sunnah) when the congregational prayer begins. The base matn states that if one is praying a four-rak'ah nafl alone and stands for the third rak'ah, and the congregation starts before his prostration, he should cut the prayer while standing because sitting (qa'dah) is only for tashahhud. Cutting with one taslim is sufficient, or he may return to sitting. This is the most correct view. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi disagrees: if he does not return to sitting, the prayer is invalid because sitting is obligatory and the performed sitting did not count as obligatory. Fakhr al-Islam favors the first view: he should say takbir while standing, intending to join the imam, and his obligation is fulfilled within that intention. The matn then addresses the sunnah of Jumu'ah and Zuhr: if one started the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib came out, or started the sunnah of Zuhr and the congregation started, he should say taslim after two rak'ahs, as narrated from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa. This combines the benefits of listening to the khutbah and performing the sunnah later. After performing the fard, he makes up the sunnah as four rak'ahs. Some mashayikh say he completes it as four right away because it is like one prayer. The hashiya author (al-Tahtawi) adds his own comment (qultu) that completing the sunnah while the muraqqi and mu'adhdhin are humming is better because it is not a time for listening to the khutbah. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the missing sitting makes the nafl invalid in Sarakhsi's view, and there is dispute about repeating tashahhud. The passage also clarifies that the phrase 'combining both benefits' refers to listening and performing sunnah after fard. The author then refines the interpretation of 'when the khatib came out' as meaning the khatib delivered the khutbah, and notes that this research is unique to him.

Key Terms
نافلة (nafila): Voluntary prayer, specifically here a four-rak'ah prayer performed alone before congregation.
قعود (qu'ud): Sitting posture in prayer, specifically the final sitting for tashahhud.
تسليمة (taslima): One salutation (salam) to end prayer; here cutting with one taslim is sufficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Continue the nafl but intend it as part of the jama'ah

Key Takeaway
When congregation starts, the Hanafi ruling is to cut the voluntary prayer—either standing with intention to join (for nafl) or after two rak'ahs with taslim (for sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr)—to avoid missing the obligatory prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Fajr Sunnah When Congregation Starts
Rulings on performing Fajr sunnah when congregation starts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Fajr sunnah when the obligatory prayer has begun, and apply the exception for Fajr based on the hadith and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
For Fajr, pray the sunnah even if the imam has started, as long as you can catch him in tashahhud.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: you arrive at the mosque for Fajr and the imam is already in the obligatory prayer. Should you skip the sunnah and join immediately, or pray the sunnah first? The Hanafi school makes an exception for Fajr due to its special virtue, allowing you to pray the sunnah as long as you are confident you will still catch the congregation (even if only the tashahhud). The lesson will explore the evidence and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The matn states: when the imam is in obligatory prayer, one should follow him and not occupy himself with sunnah. This is the default for all prayers.
2
Recognize the exception for Fajr
The text explicitly excludes Fajr: 'except in Fajr: then he prays its sunnah, even in the mosque, away from the rows, if he is safe from missing the imam.'
3
Understand the condition of safety
Safety means being able to catch the imam even in tashahhud, as agreed upon by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The hashya clarifies this is by consensus.
This differs from catching a rak'ah; tashahhud is sufficient to gain the virtue of congregation.
4
Apply the hadith and its interpretation
The hadith 'If the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory' is general but is applied to other prayers, not Fajr, due to ahadith emphasizing the virtue of Fajr sunnah. This is an exception based on textual evidence.
5
Note the recommended practice
It is better to pray the Fajr sunnah at home. If in the mosque, one should pray in a spot away from the rows to avoid disturbing the congregation. If fearing missing the imam, one should leave the sunnah and join.
Leaving the sunnah to avoid makruh is preferred over performing it when it causes violation of congregation.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling regarding the Fajr sunnah and joining the congregation. The matn states that a person who attends the mosque and finds the imam in obligatory prayer should follow him and not occupy himself with sunnah, except for Fajr. For Fajr, he should pray his sunnah even in the mosque, away from the rows, if he is safe from missing the fard (even if he catches only the tashahhud). The hadith 'If the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory' is applied to other prayers, not Fajr, due to the great virtue of Fajr sunnah. It is better to pray the Fajr sunnah at home, as reported in hadith: it brings provision, reduces family disputes, and seals with faith. The preferred time is at first break of dawn, though some say near the obligatory prayer. The commentary also discusses the virtue of praying in different mosques: Masjid al-Haram, the Prophet's Mosque, and Bayt al-Maqdis. If one fears missing the imam by engaging in the sunnah, he should leave the sunnah and follow, because performing it in the mosque at that time is makruh (disliked), especially if mixed with the rows. The hashiya from Durar clarifies that one should perform the sunnah if he catches the imam even in tashahhud, by agreement among Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa, and this is not limited to catching a rak'ah. The passage concludes with a note that the disagreement about catching Jumu'ah tashahhud is not applicable here.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the Fajr obligatory prayer.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked act; here praying sunnah in mosque after iqamah is makruh tanzihi if it causes missing congregation.
اقتدى (iqtada): To follow the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is unique: one may pray it even after iqamah as long as the imam can still be caught in tashahhud.

Virtue and Time of Sunnah al-Fajr
Ruling with proof on the virtue, time, and place of Sunnah al-Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Sunnah al-Fajr and identify the preferred time and place according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sunnah al-Fajr is a confirmed sunnah best performed at home at the first light of dawn.

This lesson examines the ruling, virtue, and optimal performance of the two rak'ahs before Fajr. It clarifies the apparent conflict with the hadith 'no prayer after iqamah' and provides evidence for the home preference, along with the blessed time at dawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The passage states that the two rak'ahs of Fajr are sunnah (confirmed sunnah, muakkadah). Note that the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, based on the strength of the evidence.
Sunnah muakkadah is a practice the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Locate the primary proof for home preference
The text cites a hadith: 'A person's prayer in his house is better than his prayer in my mosque, except the obligatory prayer.' This establishes that for nawafil (supererogatory prayers), home is superior.
The exception is obligatory prayers, which are better in congregation at the mosque.
3
Understand the exception for iqamah hadith
The opening statement 'When the iqamah is said, no prayer except the obligatory one' is interpreted as applying to other than Sunnah al-Fajr due to its specific virtue, as previously mentioned in the text.
This is a critical refinement to avoid misunderstanding.
4
Note the recommended time
The text mentions the most beloved time is 'at the first break of dawn' (أول طلوع الفجر), though some say closer to the obligatory prayer.
The Hanafi preferred view is the earliest time after true dawn.
5
Recognize the virtue hadiths
Hadiths about mosque virtures are quoted to show overall reward, but they do not override the specific sunnah home preference. The text reconciles them by distinguishing obligatory from supererogatory prayers.
Understanding this reconciliation is key to the Hanafi position.

Making Up the Sunnah of Fajr: Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Difference
Critical commentary on the ruling of qada' for the Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on making up the sunnah of Fajr, explain the difference between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
The sunnah of Fajr is made up only if missed with the fard, before noon – and even then, it is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage from Al-Tahtawi's hashya on Maraqi al-Falah focuses on the often-confused ruling of making up the sunnah of Fajr. While the reward of congregation far surpasses that of the Fajr sunnah, the proper understanding of qada' for sunnan is essential. The commentator resolves an apparent conflict between Imam Muhammad and the two Sahibayn, clarifying that the difference is more terminological than substantive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sunnah of Fajr (two rak'ahs before the fard). Its hukm is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). Determine when it can be made up if missed.
The passage states it is only made up if missed together with the fard prayer, and only before noon.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad holds that it is made up individually after sunrise before noon; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it permissible but not obligatory.
The commentator notes there is no real disagreement: the Sahibayn say 'not required' (la yajib) but 'if done, no harm'; Muhammad says 'I prefer that he make it up'.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is whether a person should deliberately make up the sunnah after sunrise. According to Muhammad, it is recommended; according to the other view, it is not required but permissible.
The mufta bihi is the recommended view, as per the sound opinion in the Hanafi madhhab.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A person wakes up after sunrise, having missed the Fajr fard and its sunnah. He prays the fard alone. Should he pray the sunnah? According to the relied-upon view, yes, he may pray it before noon, but it is not obligatory.
If he prays it after noon, it is not considered qada' of the sunnah.
5
Note the broader principle
The use of 'qada' for sunnah is metaphorical (majaz). The sunnah is not obligatory, so its make-up is not a legal obligation but a recommended follow-up when missed with the fard.
This distinguishes qada' of fard (obligatory) from qada' of sunnah (recommended).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن ثواب الجماعة أعظم من فضيلة ركعتي الفجر لأنها تفضل الفرض منفرداً بسبع ضعفاً لا تبلغ ركعتا الفجر ضعفاً واحداً منها ولم تقض سنة الفجر إلا بفوتها مع الفرض إلى الزوال، وقال محمد رحمه الله تقضى منفردة بعد الشمس قبل الزوال فلا قضاء لها قبل الشمس، ولا بعد الزوال اتفاقاً، وسواء صلى منفرداً أو بجماعة وقضى السنة التي قبل الظهر في الصحيح في وقته قبل صلاة شفعه على المفتي به كذا في شرح الكنز للعلامة المقدسي وفي فتاوى العتابي المختار تقديم الثنتين على الأربع، وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وهو الأصح لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر يصليهن بعد الركعتين، وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالتي قبل الظهر، ولا مانع عن التي قبل العشاء من قضائها بعده ولم يصل الظهر جماعة بإدراك ركعة أو ركعتين اتفاقاً يبر به في حلقه ليصلينه جماعة بل أدرك فضلها أي فضل الجماعة اتفاقاً ولو في التشهد واختلف في مدرك الثلاث من رباعية أو الثنتين من الثلاثية فإذا حلف لا يصلي الظهر جماعة فأدرك ركعة لا يحنث، وإن أدرك فضلها نص عليه محمد كذا في الهداية ذكره السيد. قوله: تركها أفاد أنه به لم يشرع فيها فلو شرع أتمها مطلقاً لأن القطع حينئذ للإبطال قوله: وقال محمد رحمه الله تقضى منفردة إلخ قيل لا خلاف بينهم في الحقيقة لأنهما يقولان ليس عليه القضاء وإن فعل لا بأس به ومحمد يقول أحب إلي أن يقضي وإن لم يفعل لا شيء عليه قوله: ولا بعد الزوال اتفاقاً أي على الصحيح وقيل يقضيها تبعاً بعده ولا يقضيها مقصوداً إجماعاً كما في الكافي وغاية البيان. قوله: وقضى السنة الخ إطلاق القضاء على ما ليس بواجب مجازاً للمشاكلة ولهذا كان الأولى أن ينوي السنة لا القضاء قهستاني قوله: في الصحيح وقيل لا تقضي أصلاً لأن المواظبة عليها إنما ثبتت قبل الفرض قوله: في وقته وقال بعض المشايخ أنها تقضي بعد أي الوقت إذا فاتت معه لأنه كم من شيء ثبت تبعاً وإن لم يثبت قصداً كذا في الشرح. قوله: قبل صلاة شفعة لأن الأربع متقدمة على الركعتين لتقدمها على الفرض المتقدم عليهما وقد تعذر التقديم على الفرض ولم يتعذر على السنة فتقدم الأربع كذا في شرح المجمع. قوله: الحديث عائشة الخ ولئلا يفوتهما أيضاً عن موضعهما قصداً بلا ضرورة. قوله: ولا مانع الخ قال السيد في شرحه والتقييد بالتي قبل الظهر وكذا الجمعة كما في الدر للاحتراز عن التي قبل العشاء لأنها مندوبة فلا تقضى أصلاً وكذا التي قبل العصر بل أولى لكراهة التنقل بعده اهـ ولو قال المصنف ولا مانع من قضاء التي قبل العشاء بعدها لكان أوضح وأخصر. قوله: بل أدرك فضلها وهو المضاعفة وفي شرح المقدسي عن الاتقاني المسبوق يدرك ثواب الجماعة لكن لا كثواب مدرك أول الصلاة مع الإمام لفوات التكبيرة الأولى اهـ. قوله: فإذا حلف الخ فرض المثال هنا نفياً وفيما قبله إثباتاً إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق بين الإثبات والنفي في الحكم قوله: اختار شمس الأئمة الخ يضعف قوله باتفاقهم في باب الأيمان أن لو حلف لا يأكل هذا الرغيف لا يحنث إلا بأكل كله وأن الأكثر لا يقوم مقام الكل قوله: يحنث بإدراكه في التشهد فذكر الركعة في الكافي وغيره ليس احترازياً واعلم أن ذكر هذه المسألة محله كتاب الأيمان وإنما ذكرت هنا لبيان أنه لا تلازم بين إدراك الفضل وإدراك الجماعة. قوله: ويتطوع قبل الفرض الخ هذه العبارة تدل على التخيير في الفعل وهو إنما يظهر في غير المؤكد أما المؤكد فيأتي به من غير تخيير إن أمن فوت الوقت أفاده السيد وفي البحر وإن لم تكن مؤكدة فإن كانت من المستحبات استحب الإتيان بها وإلا فهو مخير وقد يقال أن المراد في كلامه الجواز المطلق لا مستوى الطرفين فيلاقي المؤكدة والمستحبة. قوله: إن أمن فوت الوقت الخ لو أبدله بقوله إن أمن فوت الجماعة لكان أولى لأنه إذا علم الترك عند خوف فوت الجماعة فلأن يعلم عند خوف فوت الوقت بالطريق الأولى أفاده السيد قوله: ولو منفرداً وصل بقوله ويتطوع وقيل إنما يأتي بالمؤكدة إن صلى بجماعة وإن كان منفرداً يخير فيها لعدم نقل المواظبة عنه في غير الأداء بجماعة والأول أصح قاله السيد قوله: فإنها شرعت أي فإن السنة كما صرح به في الشرح وهذا لا يظهر في غير المؤكد قوله: والمنفرد في ذلك أحوج لنقصان صلاته من وجه واسم الإشارة يرجع إلى قطع طمع الشيطان وفيه أن المنفرد وغيره في ذلك سواء ولا يظهر ذلك إلا في المكمل للنقص. قوله: وهو أحوط أي إتيان المنفرد بالسنن فالضمير يرجع إلى معلوم من المقام. قوله: التكميل نقصها في حقنا قد يقال أن التكميل إنما يكون لشيء قد نقص وحينئذ فلا يكون إلا في البعدية فتكمل ما نقص من الفرض ويمكن أن يقال أنه الفرض ناقصاً يكمل ولو بما فعل قبله والأثر يدل عليه فإنه ورد أنه إذا وجد في صلاة بعد صلاة.(1) قوله وهو أحوط لعل ذلك نسخته التي كتب عليها وإلا فنسخة الشرح هنا وهو أصح والأخذ به أحوط كما لا يخفى والخطب سهل اهـ مصححه.
Because the reward of congregation is greater than the virtue of the two rak'ahs of Fajr, since it (congregation) surpasses the obligatory prayer performed alone by seven double degrees, while the two rak'ahs of Fajr do not reach even one double degree of it. The sunnah of Fajr is not made up except if it is missed along with the obligatory prayer, up to noon. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is made up individually after sunrise before noon; there is no making it up before sunrise, nor after noon, by agreement. Whether one prayed individually or in congregation. And he makes up the sunnah before Zuhr, according to the sound view, in its time before the prayer of its shaf' (i.e., the two rak'ahs after it), according to the mufta bihi. So it is in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Allamah al-Maqdisi. And in Fatawa al-Attabi, the chosen view is to give precedence to the two over the four. And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam, and it is the most correct due to the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he missed the four before Zuhr, prayed them after the two rak'ahs. And the ruling of the four before Jumu'ah is like those before Zuhr. And there is no prevention of making up the four before Isha after it. And he did not pray Zuhr in congregation by catching one rak'ah or two rak'ahs; by agreement, his oath is nullified regarding his intention to pray it in congregation, but rather he caught its virtue, i.e., the virtue of the congregation, by agreement, even if in the tashahhud. And there is disagreement regarding the one who catches three of a four-rak'ah prayer or two of a three-rak'ah prayer. So if one swears not to pray Zuhr in congregation, then catches one rak'ah, he does not break his oath. If he catches its virtue, it is stated by Muhammad, so it is in al-Hidayah, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'He left it' indicates that he did not begin it. If he began, he completes it absolutely, because cutting then is invalidating. His statement: 'And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is made up individually, etc.' It is said: There is no real disagreement between them because the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) say: He is not obligated to make it up, but if he does, there is no harm. And Muhammad says: I prefer that he makes it up, and if he does not, nothing is against him. His statement: 'And not after noon, by agreement' i.e., according to the sound view. And it is said: He makes it up as a follow-up after it, but not intentionally, by consensus, as in al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan. His statement: 'And he makes up the sunnah, etc.' The use of 'qada' for what is not obligatory is metaphorical for similarity. Hence it is better to intend the sunnah, not qada (Qahistani). His statement: 'According to the sound view' And it is said: It is not made up at all because the continuity (al-muwazabah) upon it was only established before the obligatory prayer. His statement: 'In its time' And some scholars said: It is made up after any time if it is missed with it, because many things are established as a follow-up, even if not established intentionally, so it is in the sharh. His statement: 'Before the prayer of its shaf'' because the four precede the two, due to their precedence over the obligatory prayer which precedes them, and presenting them over the obligatory prayer is not possible, but over the sunnah it is no obstacle, so the four are given precedence, so it is in Sharh al-Majma'. His statement: 'The hadith of Aisha, etc.' And also so that they do not miss their place intentionally without necessity. His statement: 'And there is no prevention, etc.' Al-Sayyid said in his commentary: The restriction to those before Zuhr, and similarly Jumu'ah as in al-Durr, is to guard against those before Isha because they are recommended (mandubah) and thus not made up at all. Similarly those before Asr, rather even more so due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after it. End. If the author had said 'and there is no prevention of making up those before Isha after it', it would be clearer and more concise. His statement: 'Rather he caught its virtue' i.e., the multiplication. And in Sharh al-Maqdisi from al-Atqani: The one who is preceded (al-masbuq) catches the reward of the congregation, but not like the reward of one who catches the beginning of the prayer with the imam due to missing the first takbir. End. His statement: 'So if one swears, etc.' The example here is negative, while previously it was positive, indicating that there is no difference between affirmation and negation in the ruling. His statement: 'Shams al-A'imma chose, etc.' Weakens his statement due to their agreement in the chapter of oaths that if one swears not to eat this loaf, he does not break his oath unless he eats all of it, and that the majority does not stand in for the whole. His statement: 'He breaks his oath by catching it in the tashahhud' So mentioning the rak'ah in al-Kafi and others is not restrictive. Know that the place for this issue is the chapter of oaths; it is only mentioned here to clarify that there is no correlation between catching the virtue and catching the congregation. His statement: 'And one performs supererogatory prayers before the obligatory prayer, etc.' This expression indicates choice in the act, which is only apparent regarding non-emphasized (sunan ghayr mu'akkadah). As for the emphasized ones, one performs them without choice, if safe from losing the time, as stated by al-Sayyid. And in al-Bahr: If they are not emphasized, if they are recommended ones, it is recommended to perform them; otherwise, he has a choice. It could be said that what is meant in his statement is absolute permissibility, not equal on both sides, so it includes the emphasized and recommended. His statement: 'If safe from losing the time, etc.' If he had replaced it with 'if safe from losing the congregation,' it would be better, because if he knows to leave [the sunnah] when fearing loss of the congregation, then a fortiori he knows at fear of losing the time, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'Even if alone' is connected to his statement 'and one performs supererogatory prayer' (yatatawwa'). And it is said: One only performs the emphasized ones if he prays in congregation; if he is alone, he has a choice in them due to absence of transmitted continuity (al-muwazabah) from him (the Prophet) in other than performing with congregation. The first is more correct, said al-Sayyid. His statement: 'For it (the sunnah) was legislated' i.e., the sunnah, as made clear in the sharh. This is not apparent for the non-emphasized. His statement: 'And the one praying alone is more in need of that' due to the deficiency of his prayer in one respect. The demonstrative pronoun refers to cutting off the hope of shaytan. It includes that the one alone and others are equal in that, and that is only apparent for the complement of the deficiency. His statement: 'And it is more precautionary' i.e., the one alone performing the sunan; the pronoun refers to something understood from the context. His statement: 'The completion of its deficiency in our right' It could be said that completion is only for something that has been deficient, and then it is only in the posterior (after the fard) to complete what is deficient in the fard. And it can be said that the fard deficient is completed, even by what was done before it. The effect (athar) indicates that, for it has been reported that when he finds in prayer after prayer.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is a hashya (super-commentary) on Maraqi al-Falah, critically refining and expanding upon the rulings concerning sunnah prayers and their relationship with congregational prayer. The commentator, Al-Tahtawi, engages with earlier authorities like Al-Quduri, Al-Marghinani, and others.

The passage begins by establishing that the reward of congregational prayer far exceeds the virtue of the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah, using a mathematical analogy: the congregation increases the reward of the obligatory prayer by seven double degrees, while even one such degree is greater than the entire reward of the Fajr sunnah. This serves as a motivation to prioritize congregation.

Then it addresses the make-up (qada) of the Fajr sunnah. The base ruling is that it is only made up if missed together with the fard (obligatory) prayer, and only before noon. Imam Muhammad holds that it can be made up individually after sunrise but before noon; no make-up before sunrise or after noon by agreement. The commentary clarifies that there is no essential disagreement: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it not obligatory but permissible, while Muhammad recommends it.

Next, the passage discusses the sunnah before Zuhr. The sound view is that it is made up in its time before the two rak'ahs (shaf') that follow the fard. There is a dispute about order: some say the four rak'ahs should be prayed before the two, based on a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet would pray the four after the two if he missed them. This is preferred by Shaykh al-Islam. The same rule applies to the sunnah before Jumu'ah. There is no objection to making up the four before Isha after the Isha prayer.

The passage then moves to the topic of catching the congregation. If someone catches one or two rak'ahs of the congregational prayer, his oath (if he swore to pray in congregation) is nullified, and he obtains the virtue of the congregation even if he only catches the tashahhud. There is a discussion about catching the majority of the prayer (three out of four rak'ahs, etc.) and its effect on oaths, with Shams al-A'imma favoring that it breaks the oath because the majority takes the ruling of the whole. However, the preferred view is that it does not, as in the oath of eating a loaf.

Finally, the passage addresses supererogatory prayers before the obligatory prayer. One may perform them, whether emphasized or not, as long as there is no fear of losing the time. The one praying alone is more in need of them due to the deficiency in his prayer. The commentary includes a discussion on whether the sunnah is meant to cut off the hope of shaytan, and the virtue of completing deficiencies through sunan.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer; in this context, used metaphorically for sunnah prayers since they are not obligatory.
ضعف (di'f): A multiple or degree of reward; the text uses it to indicate that congregational prayer multiplies reward by seven times compared to individual prayer.
شفع (shaf'): The two rak'ahs that follow the obligatory prayer, specifically of Zuhr or other prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on making up the sunnah of Fajr if missed with the fard before noon?
A) It is obligatory to make it up.
B) It is prohibited to make it up.
C) It is recommended to make it up, according to Imam Muhammad.
D) It is not permissible under any condition.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Fajr is made up only as a recommended follow-up when missed together with the fard, before noon, and never as an obligation.

Fulfilling an Oath to Pray in Congregation
Ruling on oath to catch Zuhr or Maghrib with congregation and what constitutes 'catching'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fulfilling an oath to pray in congregation by catching part of the prayer, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Shams al-A'imma and the zahir al-jawab.

Core Idea
Part of a thing is not the thing: catching only part of a prayer does not fulfill an oath to pray it in congregation.

This lesson examines a nuanced case at the intersection of oaths and congregational prayer. When someone swears to pray a specific prayer in congregation but only catches a portion of that prayer with the congregation, does the oath break? The Hanafi school has a disagreement between the apparent answer (zahir al-jawab) and the view of Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani. Understanding this requires distinguishing between the virtue of congregation (fadl al-jama'ah) and the legal fulfillment of an oath.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario and Issue
A person swears an oath, e.g., 'By Allah, I will pray Zuhr in congregation.' He arrives late and catches only a part of the prayer, such as one rak'ah or even just the final tashahhud. The legal question: does catching part of the prayer fulfill the oath and break it (i.e., he has done what he swore), or does the oath remain unfulfilled?
The same scenario applies to Maghrib or any prayer with a defined number of rak'ahs.
2
Identify the Two Hanafi Positions
Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani holds that the oath is broken because the majority of the prayer takes the ruling of the whole (al-akthar lahukm al-kull). The apparent answer (zahir al-jawab) from the early authorities (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the oath is not broken because part of a thing is not the thing itself.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a disagreement between madhahib.
3
Examine the Proof for the Zahir al-Jawab
The zahir position is supported by an analogy with oaths about eating: if one swears not to eat a loaf of bread, eating only part does not break the oath; the agreement of the fuqaha in the Book of Oaths is that the majority does not stand for the whole in contracts and oaths.
This analogy is drawn from the same legal context (al-ayman).
4
Examine the Opposing Proof
Shams al-A'imma relies on the principle that the majority has the rule of the whole, citing its application in prayer: catching most of a rak'ah counts as catching that rak'ah. However, this principle is not universally applied in oaths.
The opposing view is a legitimate Hanafi position, though it is outweighed.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Practical Consequence
The author states 'wa huwa al-zahir' (and that is apparent), indicating that the zahir position is preferred. Therefore, the oath is not broken by catching part of the prayer. The swearer must either pray the entire prayer in congregation later or expiate for breaking the oath if he fails to do so.
Note the distinction: the virtue of congregation (fadl) is attained by catching any part, but legal fulfillment requires the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الظهر، أو المغرب جماعة اختار شمس الأئمة أنه يحنث لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وعلى ظاهر الجواب لا يحنث لأنه لم يصلها بل بعضها بجماعة، وبعض الشيء ليس بالشيء، وهو الظاهر، ولو قال : عبده حر إن أدرك الظهر فإنه يحنث بإدراك ركعة لأن إدراك الشيء بإدراك آخره يقال : أدرك أيامه أي آخرها كذا في الكافي وفي الخلاصة يحنث بإدراكه في التشهد الإثبات، والنفي في الحكم قوله : اختار شمس الأئمة (الخ يضعف قوله باتفاقهم في باب الأيمان أن لو حلف لا يأكل هذا الرغيف لا يحنث إلا بأكل كله، وأن الأكثر لا يقوم مقام الكل قوله : ( يحنث بإدراكه في التشهد فذكر الركعة في الكافي، وغيره ليس احترازياً، واعلم أن ذكر هذه المسألة محله كتاب الأيمان وإنما ذكرت هنا لبيان أنه لا تلازم بين إدراك الفضل، وإدراك الجماعة.
Concerning Zuhr or Maghrib with congregation, Shams al-A'imma chose that he breaks his oath because the majority has the rule of the whole. According to the apparent answer, he does not break his oath because he did not pray it (the whole) but rather part of it with congregation, and part of a thing is not the thing, and that is apparent. If he said: 'My slave is free if he catches Zuhr,' then he breaks the oath by catching a rak'ah because catching a thing is by catching its end; it is said 'he caught his days' meaning the end of them. Thus in al-Kafi and in al-Khulasa: he breaks his oath by catching it in the tashahhud. Affirmation and negation in the ruling. His saying: 'Shams al-A'imma chose' weakens his saying: 'by their agreement in the chapter of oaths that if he swore not to eat this loaf, he does not break it except by eating all of it, and that the majority does not stand in place of the all.' His saying: 'he breaks by catching it in tashahhud' – the mention of rak'ah in al-Kafi and others is not exclusive. Know that the place for this issue is the Book of Oaths, and it is mentioned here only to show that there is no necessary connection between catching virtue and catching congregation.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses a case from the Book of Prayer but properly belongs to the Book of Oaths. It concerns a person who swears, for example, 'By Allah, I will pray Zuhr in congregation' but only catches part of the prayer with the congregation (e.g., one rak'ah or even just the tashahhud). The author presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani (a leading Hanafi scholar) held that the oath is broken because the majority of the prayer constitutes the whole (al-akthar lahukm al-kull). However, the apparent answer (zahir al-jawab) from the founding authorities (Abu Hanifa, etc.) is that the oath is not broken because part of a thing is not the thing. The text supports this latter view, citing the analogy of swearing not to eat a loaf of bread—one does not break the oath by eating part of it. The text also mentions that if one swears 'My slave is free if he catches Zuhr,' catching one rak'ah suffices because the complete prayer is defined by its end (like 'catching the day' means its end). This shows a nuance: the rule differs for catching Zuhr (a prayer) versus catching a community prayer (jamā‘ah). The key point is that virtue (fadl) of congregation attaches to catching any part, but the oath's legal consequence (hanth) requires the whole act.

Key Terms
الأكثر حكم الكل (al-akthar hukm al-kull): A legal principle that the majority of a thing takes the ruling of the whole, used here by Shams al-A'imma to hold that catching most of the prayer breaks the oath.
ظاهر الجواب (zahir al-jawab): The apparent or preferred answer from the early Hanafi authorities (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), as opposed to a minority view.
إدراك الفضل (idrak al-fadl): Catching the virtue or reward of the congregation, which is attained by catching any part of the congregational prayer, even a single takbir. This is distinct from legally fulfilling an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'By Allah, I will pray Zuhr in congregation' and catches only the final tashahhud with the imam, what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling?
A) His oath is broken, and he must expiate.
B) His oath is not broken, and he must pray the entire Zuhr in congregation later or expiate for the broken oath.
C) His oath is not broken, and no further action is required because catching tashahhud is enough to fulfill the oath as catching the end is catching the whole.
D) The oath is void because it includes a condition (congregation) that is not essential.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an oath to pray a specific prayer in congregation requires the entire prayer to be performed with the congregation; catching only part does not fulfill the oath, even though one obtains the virtue of congregation for that part.
