Performing Sunnah Before Fard: Conditions and Rulings
Ruling on sunnah before fard with conditions and intra-Hanafi refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi should perform sunnah prayers before the fard prayer and identify the ruling for the munfarid.

Core Idea
Perform sunnah before fard only if safe from losing time or congregation; the munfarid is especially recommended to do so.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi ruling on supererogatory prayers offered before the obligatory prayer. It distinguishes between emphasized and non-emphasized sunnahs, and discusses the crucial condition of safety from losing the fard time or congregation. The commentary also addresses the case of one praying alone, settling a difference of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of sunnah
Determine whether the sunnah is mu'akkad (emphasized) or ghayr mu'akkad (non-emphasized). This affects the ruling: mu'akkad must be performed if safe, ghayr mu'akkad is optional with recommendation.
Examples: two rak'ahs before Fajr are mu'akkad; other nawafil before Zuhr may be ghayr mu'akkad.
2
Check the condition of safety
Ensure that performing the sunnah will not cause loss of the fard time or the congregation (if praying in congregation). Safety from time loss is primary; safety from congregation loss is even more appropriate.
If either is at risk, it is not permissible to perform the sunnah.
3
Analyze the case of the munfarid
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some said the munfarid only prays mu'akkad if with congregation; the correct view (al-awwal asahh) is that he performs it even alone.
The munfarid is more in need of the sunnah to complete the deficiency of his prayer and cut the hope of shaytan.
4
Apply the ruling to other scenarios
Consider the case of small impurity: if removing it would cause loss of congregation, one may skip cleaning and pray with that congregation? The text says it is better to clean and pray with another congregation, ensuring validity by agreement.
The principle: do not occupy yourself with what causes loss of the fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويتطوع قبل الفرض الخ) هذه العبارة تدل على التخيير في الفعل، وهو إنما يظهر في غير المؤكد أما المأكد فيأتي به من غير تخيير ان أمن فوت الوقت أفاده السيد، وفي البحر وإن لم تكن مؤكدة، فإن كانت من المستحبات استحب الإتيان بها، وإلا فهو مخير، وقد يقال أن المراد في كلامه الجواز المطلق لا مستوى الطرفين فيلاقي المؤكدة والمستحبة. قوله : (إن أمن فوت الوقت الخ) لو أبدله بقوله : إن أمن فوت الجماعة لكان أولى لأنه إذا علم الترك عند خوف فوت الجماعة، فلأن يعلم عند خوف فوت الوقت بالطريق الأولى، أفاده السيد قوله : (ولو منفرداً) وصل بقوله، ويتطوع وقيل : إنما يأتي بالمؤكدة ان صلي بجماعة، وإن كان منفرداً يخير فيها لعدم نقل المواظبة عنه في غير الأداء بجماعة، والأول أصح قاله السيد قوله : (فإنها شرعت أي فإن السنة كما صرح به في الشرح، وهذا لا يظهر في غير المؤكد قوله : (والمنفرد في ذلك أحوج لنقصان صلاته من وجه واسم الإشارة يرجع إلى قطع طمع الشيطان، وفيه أن المنفرد وغيره في ذلك سواء، ولا يظهر ذلك إلا في المكمل للنقص (۱) . قوله : (وهو أحوط) أي إتيان المنفرد بالسنن فالضمير يرجع إلى معلوم من المقام . قوله : التكميل نقصها في حقنا قد يقال ان التكميل إنما يكون لشيء قد نقص، وحينئذ فلا يكون إلا في البعدية فتكمل ما نقص من الفرض، ويمكن أن يقال أنه الفرض ناقصاً يكمل، ولو بما فعل قبله والأثر يدل عليه فإنه ورد أنه إذا وجد في صلاة بعد صلاة  طمع للشيطان فيها (وإلا) أي إن لم يأمن بأن يفوته الوقت أو الجماعة بالتنفل، أو إزالة نجس قليل (فلا) يتطوع، ولا يغسل لأنّ الاشتغال بما يفوّت الأداء لا يجوز وإن كان يدرك جماعة أخرى فالأفضل غسل ثوبه واستقبال الصلاة لتكون صحيحة اتفاقاً قوله: (اتفاقاً) فإن الإمام الشافعي يحكم بفسادها بقليل النجاسة.
His saying: 'And he performs supererogatory prayers before the obligatory prayer, etc.' This expression indicates choice in action, and that is only apparent for non-emphasized sunnahs. As for the emphasized, he performs it without choice if safe from losing time, as stated by al-Sayyid. In al-Bahr: even if it is not emphasized, if it is among the recommended, it is recommended to perform it; otherwise, he has a choice. It may be said that the intended meaning in his speech is absolute permissibility, not equal on both sides, so it includes the emphasized and the recommended. His saying: 'if safe from losing time' – if he were to substitute 'if safe from losing congregation' it would be more appropriate, because if he knows he will leave it when fearing the loss of congregation, then he will know it when fearing the loss of time as a primary matter, as stated by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'even if alone' is connected to his saying 'and he performs supererogatory prayers'. And it is said: he only performs the emphasized if he prays with congregation; if he is alone, he has a choice in them due to the lack of transmission of his constant practice when not performing with congregation. The first is more correct, as stated by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'for it (the sunnah) was legislated' – i.e., the sunnah, as stated clearly in the sharh. And this is not apparent for non-emphasized. His saying: 'and the one alone is more in need of that' due to the deficiency of his prayer in one respect. The demonstrative pronoun refers to cutting the hope of shaytan. And it is said that the one alone and others are equal in that, and that is only apparent for the one who completes the deficiency. His saying: 'and it is more precautionary' i.e., the performance of sunnahs by the one alone, so the pronoun refers to something known from the context. His saying: 'the completion of deficiency in our right' – it may be said that completion is only for something that has been deficient, and then it is only in the after-prayer (sunnah ba'diyyah) to complete what is deficient from the fard. And it can be said that the fard is deficient and is completed by what is done before it, and the effect indicates that, for it has been reported that if he is found to have prayer after prayer, there is hope for shaytan in it. (And otherwise) i.e., if he is not safe from losing the time or congregation by performing supererogatory prayers, or removing a small impurity, (then he does not) perform supererogatory prayers, nor wash it, because occupying oneself with what causes loss of performance is not permissible. And if he can catch another congregation, it is better to wash his garment and face the prayer so that it will be valid by agreement. His saying: 'by agreement' – indeed Imam al-Shafi'i rules that it is invalidated by a small impurity.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains the ruling on performing sunnah (nafl) prayers before the obligatory (fard) prayer. The matn (Maraqi al-Falah) stated that one performs supererogatory prayers before the fard, both mu'akkad and ghayr mu'akkad, whether resident or traveling, if one is safe from missing the time, even if praying alone. The hashiah clarifies: For mu'akkad sunnah (like the two rak'ahs before Fajr), it is not a matter of choice; one must perform them if safe. For non-mu'akkad, there is choice (takhayyur). The commentary also discusses the condition of safety from losing congregation, noting that safety from losing time is the primary consideration, but safety from losing congregation is more appropriate. Regarding a person praying alone (munfarid), there is a difference: some say he only prays the mu'akkad if he prayed with congregation, otherwise he has a choice. The correct view is that he prays the mu'akkad even if alone. The wisdom behind sunnah before fard is to cut the hope of shaytan, as a hadith indicates: shaytan hopes that one will omit the fard, but if one prays sunnah, shaytan despairs. The munfarid is more in need of this because his prayer is incomplete in some way. The passage also addresses cases where performing sunnah or removing impurity may cause loss of time or congregation; in such cases, one should not do it. If one can catch another congregation, it is better to clean the impurity and pray with that congregation, even if it means missing the current congregation, because the prayer will be valid by agreement (ittifaq), though Imam Shafi'i differs regarding small impurity.

Key Terms
المؤكد (al-mu'akkad): Emphasized sunnah prayer, such as the two rak'ahs before Fajr, which the Prophet regularly performed and did not leave except rarely.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): One who prays alone, not in congregation. The text discusses whether he should still perform sunnah before fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what should a person praying alone (munfarid) do regarding the sunnah mu'akkadah before the fard prayer?
A) He has a choice, it is not recommended.
B) He should perform it, as it completes the deficiency of his prayer.
C) He should not perform it, because the Prophet did not consistently do so when alone.
D) He may perform it only if he fears losing the fard time.

Key Takeaway
The mu'akkad sunnah before fard is performed even by the munfarid, provided safety from losing time or congregation; for non-mu'akkad, it is optional.

Catching the Rak'ah by Joining the Imam in Ruku'
Ruling on catching the rak'ah with the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching the rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku', and identify the mufta bihi position among the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
You must participate in a part of the ruku' before the imam raises his head to catch the rak'ah.

A common scenario in congregational prayer is a latecomer joining the imam while he is already in ruku'. Many worshippers assume that simply bending down as the imam rises counts for the rak'ah. This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah clarifies the precise condition: actual participation in the ruku' movement is required, and the Hanafi school has refined this through multiple opinions and a final tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The latecomer (masbuq) joins the imam when the imam is already in ruku'. The question: has he caught that rak'ah?
2
State the primary ruling from the matn
The matn states that if the latecomer bows before the imam raises his head, he catches the rak'ah. The hashiah elaborates on the conditions.
The takbir must be said while standing for obligatory prayers.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi differences
The hashiah lists several opinions: (1) participation in any part of ruku' is required; (2) beginning to bend as imam starts raising counts; (3) participation in the raising before the imam stands fully; (4) the entire ruku' must be shared; (5) the amount of one tasbihah.
These represent different interpretations of the same hadith.
4
Apply the tarjih
Ibn Amir Haj finds the first view (participation in any part) more appropriate; al-Halabi declares it the most correct.
This is the mufta bihi position: participation in any part of the ruku' suffices.
5
Verify with the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited: 'If you catch the imam bowing and you bow before he raises his head, you have caught the rak'ah.' The 'kaf' in 'kama warada' indicates that the hadith is the cause (illah) for the ruling.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, but it is the primary evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فكبر) أي قائماً فلو كبر منحنياً إن كان إلى الركوع أقرب لا يصح شروعه، وظاهر ذلك، ولو كان في النقل الذي لا يشترط له القيام كما تفيده عبارة الزاهدي لأنه ليس بافتتاح قائماً ولا قاعداً وقوله : راكعاً احترز به عما لو أدركه في القيام ولم يركع . معه فإنه يصير مدركاً لها فيكون لاحقاً فيأتي بها قبل الفراغ سيد عن الدر. قوله : (أو لم يقف، بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه) بحيث لم تتحقق مشاركته له فيه فإنه يصح اقتداؤه، ولكنه لم يدرك الركعة حيث لم يدركه في جزء من الركوع قبل رفع رأسه منه، وقيل : إذا شرع في الانحطاط وشرع الإمام في الرفع فقد أدركه في الركوع أضاً، ويعتد بتلك الركعة ، وقيل : إذا شاركه في الرفع قبل أن يستتم قائماً يعتد بها، وإن قل، وقيل: يصير مدركاً تلك الركعة ما لم يشارك الإمام في الركوع كله، وقيل في مقدار تسبيحة. قال ابن أمير حاج والأول أوجه وقال الحلبي : هو الأصح لأن الشرط المشاركة في جزء من الركوع، وإن قل، والحاصل أنه إذا وصل إلى حد الركوع قبل أن يخرج الإمام من حد الركوع، فقد أدرك معه الركعة، وإلا فلا كما يفيده أثر ابن عمر كذا في الحلبي من صفة الصلاة وإنما ذكرنا هذه الأقاويل لأن الناس يقع منهم الاقتداء في الركوع كثيراً من غير إدراك جزء منه، ويعتدون به فهم في ذلك موافقون لبعض أقوال العلماء قوله : (فرفع الإمام رأسه مراده أنه . رفع قبل أن يشاركه المؤتم في جزء من الركوع، وإلا فظاهر التعبير بالفاء أن الرفع تحقق بعد الإنحطاط، وحينئذ تحقق المشاركة، فتكون الصلاة صحيحة قوله : (كما ورد عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما ولفظه إذا أدركت الإمام راكعاً فركعت قبل أن يرفع رأسه فقد أدركت الركعة وإن رفع قبل أن تركع فقد فاتتك الركعة اهـ والكاف في كما ورد بمعنى لام التعليل.
His saying: 'and he says the takbir' – i.e., standing. So if he says the takbir while bending, if he is closer to ruku', his commencement is not valid, and that is apparent. Even if it is in a supererogatory prayer for which standing is not a condition, as is indicated by the statement of al-Zahidi, because it is not an opening takbir while standing nor while sitting. His saying: 'while he (the imam) is in ruku'' – this excludes the case where he catches him in qiyam and does not bow with him; then he becomes a latecomer (lahiq) and performs it (the missed rak'ah) before finishing (the prayer) – from al-Durr via al-Sayyid. His saying: 'or he does not stand, but rather bends down immediately after his tahrimah, and then the imam raises his head' such that his participation with him in it is not realized; then his following (iqtida') is valid, but he has not caught the rak'ah because he did not catch him in any part of the ruku' before his raising his head from it. And it is said: if he begins to bend down and the imam begins to raise, then he has caught him in ruku' as well, and that rak'ah counts. And it is said: if he participates with him in the raising before he (the imam) becomes fully standing, it counts, even if little. And it is said: he becomes one who has caught that rak'ah as long as he does not participate with the imam in the entire ruku'. And it is said: (the condition is) the amount of one tasbihah. Ibn Amir Haj said the first is more appropriate, and al-Halabi said it is the most correct because the condition is participation in a part of the ruku', even if little. In summary: if he reaches the limit of ruku' before the imam leaves the limit of ruku', then he has caught the rak'ah with him; otherwise, no, as is indicated by the effect of Ibn Umar. Thus in al-Halabi in the description of the prayer. And we have mentioned these opinions because people often follow the imam in ruku' without catching a part of it and consider it valid, and in that they follow some of the sayings of the scholars. His saying: 'then the imam raises his head' – his meaning is that he raises before the follower participates in any part of the ruku'. Otherwise, the apparent expression with 'fa' indicates that the raising occurs after the bending, and then participation is realized, so the prayer is valid. His saying: 'as has been reported from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, and its wording: If you catch the imam bowing and you bow before he raises his head, then you have caught the rak'ah, and if he raises before you bow, then the rak'ah has been missed.' And the 'kaf' in 'kama warada' is in the sense of 'lam al-ta'lil' (indicating causation).
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains the ruling on a latecomer (masbuq) who joins the imam while the imam is in ruku'. The main ruling from the matn is that if one catches the imam in ruku' and bows before the imam raises his head, he has caught the rak'ah. The hashiah elaborates on several details: (1) The takbir (tahrimah) must be said while standing; if one says it while bending closer to ruku', it is invalid for the obligatory prayer (and for nafl if standing is a condition). (2) If the latecomer catches the imam standing (qiyam) before ruku' and does not bow with him, he is a 'lahiq' (one who joins later but catches the entire prayer) and must make up the missed rak'ah after the imam finishes. (3) There are multiple opinions within the Hanafi school about exactly when the latecomer catches the ruku': the most correct view (as per al-Halabi) is that he must participate in at least a part of the ruku' before the imam raises his head. If he only starts to bow as the imam is raising, the rak'ah is not caught, according to the authentic report from Ibn Umar. The text notes that many laypeople mistakenly think they have caught the rak'ah even when they don't join any part of the ruku', and some scholars have accommodated this by stating that catching the ruku' in its entirety is not required; rather, a small part suffices. The key principle is that if the follower reaches the limit of ruku' (i.e., his back is level) before the imam leaves that position, he has caught the rak'ah. The hadith of Ibn Umar is the primary evidence, and it is interpreted as meaning that the condition is participation in any part of the ruku'.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the imam after the prayer has started; here specifically one who joins during ruku'.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): One who catches the imam in qiyam (standing) and bows later; he is considered to have caught the entire prayer and must make up what he missed later.
حد الركوع (hadd al-ruk'u): The limit or position of ruku', i.e., when the back is level and the hands are on the knees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi view, what is the minimum requirement for a latecomer to catch the rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku'?
A) He must say the takbir while standing.
B) He must participate in any part of the ruku' before the imam raises his head.
C) He must say the entire tasbihah of ruku' with the imam.
D) He must begin to bend as soon as he sees the imam in ruku'.

Key Takeaway
The key takeaway is that catching the rak'ah requires actual participation in a part of the ruku' movement before the imam begins to rise; merely bending after he starts to raise is insufficient.

Catching the Rak'ah When Joining the Imam Late
Commentary on conditions and disagreements regarding catching the rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition for catching the rak'ah when joining the imam late and distinguish the relied-upon position from minority views within the school.

Core Idea
Catching the rak'ah requires sharing any part of ruku' before the imam raises his head.

When you join the congregation after the imam has begun ruku', do you still get that rak'ah? The answer depends on timing: you must perform ruku' before the imam lifts his head. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi refines the condition by presenting several scholarly opinions and settling on the position that any part of ruku' suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central legal question
What is the precise condition for a latecomer to catch a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku'? The answer determines whether that rak'ah counts or must be made up.
2
Extract the primary dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar states: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and perform ruku' before he raises his head, you have caught the rak'ah.' Identify the operative phrase 'before he raises his head.'
Hadith is ahad, but relied upon.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
List the four opinions reported in the text: (1) any part of ruku', (2) the measure of one tasbih, (3) participating in the raising as well, (4) as long as not left the ruku' completely.
These are transmitted as 'qila' opinions.
4
Analyze the tarjih mechanism
Ibn Amir Haj and al-Halabi prefer the first opinion (any part suffices). Understand their reasoning: the hadith does not specify a duration, and the condition is simply participation before the imam's exit from ruku'.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider a follower who bends down just as the imam begins to rise, but reaches the ruku' posture before the imam fully straightens. According to the relied-upon view, he caught the rak'ah.
Contrast with a scenario where he starts bending after the imam has already left the ruku' limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا) أي إن لم يأمن بأن يفوته الوقت أو الجماعة بالتنفل، أو إزالة نجس قليل (فلا) يتطوع، ولا يغسل لأنّ الاشتغال بما يفوّت الأداء لا يجوز وإن كان يدرك جماعة أخرى فالأفضل غسل ثوبه واستقبال الصلاة لتكون صحيحة اتفاقاً (ومن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع الإمام رأسه من الركوع أو لم يقف، بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل ركوع المؤتم لم يدرك (الركعة كما ورد عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما. قوله: (أو لم يقف، بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه) بحيث لم تتحقق مشاركته له فيه فإنه يصح اقتداؤه، ولكنه لم يدرك الركعة حيث لم يدركه في جزء من الركوع قبل رفع رأسه منه، وقيل: إذا شرع في الانحطاط وشرع الإمام في الرفع فقد أدركه في الركوع أيضاً، ويعتد بتلك الركعة، وقيل: إذا شاركه في الرفع قبل أن يستتم قائماً يعتد بها، وإن قل، وقيل: يصير مدركاً تلك الركعة ما لم يشارك الإمام في الركوع كله، وقيل: في مقدار تسبيحة. قال ابن أمير حاج والأول أوجه وقال الحلبي: هو الأصح لأن الشرط المشاركة في جزء من الركوع، وإن قل، والحاصل أنه إذا وصل إلى حد الركوع قبل أن يخرج الإمام من حد الركوع، فقد أدرك معه الركعة، وإلا فلا كما يفيده أثر ابن عمر. قوله: (فرفع الإمام رأسه) مراده أنه رفع قبل أن يشاركه المؤتم في جزء من الركوع، وإلا فظاهر التعبير بالفاء أن الرفع تحقق بعد الإنحطاط، وحينئذ تحقق المشاركة، فتكون الصلاة صحيحة. قوله: (كما ورد عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما) ولفظه إذا أدركت الإمام راكعاً فركعت قبل أن يرفع رأسه فقد أدركت الركعة وإن رفع قبل أن تركع فقد فاتتك الركعة. ولا يشترط تكبيرتان للإحرام والركوع ولو كبر ينوي الركوع لا جاز، ولغت نيته، وإذا وجد الإمام ساجداً تجب مشاركته فيه فيخر ساجداً وإن لم له صلاته، فلو ركع وحده ثم شاركه في السجدتين لا تفسد صلاته ولا يحسب له ذلك وإن لم يشاركه إلا في الثانية بطلت صلاته والفرق أنه في الأولى لم يزد إلا ركوعاً وزيادته لا تضر وفي الثانية زاد ركعة وهي مفسدة. ولو أدركه جالساً للقعود الأخير واستمر قائماً وقرأ فما وجد قبل فراغ الإمام من التشهد لا يكون معتبراً. وإن ركع المقتدي قبل إمامه وكان ركوعه بعد قراءة الإمام ما تجوز به الصلاة وهو آية فأدركه إمامه فيه صح ركوعه، وكره لوجود المشاركة والمسابقة. وإلا أي وإن لم يدركه الإمام أو أدركه لكن لم يكن قرأ المفروض قبل ركوع المقتدي لا يصح ركوعه لكونه قبل أوانه.
And otherwise, meaning if he does not feel safe that the time or the congregation will be lost by supererogatory prayer or by removing a minor impurity, then do not perform supererogatory prayers and do not wash, because occupying oneself with what loses the performance is not permissible. And if he is able to catch another congregation, it is better to wash his garment and begin the prayer so that it is valid by agreement. And whoever catches his imam in ruku', then he says takbir and stands until the imam raises his head from ruku', or he does not stand but rather bends down immediately upon his ihram, and then the imam raises his head before the follower's ruku', he does not catch the rak'ah as narrated from Ibn Umar. His statement: 'or he did not stand, but rather bent down immediately upon his ihram and the imam raised his head' such that his participation in it was not realized, then his following is valid, but he did not catch the rak'ah because he did not catch him in a part of the ruku' before he raised his head from it. And it is said: if he started bending down and the imam started raising, he caught him in ruku' as well, and that rak'ah is counted. And it is said: if he participated with him in raising before he fully stood up, it is counted, even if little. And it is said: he becomes a catcher of that rak'ah as long as he did not participate with the imam in all of the ruku'. And it is said: [the minimum] is the measure of one tasbih. Ibn Amir Haj said: the first is more appropriate. Al-Halabi said: it is the most correct because the condition is participation in a part of ruku', even if little. The summary: if he reaches the limit of ruku' before the imam leaves the limit of ruku', then he caught the rak'ah with him; otherwise no, as indicated by the athar of Ibn Umar. His statement: 'then the imam raised his head' means he raised before the follower participated in a part of ruku'; otherwise, the apparent meaning of the fa' is that the raising occurred after the bending down, and then participation is realized, so the prayer is valid. His statement: 'as narrated from Ibn Umar' and its wording: if you catch the imam in ruku' and you perform ruku' before he raises his head, you have caught the rak'ah; if he raises before you perform ruku', you have missed the rak'ah. And two takbirs for ihram and ruku' are not required; if he says takbir intending ruku', it is not permissible and his intention is void. And if he finds the imam in sajdah, it is obligatory to participate with him in it, so he falls into sajdah even if it is not counted as his prayer. If he performed ruku' alone then participated with him in the two prostrations, his prayer is not invalidated and it is not counted for him; if he did not participate with him except in the second, his prayer is invalid. The difference: in the first case he only added a ruku', and his addition does not harm; in the second case he added a rak'ah, which is invalidating. And if he catches him sitting for the final sitting, and he continues standing and recites, then what he did before the imam finished the tashahhud is not considered. And if the follower performed ruku' before his imam, and his ruku' was after the imam's recitation of what validates the prayer, i.e., one verse, and his imam catches him in it, his ruku' is valid but disliked, because participation and precedence occurred. Otherwise, i.e., if the imam did not catch him or caught him but had not recited the obligatory before the follower's ruku', his ruku' is not valid because it is before its proper time.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement addressing rulings on the latecomer (masbuq) in congregational prayer. It begins by stating that if a person fears losing the entire prayer time or the congregation by engaging in supererogatory acts or removing a minor impurity, he should not do so, as occupying oneself with what causes loss of the obligatory performance is impermissible. If another congregation is expected, washing the garment and starting fresh is superior. The main focus is the condition for catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku'. The follower must say takbir while standing, then either stand until the imam raises his head or bend down immediately. If the imam raises his head before the follower bends down, the rak'ah is not caught, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. The commentary then presents multiple opinions (aqwal) among Hanafi scholars on the minimal part of ruku' that must be caught: some say any part, some say the measure of one tasbih, etc. The preferred view (as stated by Ibn Amir Haj and Al-Halabi) is that participation in any part of ruku' suffices, as long as the follower reaches the limit of ruku' before the imam leaves it. The text also clarifies that two takbirs (for ihram and ruku') are not required; if one intends ruku' with the takbir, the intention is void and it counts as takbir al-ihram. If the follower finds the imam in sajdah, it is obligatory to join even though it does not count as a rak'ah; missing sajdah altogether invalidates the prayer. When joining the imam in the final sitting, the follower must not perform extra rak'ahs before the imam finishes. Finally, if the follower precedes the imam in ruku' after the imam recited one verse, the ruku' is valid but disliked; otherwise it is invalid. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the Hanafi position and cites differences (e.g., with Shafi'i on validity of prayer with minor impurity). The authority weight is from the later fatwa works (mutakhkhirin) and the relied-upon position is that catching any part of ruku' suffices.

Key Terms
إدراك الركعة (idrak al-rak'ah): Joining the imam while he is in ruku' such that the follower performs ruku' with him before the imam raises his head.
مقتدي (muqtadi): A follower who is performing prayer behind an imam.
قيل (qila): It is said; used to introduce alternative opinions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, the minimum condition for catching the rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku' is that the follower must...
A) perform ruku' for at least one tasbih.
B) participate in any part of ruku' before the imam raises his head.
C) join the imam while still standing and then go into ruku' with him.
D) make both takbirs for ihram and ruku'.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that any part of ruku' suffices to catch the rak'ah, as long as it occurs before the imam raises his head.

Latecomer Joining Imam in Ruku' and Sujud
Explains conditions for catching a rak'ah and rulings on joining imam in sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for catching a rak'ah and apply the ruling on joining the imam in sujud, distinguishing valid actions from invalid ones.

Core Idea
Catching ruku' catches the rak'ah; joining in sujud is wajib but does not count as a rak'ah.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashiah refines key rulings for the latecomer (masbuq) in congregational prayer. You must understand when a rak'ah is counted and how to follow the imam when joining mid-prayer. The hadith 'Whoever catches the ruku' has caught the rak'ah' is central, but its application has nuances, especially regarding prostration and the number of takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for catching a rak'ah
Locate the statement: 'sharing part of the standing or part of what has the ruling of standing, which is bowing'. Recognize that catching even part of ruku' suffices, and this is the Hanafi position.
This is a key difference from other schools.
2
Examine the ruling on two takbirs
Note that the latecomer catching the imam in ruku' does not need two separate takbirs; one takbir suffices. Understand the reasoning: the opening takbir covers what is close to it, unlike when joining in prostration or sitting.
Contrary to some scholars (possibly Shafi'i).
3
Analyze the ruling on joining the imam in sujud
Read the hadith and the commentator's emphasis: joining the imam in prostration is obligatory (wajib) even though it does not count as a rak'ah. The follower must prostrate and later make up the missed rak'ah.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud.
4
Distinguish the scenarios of joining in only one sajdah
If the follower joins only in the second sajdah (without the first), his prayer is invalidated because he effectively adds an extra rak'ah. If he joins in both sajdahs after bowing alone, it is valid but disliked.
Difference lies in adding a rak'ah vs. adding a ruku'.
5
Apply the ruling on preceding the imam in ruku'
If the follower bows before the imam, but after the imam's recitation of a verse, and then the imam catches him in that bowing, the bowing is valid but makruh tahrimi. Otherwise, it is invalid.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa holds prostration before imam's raising invalid.

So the condition for catching the rak'ah is either sharing with the imam in part of the standing, or part of what has the ruling of standing, which is bowing. And two takbirs (for ihram and ruku') are not required. And if he says the takbir intending ruku', it is not valid and his intention is void. And if he finds the imam prostrating, it is obligatory for him to join him in it, so he falls into prostration even if it does not count for his prayer. So if he bowed alone and then joined him in the two prostrations, his prayer is not invalidated, and it is not counted for him. But if he does not join him except in the second, his prayer is invalidated. The difference is that in the first he added only one bowing, and his addition does not harm, but in the second he added a rak'ah, which is invalidating. And if he catches him sitting for the final tashahhud and he remains standing and recites, what he does before the imam finishes the tashahhud is not considered. And if the follower bows before his imam, and his bowing is after the imam's recitation of what suffices for prayer (which is a verse), and then the imam catches him in it (i.e., in his bowing), then his bowing is valid but disliked, due to the existence of sharing and preceding. Otherwise—that is, if the imam does not catch him, or catches him but he had not recited the obligatory before the follower's bowing—then his bowing is not valid because it was before its proper time. And it is not required to have two takbirs for ihram and ruku'; the one who catches the imam in ruku' does not need two takbirs, contrary to some. This is more appropriate than the author's expression. And in Ibn Amir Hajj, from al-Khaniyah and al-Muhit: this is different from catching him in prostration and sitting, for he says the takbir for opening and another for lowering. Perhaps the reason is that the first is close to bowing, so the opening takbir said while standing suffices for what is near it, but not the takbir for lowering mentioned. He said: (and his intention is void) so it falls as for opening because the integral in its place does not change by intention. Thus in al-Fath. And in al-Bahr: if he catches him in bowing, he should estimate; if his stronger opinion is that if he were to recite the thana', he would catch some of the bowing, he does it; otherwise not. And the correct view is that he does not do it after the imam starts recitation, even silently. He said: (and if he finds the imam prostrating, it is obligatory for him to join him in it) the apparent meaning of his expression is obligation even if he intended bowing and missed it. It is supported by the hadith of Abu Dawud from Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When you come to prayer and we are prostrating, then prostrate, and do not count it as anything. And whoever catches the bowing has caught the rak'ah.' And the expression of the Sharh: It is obligatory for the follower, if he misses the bowing, to follow the imam in prostration, even if it is not counted for him in his prayer. And if he does not follow him, and waits until he stands and then follows him in the rest of the prayer, and makes up what he missed of rak'ahs after the imam finishes, his prayer is valid, because he prays that missed rak'ah with its two prostrations. He said: (and if he does not join him except in the second) i.e., the second prostration without the first. He said: (and his addition does not harm) i.e., the harm of invalidity, even though it is disliked because it is separation from the imam after following him. He said: 'fama wajada' means what he does of standing and recitation as a follower. He said: (is not considered) because while the imam remains in his prayer, he is following him, so what he does while following in his state of separation to make up what preceded is not considered. He said: (and it is a verse (آفة؟)) i.e., the great imam (likely meaning the imam's recitation of a verse). He said: (and it is disliked) i.e., prohibitively disliked due to the prohibition in his saying: 'Do not precede me in bowing and prostration.' He said: 'wujud al-musharakah wa al-musabaqah' is a justification for validity and dislike in the manner of ordered distribution. So he must bow a second time after him; if he does not do so and leaves his prayer, it is invalidated. And if he prostrates before his imam—if it is after the imam raises from bowing, and then the imam joins him in prostration—it is valid. But if it is before the imam raises from bowing, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is not sufficient for him, because it is before its proper time with respect to the imam. And similarly regarding... (unclear). And if the imam lengthens the prostration and the follower raises, then prostrates while the imam is prostrating: if he intends the second and following, it counts as the first, just as if he intended it or had no intention, giving precedence to following. But if he intends the second only, it counts as the second. If the imam catches him in it, it is valid. And by analogy to what is narrated from the imam regarding prostration before the imam raises, it must be that it is not permissible because it is before its proper time, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah) from al-Tahtawi on the rulings of a latecomer (masbuq) joining congregational prayer. The author first establishes the condition for catching a rak'ah: sharing a part of qiyam (standing) or what has the ruling of qiyam, which is ruku' (bowing). This means that if a latecomer joins the imam while the imam is in ruku' (bowing) and catches even part of it, he has caught that rak'ah. The text then discusses various scenarios. First, the latecomer does not need to recite two takbirs (one for ihram and one for ruku') if he catches the imam in ruku'; a single takbir suffices for both. However, if he intends ruku' with the takbir, it is not valid and the intention is void; the takbir counts as the opening takbir only. Next, if the latecomer finds the imam prostrating (sajdah), he must join the imam in prostration even though it does not count as a rak'ah for him. The hadith from Abu Dawud supports this: 'When you come to prayer and we are prostrating, then prostrate, and do not count it as anything. Whoever catches the bowing has caught the rak'ah.' Thus, the latecomer should follow the imam in sujūd, and later make up the missed rak'ah. The text distinguishes between missing the first sajdah and the second: if he joins only in the second sajdah (without the first), his prayer is invalidated because he has effectively added an extra rak'ah, which is invalidating. If he joins in both sajdahs after having bowed alone, the prayer is valid albeit disliked due to separation from the imam. The passage also addresses the case where the follower bows before the imam. If the imam has already recited the minimum (a verse) and then catches the follower in the bowing, the follower's bowing is valid but disliked (makruh tahrimi). If the imam has not recited the minimum, the follower's bowing is invalid because it occurred before its proper time. The discussion includes intra-Hanafi rulings: from Abu Hanifa, if the follower prostrates before the imam raises from ruku', it is not valid. But if he prostrates after the imam raises and then the imam joins him, it is valid. There are details about intention: if the follower raises from sajdah and then prostrates again while the imam is still prostrating, the intention determines which sajdah it counts as, with precedence given to following. Throughout, the commentary uses terms like 'adā' (performance) and qaḍā' (make-up), and distinguishes between acts that invalidate (mufsidāt) and those that are disliked. The overall ruling (mufta bihi) emphasizes following the imam and avoiding preceding him.

Key Terms
مشاركة الإمام (mushārakat al-imām): The follower's act of sharing a part of the imam's prayer posture (qiyam, ruku', sujud) to catch the rak'ah or maintain following.
قبل أوانه (qabla awānihi): An action performed before its legally prescribed time, e.g., bowing before the imam has completed his recitation or before raising from bowing.
تكبيرتي الإحرام والركوع (takbīratā al-ihrām wa al-rukū'): The two takbirs: the opening takbir (tahrīmah) and the takbir for bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A latecomer enters the mosque and finds the imam in prostration (sajdah). According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Wait until the imam stands up to join the next rak'ah.
B) Join the imam in prostration, but it does not count as a rak'ah.
C) Join the imam in prostration and it counts as a rak'ah.
D) Say the opening takbir and then wait without prostrating.

Key Takeaway
The key Hanafi rule: catching the imam in ruku' counts as a rak'ah; joining in sujud is obligatory but does not count, and preceding the imam is invalid without proper conditions.

Leaving the Mosque After Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Rulings on leaving the mosque after the adhan, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the exceptions that make it permissible.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after adhan is prohibitively disliked unless for a valid need.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the call to prayer. The text from al-Tahtawi's hashiah clarifies the general prohibition and its exceptions, grounded in a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Find the general hukm (legal ruling) on leaving the mosque after the adhan as stated in the text. Is it haram, makruh, or something else?
The text says 'kariha' which is interpreted as makruh tahrimi.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence
Read the hadith cited: 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' Identify the evidence (dalil) and its strength (thubut and dalala).
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut, but its dalala is qati can still yield a prohibition.
3
Enumerate the exceptions
List the exceptions mentioned: leaving to establish another congregation (as imam or mu'adhdhin), or leaving for a genuine need with intention to return. Also, leaving after having prayed alone is not disliked.
The exceptions are based on the hadith's own exception 'illa li-haja' and the principle of takmil ma'na.
4
Understand the principle of 'takyil ma'na'
The exception for imam/mu'adhdhin is explained as 'completing the meaning' of prayer — the outward act of leaving is contravened by the inner purpose of attaining congregation reward.
This shows that intentions and meanings affect the ruling, a key Hanafi principle.
5
Apply to scenarios
Consider different scenarios: leaving for work, leaving to attend another mosque without need, leaving after praying alone, etc. Determine the ruling for each based on the text.
Reinforces the rule: general prohibition, but not disliked if need or if prayer already performed.

His saying: (like an imam) it is restricted in al-Kabīr and Sharh al-Sayyid and others to an imam whose absence would cause the people to disperse; so it implies that if he is not like that, he should not leave. And it apparently is disliked for the mu'adhdhin to leave if there is someone to replace him in his absence. His saying: (because it is a completion of meaning) i.e., like this prayer due to what is added to it of increased reward that he went out to attain, even if it is a leaving in form, and the consideration is for meanings. His saying: (it is not disliked) i.e., leaving, even if leaving is disliked.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This section from al-Tahtawi's hāshiyah addresses the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan (call to prayer). The base text states that it is 'makrūh' (disliked) to leave a mosque after the adhan, whether the adhan was called in that mosque or another, until one prays. The proof is the hadith: 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' The commentary then clarifies that this is a prohibitively disliked (makrūh taḥrīmī) act, due to the explicit prohibition. Exceptions are made for those who are establishing another congregation, such as an imam or mu'adhdhin going to another mosque, because this serves to complete the benefit of congregation. The commentary also notes that if one prays alone in the mosque and then leaves, it is not disliked, because the command to pray immediately after the adhan has been fulfilled. The text includes a discussion about the timing relative to the adhan: it applies whether one was present at the adhan or entered after it, as long as the adhan has been called. The restriction for the imam is that his absence would cause the congregation to disperse; otherwise, his leaving is still disliked. Similarly, a mu'adhdhin should not leave if there is no replacement. The underlying principle is that the act of leaving to attend another congregation is a completion of the meaning of prayer, i.e., it serves the purpose of increasing reward, even though it involves leaving the mosque. Hence, the ruling is tailored to balance the prohibition against legitimate needs.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karāhah taḥrīmiyyah): An action that is prohibited by an authoritative but not definitive proof; it is sinful to do but does not reach the level of haram.
تكميل معنى (takyīl ma'nā): Completing the purpose or meaning of an act, e.g., praying in congregation for greater reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which of the following circumstances is it NOT disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan?
A) Leaving to go to work.
B) Leaving to join another congregation as an imam.
C) Leaving after having prayed alone.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh tahrimi unless there is a genuine need or the prayer has already been performed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Following the Imam: Bowing and Prostrating Before the Proper Time
Explains rulings for muqtadi who acts before imam in ruku' and sajda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a follower who bows or prostrates before the imam's proper time and explain the difference between the narrated opinion (riwayah) and the well-known (mashhūr) position.

Core Idea
A follower's action before the imam's proper time is invalid per one narration, but the well-known view considers it valid because raising from ruku' is sunnah.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) must perform actions after the imam. But what if he bows or prostrates too early? This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah presents a nuanced ruling: a riwayah from Abu Hanifa deems such early prostration invalid, yet the well-known Hanafi position holds that raising from ruku' is only sunnah, so the follower's act remains valid. Understanding this intra-madhhab distinction is key to applying the rules of following (muṭāba‘ah) correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the initial ruling
Read the opening: 'if he prostrates before his imam: if it is after the imam raises from bowing... it is valid. If it is before the imam raises... it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it does not suffice.' Note that the ruling depends on timing relative to the imam's raising from ruku'.
The key phrase is 'la yujzihi' – it does not suffice.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The commentary clarifies that the narration (riwayah) is not the well-known (mashhūr) position of the school. The mashhūr view considers raising from ruku' as sunnah, so omitting it does not invalidate. Therefore, the follower's early prostration might be valid in the mashhūr view.
This shows how different narrations within the Hanafi school can coexist, with the muftā bihī often being the mashhūr.
3
Apply the ruling to the case of a latecomer (lāḥiq)
The passage then discusses a follower who misses part of the prayer. He must repeat the bowing before following the imam in subsequent actions. Delaying it after the imam finishes is valid but disliked.
The term 'lāḥiq' refers to one who joins late and must complete missed parts after the imam’s taslīm.
4
Understand the role of intention in prolonged sujūd
If the imam prolongs sujūd and the follower raises and prostrates again, intention matters. If he intends the second sajdah with the intention of following, it counts from the first. Giving preponderance to following (muṭāba‘ah) is key.
The ruling prioritises the act of following over a specific intention.
5
Reconcile the riwayah with the mashhūr
The commentator notes that by analogy to the riwayah, a second sajdah before the imam’s raising from ruku' would be invalid, but the mashhūr view (raising is sunnah) does not support that. Thus, the riwayah is a minority view not followed in practice.
This step highlights the critical refinement of weighing narrations within the school.

قوله: (فيلزمه أن يركع بعده (ثانياً) أي قبل المتابعة له فيما هو فيه لأنه لاحق وان أخره إلى ما بعد فراغ الإمام صح وكره كما هو حكم اللاحق، ومثله يقال في مسألة السجود المذكورة بعد قوله : روي عن أبي حنيفة (الخ) وقياس ما تقدم أي في مسألة المصنف أنه الأن ركوع المقتدي اعتبروا لحال أن الإمام لم يفرغ من قراءته، فلم يأت، أوانه في حقه، ولو اعتبرنا هذه الرواية هنا لحكمنا ببطلان صلاته، ثم هذا لا يتأتي على المشهود من مذهب الإمام أن الرفع من الركوع سنة ، فإذا تركه الإمام لا تفسد صلاته، وإن كان قبل أوانه المسنون فمقتضاه أن يقال في المأموم كذلك قوله : (تكون عن (الأولى) ترجيحاً لجانب المتابعة، فقوله بعد ترجيحاً للمتابعة تعليل لهذه أيضاً قوله : (كما لو نواها أي الأولى ومثله لو نوى السجدة التي فيها الإمام. قوله : (فإن أدركه الإمام فيها صحت) وإلا أعادها بعد وإلا فسدت كما تقدم في الركوع . قوله : ( وعلى قياس المروي عن (الإمام أي الذي ذكره قريباً بقوله روي عن الإمام أبي حنيفة لا يجزيه قوله : (قبل رفع الإمام أي من الركوع قوله: (يجب أن لا يجوز) أي السجود الثاني من المؤتم ولو أدرك فيه الإمام لكون المؤتم فعله قبل أوانه.
Because it is his right, so he must bow again after it. If he does not do so and leaves his prayer, it becomes invalid. Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a detailed critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the rulings of a follower (muqtadi) who performs ruku' or sajdah before the imam's proper timing. The author begins by stating that if a follower bows (rukū‘) after the imam's ruku' but does not repeat it, his prayer becomes invalid. If he prostrates before the imam's raising from ruku', it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it does not suffice. The commentary explains that the follower is considered a lāḥiq (one who joins late) and must repeat the bowing before following the imam; delaying it after the imam finishes is valid but disliked. Regarding prolonged sajdah, if the follower raises and then prostrates again while the imam is still prostrating, the intention matters: if he intends the second sajdah with the intention of following, it counts from the first sajdah (giving priority to following); if he intends only the second, it is from the second. If the imam catches up to him in that sajdah, it is valid; otherwise, he must repeat it. The commentator notes that by analogy to the narration from Abu Hanifa, a follower's sajdah before the imam's raising from ruku' is invalid because it is before its time. However, this is reconciled with the well-known Hanafi position that raising from ruku' is only sunnah, so the imam's omission does not invalidate his prayer. The commentator clarifies that the same applies to the follower.

Key Terms
متابعة (muṭāba‘ah): The follower's act of following the imam in prayer actions; the requirement to perform actions after the imam, not simultaneously or before.
لاحق (lāḥiq): A follower who misses one or more rak'ats of the prayer with the imam and joins later, having specific rules for making up missed parts.
أوان (awān): The proper time for a specific action in prayer; performing an action before its awān relative to the imam is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known (mashhūr) Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a follower who prostrates before the imam raises his head from ruku'?
A) The follower's prayer becomes invalid (batil).
B) The follower's prostration does not suffice (la yujzihi).
C) The follower's prostration is valid because raising from ruku' is sunnah.
D) The follower must repeat the prostration after the imam raises.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a narrated opinion that a follower's early prostration is invalid, but the well-known position holds it valid because raising from ruku' is sunnah, and this latter view is generally relied upon.

Leaving the Mosque After Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the exceptions and their conditions.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) except for a genuine need.

You hear the adhan and are in the mosque. May you leave without praying? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling based on the hadith and its exceptions, including for imams and those with valid reasons. We also explore the nuance of avoiding accusation when the congregation is established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving a mosque after the adhan without having prayed. The ruling is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The hadith provides the basis: only a hypocrite or one with a need intending to return leaves.
2
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The hadith: 'لا يخرج من المسجد بعد النداء إلا منافق أو رجل يخرج لحاجة يريد الرجوع'. The prohibition yields karahah tahrimiyyah because the hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
The conjunction 'except' indicates the general prohibition is lifted only for the two categories.
3
Note the exceptions
Exceptions: an imam whose absence would disperse the congregation, a mu'adhdhin of another mosque, and one leaving for a need intending to return. The exception is to complete the meaning of prayer.
If one prays alone and then leaves, it is not disliked (though staying is better).
4
Recognize the additional ruling when the congregation is established
If the iqamah is called for Zuhr or 'Isha and one has not yet left, leaving is disliked because it creates suspicion of opposing the congregation. Instead, one should pray (as a nafl) with the congregation to avoid accusation.
For Fajr, 'Asr, and Maghrib, the ruling differs due to prohibition of nafl at those times.
5
Apply to different prayer times
In Zuhr and 'Isha, one follows the imam as a nafl. In Maghrib, one completes four rak'ats (praying four as nafl) rather than following as three. In Fajr and 'Asr, it is recommended to leave because staying without prayer is worse.
The hadith about not repeating a prayer like it is interpreted to avoid suspicion and waswasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كتاب الصلاة
لأنه قد أجاب داعي الله ،مرة، فلا يجب عليه ثانياً (إلا) أنه يكره خروجه (إذا أقيمت الجماعة قبل خروجه في الظهر و) في (العشاء) لأنه يجوز النقل فيهما مع الإمام يتهم بمخالفة الجماعة كالخوارج، والشيعة وقد قال : من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يقفن مواقف التهم فيقتدي فيهما) أي الظهر والعشاء (متنفلاً) لدفع التهمة عنه، ويكره جلوسه
من غير اقتداء لمخالفة الجماعة بخلاف الصبح والعصر والمغرب لكراهة النفل والمخالفة في المغرب لأنه لا يتنفل مع الإمام فيها في ظاهر الرواية وإتمامها أربعاً أولى من فسادها موافقته، وروي بالسلام معه فيقضي أربعاً كما لو نذر ثلاثاً يلزمه أربع (ولا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها هذا لفظ الحديث قيل معناه لا يصلي ركعتان بقراءة، وركعتان بغير قراءة، وقيل : نهوا عن الإعادة لطلب الأجر وقيل : نهى عن الإعادة بمجرد توهم الفساد لدفع الوسوسة، وقيل: نهى عن تكرار الجماعة في المسجد على الهيئة الأولى، أو عن إعادة الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدى .
الشيعة،
الجماعة لأن من صلى وحده ارتكب الكراهة بحر قوله : (إذا أقيمت فيكره لمن صلى وحده الخروج إلا لمقيم جماعة أخرى فلا يكره له الخروج عندهما كما في صدر الشريعة، والحموي عن البرجندي. قوله : ( يتهم) الذي في الشرح لأنه وإن أجاب الداعي لكن يتهم بمخالفة الجماعة عياناً أو ربما يظن أنه لا يرى جواز الصلاة خلف أهل السنة كما يزعم والخوارج، وهو الأولى، وفي نسخة لئلا يتهم والمعنى عليه وقوله : كالخوارج مثال للمنفي . قوله: (من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر) أي إيماناً كاملاً أي من كان يريد الإيمان الكامل. قوله : ( فلا يقفن الخ) لأنه أبرأ لدينه، وعرضه، وأمنع للناس من الوقوع في المحرمات. قوله: لكراهة النقل) أي بعد الصبح والعصر، وفي النهر ينبغي أن يجب خروجه لأن كراهة مكثه بلا صلاة أشد قوله : ( والمخالفة في (المغرب) أي بإتمام الرابعة ولم يعرج على التنفل بها لأنه باطل على قول الجمهور، والذي يظهر أن ما في الدر عن القهستاني من أن كراهة النفل بالثلاث تنزيهية وما في المضمرات لو أقتدى فيه لا مبنى على رواية بشر المريسي من . الإقتداء في الثلاث متنفلاً قوله: (فيها) أي المغرب من غير إتمام، وقوله في ظاهر الرواية مقابله ما روي عن بشر المريسي . قوله : (وإتمامها أربعاً أولى من موافقته) لأن مخالفته أهون مخالفة السنة لأنها مخالفة بعد الفراغ، ويصير كالمقيم إذا اقتدى بمسافر وكالمسبوق كذا في الشرح قوله: (فيقضي أربعاً) لأنها لزمته باقتدائه في ثلاث ركعات. قوله: (قيل : معناه لا يصلي ركعتان بقراءة وركعتان بغير قراءة) فيكون بياناً لفرض القراءة في ركعات النفل كلها كذا في الشرح قوله : (وقيل نهوا عن الإعادة لطلب الأجر) قد تقدم ما يفيد الطلب في غير وقت مكروه وهو غير المشهور قوله : (بمجرد توهم الفساد بذكر الفساد هنا، والخلل أي النقص غير المفسد في الاحتمال الأخير يرتفع التكرار قوله : ( على الهيئة الأولى) أي بأذان وإقامة أما
من
صحة
And it is disliked for him to leave a mosque in which the adhan was given or another mosque until he prays, due to his statement, peace be upon him: ‘No one leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.’ Except if he is establishing another congregation, like an imam and the mu'adhdhin of another mosque, because it is completion of meaning. And if he leaves after praying alone, it is not disliked. ‘Yujzīhi’ He said: (And it is disliked for him to leave) i.e., prohibitively disliked because of the prohibition in the mentioned hadith. He said: ‘Adhan was given’ means the time entered whether adhan was given or not; there is no difference between whether the adhan was given while he was present or he entered after the adhan, as said by al-Sayyid from al-Nahr: because the latter is not described as leaving the mosque after the call without praying. He said: (Like an imam) – in al-Kabir and Sharh al-Sayyid and others it is restricted to an imam whose absence would cause the people to disperse, indicating that if he is not of that standing, he should not leave. And it appears that if the mu'adhdhin has someone to take his place during his absence, leaving is also disliked for him. He said: (Because it is completion of meaning) i.e., like this prayer due to the additional reward attached to it which he leaves to obtain, even if it is leaving in form, and consideration is given to meanings. He said: (Not disliked) i.e., leaving, although staying is disliked because he has answered the call of Allah once, so he is not obligated a second time. Except that it is disliked for him to leave (if the congregation is established before his departure in Zuhr and in ‘Isha because transfer is permissible in them, and he may be accused of violating the congregation like the Khawarij and Shi’a. And he said: Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of accusation. So he prays in them i.e., Zuhr and ‘Isha as a nafl to ward off accusation from himself. And his sitting without following is disliked due to violating the congregation, unlike Fajr, ‘Asr, and Maghrib because of the dislike of nafl and the violation in Maghrib because he does not pray nafl with the imam in it in the apparent narration, and completing it as four is better than corrupting it by agreeing with him. And it is narrated that he says the salam with him and then prays four, like if he vowed three, four become obligatory. (And do not pray after a prayer like it) – this is the wording of the hadith. It is said its meaning is: do not pray two rak'ats with recitation and two rak'ats without recitation. And it is said: they were forbidden from repetition seeking reward. And it is said: they were forbidden from repetition merely due to suspicion of invalidity to ward off waswasa. And it is said: they were forbidden from repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or from repeating obligatory prayers for fear of defect in what was performed. The Shi’a, the congregation because one who prays alone commits a disliked act. He said: (When it is established, it is disliked for one who prayed alone to leave, except for one establishing another congregation, so leaving is not disliked for him according to the two, as in Sadr al-Shari’ah and al-Hamawi from al-Barjandi. He said: (He is accused) – what is in the Sharh: because even if he answered the caller, he is accused of violating the congregation openly, or perhaps it is thought that he does not consider prayer behind Ahl al-Sunnah permissible, as the Khawarij claim. And this is the better version. In another copy: ‘lest he be accused’ and the meaning follows. His statement: ‘like the Khawarij’ is an example of what is negated. He said: (Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day) i.e., complete faith, i.e., whoever desires complete faith. He said: (Then let him not stand) because it is more exonerating for his religion and honor, and more preventative of people falling into prohibitions. He said: (Due to the dislike of nafl) i.e., after Fajr and ‘Asr. And in al-Nahr: it is necessary for him to leave because the dislike of staying without prayer is stronger. He said: (And the violation in Maghrib) i.e., by completing it as four. And he did not consider praying nafl by it because it is invalid according to the majority. It appears that what is in al-Durr from al-Qahistani that the dislike of nafl by three is tanzihi, and what is in al-Mudmarat about following in it is based on the riwaya of Bishr al-Marisi of following in three as a nafl. He said: (In it) i.e., Maghrib without completion. And his statement ‘in the apparent narration’ is contrasted with what is narrated from Bishr al-Marisi. He said: (And completing it as four is better than agreeing with him) because disagreeing is easier than disagreeing with the Sunnah, since it is a disagreement after completion, and he becomes like a resident who follows a traveller, and like a masbuq. He said: (Then he prays four) because it becomes obligatory by his following in three rak'ats. He said: (It is said: its meaning is do not pray two rak'ats with recitation and two without recitation) thus it is an explanation of the obligation of recitation in all rak'ats of nafl. He said: (And it is said: they were forbidden from repetition seeking reward) – it has already been mentioned that seeking reward at a disliked time is not well-known. He said: (Mere suspicion of invalidity) – mentioning invalidity here, and defect meaning non-invalidating deficiency, in the last possibility the repetition is removed. He said: (In the first manner) i.e., with adhan and iqamah. As for from the soundness.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya discusses the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan. It begins with the matn stating that it is disliked (makruh) to leave a mosque after the adhan until one prays, based on the hadith: 'No one leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' The commentary clarifies that this is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to the prohibition in the hadith. The ruling applies whether the adhan was given in that mosque or another, and regardless of whether one was present when the adhan was given or entered later. Exceptions include an imam whose absence would cause the congregation to disperse, and the mu'adhdhin of another mosque, because leaving to establish another congregation is a completion of the meaning of prayer. If one prays alone and then leaves, it is not disliked. The passage then discusses a related issue: if the congregation is established before one leaves in Zuhr or 'Isha, it is disliked to leave, because one might be accused of opposing the congregation like the Khawarij and Shi'a. To avoid accusation, it is recommended to pray nafl behind the imam in those prayers. It is also disliked to sit without following the congregation. For Fajr, 'Asr, and Maghrib, the ruling is different because nafl is disliked after Fajr and 'Asr, and in Maghrib one cannot pray nafl with the imam in the apparent narration; completing Maghrib as four rak'ats is better than corrupting it by agreeing with the imam. The passage then explains various interpretations of the hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer like it', including that it forbids repetition seeking reward, repetition due to suspicion of invalidity, or repeating the congregation in the same manner. The commentary concludes with details on leaving after the iqamah and other nuances.

Key Terms
مكروه تحريما (makruh tahrimi): A disliked act that is close to haram due to a strong prohibition (based on a zanni proof). Committing it is sinful and avoiding it is rewarded.
مواقف التهم (mawāqif al-tuham): Places or situations where one might be accused of wrongdoing, even if the act itself is permissible. The believer should avoid them to protect his reputation.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who prays a supererogatory (nafl) prayer. In this context, it refers to praying an extra prayer behind the imam to avoid accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who has prayed alone in the mosque and then, before leaving, the iqamah is called for Zuhr prayer?
A) It is not disliked to leave because he has already prayed.
B) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) to leave, except if he is establishing another congregation.
C) It is obligatory to stay and pray with the congregation.
D) It is recommended to leave to avoid suspicion.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying is makruh tahrimi, with exceptions for imams, muadhdhins, and those with a genuine need intending to return.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Joining the Congregation After Praying Alone: Ruling and Reasoning
Explains ruling and hadith interpretation on repeating prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who prays alone and then arrives at a congregation for the same prayer, and explain the role of avoiding accusation (tuhmah) and the hadith 'لا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها'.

Core Idea
It is disliked to leave the mosque; join the congregation as nafl to avoid accusation.

You have prayed Zuhr at home. Then you enter a mosque and find the congregation for Zuhr being established. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer balancing the general principle of not repeating prayers with the need to avoid the appearance of opposing the congregation. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the default ruling
Recognize the case: a person has already prayed the fard alone (e.g., Zuhr). Then the congregation for that same fard is established while he is still in the mosque. The matn states it is not obligatory to repeat, but it is disliked (makruh) for him to leave.
The dislike is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Understand the reason: avoiding accusation (tuhmah)
The reason for the dislike is to avoid the accusation that he is opposing the congregation, like the Khawarij and Shi'a. The hadith 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of accusation' is cited as a proof.
The principle of avoiding tuhmah is a recognized legal basis.
3
Distinguish applicable prayers (Zuhr and Isha) from others
The ruling applies specifically to Zuhr and Isha because nafl prayer is permissible in congregation at these times. For Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib, the dislike of nafl at those times overrides, so the person is not required to join; in fact, it may be better to leave.
In Maghrib, completing as four (if joined) is better than following the imam in three to avoid invalidating the prayer.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference regarding leaving for another congregation
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), if the person intends to establish a separate congregation elsewhere, leaving is not disliked. Abu Hanifa's default view is that leaving is generally disliked.
This difference is noted in the hashya as 'عندهما'.
5
Examine the hadith 'لا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها' and its multiple interpretations
The hadith is used by some to prohibit repeating prayers, but the Hanafi school interprets it in several ways: it may refer to praying two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, or it may prohibit seeking extra reward, or it may caution against repeating due to suspicion of invalidity. The variety of interpretations shows it does not prohibit joining as nafl to avoid accusation.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, so it does not override the need to avoid accusation.

Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from the hashya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the ruling for one who has already performed the obligatory prayer alone and then the congregation for that same prayer is established. The matn states that it is not obligatory for him to go out again, but it is disliked (makruh) for him to leave if the congregation is established before his departure, specifically for Zuhr and Isha. The reason is that he would be accused of opposing the congregation, similar to the Khawarij and Shi'a. To avoid this accusation, he should join the congregation as a nafl prayer. The hashya then elaborates on various points: exceptions for Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib due to dislike of nafl at those times; the Maghrib case where completing four rak'ahs is better than following the imam in three; a narration that he should conclude with salam and then make up four rak'ahs; and the hadith 'لا يصلي بعد صلاة مثلها' with multiple interpretations regarding repeating prayers. The passage also includes intra-Hanafi differences, such as the permission to leave for another congregation according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The relied-upon position is that it is disliked to leave unless for another congregation.

Key Terms
النقل (al-naql): Supererogatory (nafl) prayer performed in congregation, especially in Zuhr and Isha when one has already prayed alone.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Accusation or suspicion of opposing the congregation, which the believer is commanded to avoid by not standing in places of accusation.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) found in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who has prayed Zuhr alone, then enters a mosque where the congregation for Zuhr is being established?
A) He must leave the mosque immediately.
B) It is wajib for him to join the congregation as fard.
C) It is disliked for him to leave; he should join as nafl to avoid accusation.
D) It is haram for him to pray again.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling balances the general prohibition on repeating prayers with the need to avoid accusation, resulting in a nuanced makruh tanzih for leaving the mosque in Zuhr and Isha.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sujud al-Sahw: Definition and Obligation
Definition and ruling of sujud al-sahw with proof and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of sujud al-sahw and explain why it is wajib, including the condition that the missed act must be wajib.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is wajib because it compensates for a wajib act missed due to forgetfulness.

Sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is a key element of Hanafi prayer law, performed to rectify certain omissions. In this passage, the author defines sahw and establishes that sujud al-sahw is wajib (obligatory), not sunnah, based on the principle that it compensates for a missed wajib act. Understanding this ruling helps you distinguish between fard and wajib omissions in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the passage is about sujud al-sahw, defined as two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness.
The text begins 'باب سجود السهو' – chapter on sujud al-sahw.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
Note the explicit statement 'يجب' (it is obligatory). The author asserts this is the correct position (al-sahih) and mentions a weaker opinion that it is sunnah.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the missed act is wajib.
3
Identify the Condition for Obligation
The condition is that the missed act (matruk) must be wajib. The text says 'ضمان فائت وهو لا يكون إلا واجباً' (compensation for something missed, and that is not except wajib).
If the missed act is a rukn (fard), the prayer is invalid and sujud al-sahw does not compensate.
4
Understand the Proof (Compensation)
The reasoning is that sujud al-sahw acts as daman (compensation) for a missed wajib. Since compensation is only required for wajib, the sujud becomes wajib itself.
This is a logical proof (talil) – not a direct textual dalil.
5
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
The text reports that some said it is sunnah, but the author chooses the wajib view as correct. This is a known ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that it is wajib.

Source Text

لأنها ركن حتى لو سلم من غير إعادتها، أو لم يسلم صحت مع النقصان، وأما السجدة الصلبية، والتلاوية فكل يرفع القعود فيفترض إعادته، صلاته مجرد تكرارهما بغير أذان، أو بهما في المسجد الجامع، أو مسجد الحي المضاف إليه سبباً للمضاف إلا إذا دل الدليل على خلافه كصدقة الفطر، وحجة الإسلام، فإنها فيهما من الإضافة إلى الشرط، فالإضافة في الأول لشرط الوجوب، وفي الثاني لشرط الصحة وشرطه صحة ووجوباً أن يكون المتروك واجباً، وتأدية السجود بشرائط الصلاة وأن لا يسلم متذكراً ركناً، وأن لا يطرأ عليه ما يمنع البناء، ومنه طرو الوقت الناقص، وليس من شرطه أن يسلم قاصداً له .اهـ. قوله: (وهو لا يكون إلا واجباً) لأن الفائت موصوف بالوجوب . قوله: (أنه يرفع الواجب الخ) أي فيعادان بعد فعله أي، ولولا أنه واجب لما رفعهما قوله لأنها ركن) أي فهي أقوى منه ، والشيء لا يرفع ما هو أقوى منه . قوله : (صحت صلاته النقصان) لأن الواجب إعادة السلام والتشهد، وقد تركهما، قوله: (فكل يرفع القعود أما السجدة الصلبية فهي أقوى من القعدة لكونها ركناً، والقعدة لختم الأركان، فلا تعتبر إلا بعد تمام الأركان وبدون السجدة الصلبية لا تتم، وأما سجدة التلاوة فلأنها أثر القراءة، فيعطي لها حكمها ، وقيل : إن سجدة التلاوة لا ترفع القعدة لأنها واجبة، فلا ترفع الفرض، واختاره شمس الأئمة، والأول أصح، وهو المختار، وهو أصح الروايتين، واختلف الترجيح في ارتفاض القعدة بقراءة التشهد بعدما كان تركه ساهياً، وقعد قدر التشهد
Book of Prayer: Chapter on Sujud al-Sahw. From the addition of the ruling to the cause, and sahw is heedlessness. (It is obligatory) because it is compensation for something missed, and that is not except wajib, and this is the correct position; and it was said: it is sunnah. The face of the correct position is that it raises the wajib from reciting the tashahhud and the salam, and it does not raise the sitting (qa'dah) because it is a rukn, such that if he performed salam without repeating it, or did not perform salam, his prayer is valid despite the deficiency. As for the prostrations of the prayer (sajdah sulbiyyah) and of recitation (tilawah), each raises the sitting, so repeating it is obligatory... etc.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw from the Hashiya. The author defines 'sahw' as heedlessness and states the obligation of sujud al-sahw, explaining that it is compensation (daman) for a missed wajib act. He presents the correct view (al-sahih) that it is wajib, and mentions a weak opinion that it is sunnah. The reasoning is that sujud al-sahw raises the missed wajib (tashahhud and salam) but does not raise the sitting (qa'dah) because the sitting is a rukn (pillar) and thus stronger. The passage then discusses the conditions for sujud al-sahw, such as the missed act being wajib, performing the sujud with the conditions of prayer, not intentionally remembering a rukn, and no occurrence of anything preventing continuation. It also clarifies that forgetfulness (nisyan) and doubt (shakk) are treated the same in legal ruling. The discussion about raising the sitting includes a disagreement: some say sujud al-tilawah does not raise the sitting because it is only wajib, while the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that it does raise it. The passage ends with a differing opinion on whether reciting tashahhud after forgetfully leaving it raises the sitting.

Key Terms
السهو (al-sahw): Heedlessness or forgetfulness during prayer, specifically regarding acts of prayer.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness, the absence of something from the mind after it was present.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for mandatory (wajib) acts omitted or delayed due to forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of sujud al-sahw?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib because it compensates for a missed wajib act; it does not compensate for missed fard (rukns).
